قوله (والكلب والخنزير وسباع البهائم (نجس) أي سؤر هذه الأشياء نجس. والمراد بسباع البهائم نحو الأسد والفهد والنمر . قال الزيلعي رحمه الله : قوله «والكلب إلى آخره» بالرفع أجود على أنه حذف المضاف وأقيم المضاف إليه مقامه وذلك جائز بالاتفاق إذا كان الكلام مشعراً بحذفه وقد وجد هنا ما يشعر بحذفه وهو تقدم ذكر السؤر، ولو جر على أنه معطوف على ما قبله من المجرور لا يجوز عند سيبويه لأنه يلزم منه العطف على عاملين وهو ممتنع عند البصريين ويجوز عند الفراء ولو قيل إنه مجرور على أنه حذف المضاف وترك المضاف إليه على إعرابه كان جائزاً إلا أنه قليل نحو قولهم ما كل سوداء تمرة ولا كل بيضاء شحمة». ويشترط أن يتقدم في اللفظ ذكر المضاف أهـ. وقد أطال رحمه الله الكلام مع عدم التحرير لأن قوله «لأنه يلزم منه العطف على عاملين مجاز وإنما يلزم منه العطف على معمولي عاملين لأن الكلب معطوف على الآدمي وهو معمول للمضاف أعني سؤر، ونجس معطوف على طاهر وهو معمول المبتدأ أعني سؤر ، فكان فيه العطف على معمولين وهما الآدمي وطاهر لعاملين وهما المضاف والمبتدأ . هذا إذا كان المضاف عاملاً في المضاف إليه، أما إذا كان العامل هو الإضافة فلا إشكال أنه من باب العطف على معمولي عاملين مختلفين . قال في المغني: وقولهم على عاملين فيه تجوز قال الشمني : يعني بحذف المضاف. قال الرضي: معنى قولهم العطف على عاملين أن تعطف بحرف واحد معمولين مختلفين كانا في الإعراب كالمنصوب والمرفوع أو متفقين كالمنصوبين على معمولي عاملين مختلفين نحو «إن زيداً ضرب عمراً وبكراً خالداً فهو عطف متفقي الاعراب على معمولي عاملين مختلفين. وقولك «إن زيداً ضرب غلامه وبكراً أخوه عطف مختلفي الإعراب ولا يعطف المعمولان على عاملين بل على معموليهما فهذا القول منهم على حذف المضاف أهـ. وفي المغني: الحق جوازاً العطف على معمولي عاملين في نحو في الدار زيد والحجرة عمرو أهـ. أما سؤر الكلب فهو طاهر عند مالك ومن تبعه ولكن يغسل الإناء منه سبعاً تعبداً. وقال الشافعي: إنه نجس ويغسل الإناء سبعاً إحداهن بالتراب . لما رواه أبو هريرة رضي الله عنه عنه الا أنه قال «يغسل الإناء إذا ولغ فيه الكلب سبع مرات أولاهن أو أخراهن بالتراب» رواه الأئمة الستة في كتبهم. وفي لفظ لمسلم وأبي داود طهور إناء أحدكم إذا ولغ فيه الكلب أن يغسل سبع مرات» ورواه أيضاً مسلم من حديث أبي هريرة إذا ولغ الكلب في إناء أحدكم فليرقه ثم ليغسله سبع مرات. وروى مالك في الموطأ عن أبي الزناد عن الأعرج عن أبي هريرة أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال «إذا شرب الكلب في إناء أحدكم فليغسله سبع مرات قال ابن عبد البر : إن حديث أبي هريرة تواترت طرقه وكثرت عنه . والأمر بالإراقة دليل التنجيس وكذا الطهور لأنه مصدر بمعنى الطهارة فيستدعي سابقية الحدث أو الخبث ولا حدث في الإناء فتعين الثاني، ولأنه متى دار الحكم بين كونه تعبدياً ومعقول المعنى كأن جعله معقول المعنى هو الوجه لندرة التعبد وكثرة التعقل . ولنا قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «يغسل الإناء من ولوغ الكلب ثلاثاً روي عن أبي هريرة فعلاً وقولاً مرفوعاً وموقوفاً من طريقين: الأول أخرجه الدارقطني بإسناد صحيح عن عطاء عن أبي هريرة إذا ولغ الكلب في الإناء فاهرقه ثم اغسله ثلاث مرات وأخرجه بهذا الاسناد عن أبي هريرة أنه قال إذا ولغ الكلب في الإناء أهرقه وغسل ثلاث مرات قال الشيخ تقي الدين في الإلمام : هذا إسناد صحيح الطريق الثاني أخرجه ابن عدي في الكامل عن الحسين بن علي الكرابيسي بسنده إلى عطاء عن أبي هريرة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا ولغ الكلب في إناء أحدكم فليهرقه وليغسله ثلاث مرات ولم يرفعه غير الكرابيسي. قال ابن عدي قال لنا أحمد الحسين الكرابيسي يسأل عنه وله كتب مصنفة ذكر فيها اختلاف الناس من المسائل وذكر فيها أخباراً كثيرة وكان حافظاً لها ولم أجد له منكراً غير هذا الحديث والذي حمل أحمد بن حنبل عليه إنما هو من أجل اللفظ بالقرآن فأما في الحديث فلم أر به بأساً أهـ. ومن المعلوم الحكم بالضعف والصحة إنما هو في الظاهر، أما في نفس الأمر فيجوز صحة ما حكم بضعفه ظاهراً وثبوت كون مذهب أبي هريرة ذلك كما تقدم بالسند الصحيح قرينة تفيد أن هذا الحديث مما أجاده الراوي المضعف، وحينئذ يعارض حديث السبع ويقدم عليه لأن مع السبع دلالة التقدم للعلم بما كان من التشديد في أمر الكلاب أوّل الأمر حتى أمر بقتلها والتشديد في سؤرها يناسب كونه إذ ذاك وقد ثبت نسخ ذلك، فإذا عارض قرينه معارض كانت التقدمة له ولو طرحنا الحديث بالكلية كان في عمل أبي هريرة على خلاف حديث السبع وهو رواية كفاية لاستحالة أن يترك القطعي بالرأي. منه، وهذا لأن ظنية خبر الواحد إنما هو بالنسبة إلى غير راوية فأما بالنسبة إلى رواية الذي سمعه من في النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقطعي مبني . التقرير السابق إشكالاً لأنه . سؤر واحد في الحقيقة لكن عمله في المضاف إليه وفي الخبر مختلف فكان كعاملين، وكذا لا إشكال على تنزيل اختلاف العمل منزلة اختلاف العامل لأن العامل وهو
His statement (And the dog, the pig, and the beasts of prey are impure) i.e., the leftover water of these things is impure. What is meant by beasts of prey are like the lion, leopard, and tiger. Al-Zayla'i said: His statement 'and the dog to the end' in the nominative is better, on the basis that the construct was omitted and the construct to it was put in its place, and that is permissible by agreement if the speech indicates its omission, and it is found here that indicates its omission, which is the prior mention of the leftover water. If it were in the genitive as coordinated with what precedes from the genitive, it is not permissible according to Sibawayh because it would entail coordinating two agents, and that is impermissible according to the Basrans, but it is permissible according to al-Farra'. And if it were said that it is in the genitive on the basis that the construct was omitted and the construct to it was left in its inflection, it would be permissible except that it is rare, like their saying 'Not every black thing is a date, nor every white thing is fat' (i.e., not all black objects are dates, nor all white objects are fat). And it is required that the mention of the construct precedes in the wording. End. He has spoken at length without precision, because his statement 'because it entails coordinating two agents' is metaphorical; rather it entails coordinating the objects of two agents. For the dog is coordinated with the human, which is an object of the construct (i.e., leftover water), and 'impure' is coordinated with 'pure', which is an object of the subject (i.e., leftover water). Thus there is coordination of two objects (the human and pure) for two agents (the construct and the subject). This is if the construct acts upon the construct to it. But if the operator is the idafa (construct state), then there is no problem that it is of the type of coordinating the objects of two different agents. Al-Mughni said: Their saying 'two agents' involves a metaphor. Al-Shumunni said: meaning by omission of the construct. Al-Radi said: The meaning of their saying 'coordinating two agents' is that you coordinate with one particle two different objects, whether they agree in inflection (like accusative and nominative) or differ (like two accusatives) for two different agents, e.g., 'Indeed Zayd struck Amr and Bakr Khalid' is coordinating two objects of the same inflection for two different agents. And your saying 'Indeed Zayd struck his slave and Bakr his brother' is coordinating objects of different inflections. And the two objects are not coordinated on two agents but rather on their objects. So this statement of theirs is based on omission of the construct. End. In al-Mughni: The truth is the permissibility of coordinating the objects of two agents in such as 'In the house is Zayd and in the room is Amr'. End. As for the leftover water of the dog, it is pure according to Malik and those who follow him, but the vessel is washed seven times out of devotion. Al-Shafi'i said: It is impure and the vessel is washed seven times, one of which with earth, because of what Abu Hurayra narrated from him, except that he said: 'The vessel is washed when a dog drinks from it seven times, the first or last of which with earth', narrated by the six imams in their books. In a wording of Muslim and Abu Dawud: 'The purification of the vessel of any one of you when a dog drinks from it is that it be washed seven times.' Muslim also narrated from Abu Hurayra: 'When a dog drinks from the vessel of any one of you, let him pour it out, then wash it seven times.' Malik narrated in al-Muwatta' from Abu al-Zinad from al-A'raj from Abu Hurayra that the Messenger of Allah said: 'When a dog drinks from the vessel of any one of you, let him wash it seven times.' Ibn Abd al-Barr said: The hadith of Abu Hurayra has mutawatir chains and many recensions. The command to pour out is evidence of impurity, and likewise the word 'tahoor' because it is a verbal noun meaning purification, so it requires prior existence of ritual impurity or filth, and there is no ritual impurity in the vessel, so the second (filth) is determined. And because whenever a ruling revolves between being devotional and being rationally understandable, making it rationally understandable is the correct face due to the rarity of devotional acts and the abundance of reasoning. Our proof is his statement: 'The vessel is washed from the lapping of a dog three times' reported from Abu Hurayra in both action and statement, marfu' and mawquf, through two chains: The first: al-Daraqutni narrated with a sound chain from Ata' from Abu Hurayra: 'When a dog drinks from a vessel, pour it out and wash it three times.' And he narrated through this chain from Abu Hurayra that he said: 'When a dog drinks from a vessel, pour it out and wash it three times.' Shaykh Taqi al-Din said in al-Ilmam: This chain is sound. The second chain: Ibn Adi narrated in al-Kamil from al-Husayn ibn Ali al-Karabisi through his chain to Ata' from Abu Hurayra who said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'When a dog drinks from the vessel of any one of you, let him pour it out and wash it three times.' No one raised it (to the Prophet) except al-Karabisi. Ibn Adi said: Ahmad said: al-Husayn al-Karabisi is asked about, he has compiled books mentioning differences of people on issues and many hadiths, he was a memorizer, and I have not found any unacceptable thing from him except this hadith. What made Ahmad ibn Hanbal criticize him was only because of the recitation of the Quran, but as for hadith, I see no harm in him. End. It is known that judgment of weakness or authenticity is only apparent; but in reality, it is possible that what is judged weak is actually authentic. And the proven position of Abu Hurayra as above with a sound chain is a context that indicates that this hadith is among what the weakened narrator perfected. Then it contradicts the hadith of seven, and it (the three-time hadith) is given precedence because with the hadith of seven there is an indication of earlier time, because the severity in the matter of dogs was at first, until killing them was ordered, and severity in their leftover water suits that time; and it has been proven that this was abrogated. So when a context contradicts, precedence is given to it. Even if we completely discard the hadith (of three), the action of Abu Hurayra contrary to the hadith of seven is sufficient evidence, because it is impossible that he would leave certain knowledge for opinion. And this is because the probability of a lone narrator hadith is only relative to someone other than the narrator; but for the narrator who heard it from the Prophet it is certain, built on that. The earlier explanation has a problem because ... leftover water is actually one thing, but its operation in the construct to it and in the predicate is different, so it is like two agents. Likewise there is no problem on the basis of considering difference of operation as difference of agent, because the agent is
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addressing the ruling on the leftover water (su'ur) of dogs, pigs, and beasts of prey. The author first states the ruling: these are impure, meaning their su'ur is impure. He then defines 'beasts of prey' as lion, leopard, tiger, etc. A lengthy grammatical discussion follows, analyzing how the matn should be read: whether 'al-kalb' should be nominative or genitive. The author cites al-Zayla'i and others on the permissibility of omitting the construct (the word 'su'ur') and leaving the construct to it in its place, a rare but recognized usage. He goes into the issue of 'coordinating two agents' versus 'coordinating objects of two agents', concluding that the correct interpretation avoids this problem. After resolving the grammar, he turns to the fiqh dispute. He notes that Imam Malik considers the dog's su'ur pure, but requires washing the vessel seven times out of devotion. Imam al-Shafi'i considers it impure, requiring seven washes, one with earth. The Shafi'i proof includes the famous hadith of seven washes. The Hanafi rebuttal, presented here, relies on another hadith narrated by Abu Hurayra that the vessel is washed three times. The discussion includes verification of the chain: al-Daraqutni's chain is sound, and al-Karabisi's marfu' version, though criticized, was defended by Ibn Adi. The Hanafi position argues that the severe ruling of seven washes was early and later abrogated by the three-wash hadith. Even if the three-wash hadith is weak, the practice of Abu Hurayra (acting on three) is decisive for him. The passage ends by returning to the grammatical point, emphasizing that the difference in grammatical operation does not invalidate the coordination. Overall, this passage demonstrates the Hanafi methodology: careful textual reading, use of hadith, and rational preference for coherence with later practice.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'ur): The leftover water or liquid remaining in a vessel after an animal drinks from it.
سباع البهائم (siba' al-baha'im): Beasts of prey among land animals that hunt with fangs, such as lions, leopards, tigers, wolves, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, how many times should a vessel be washed if a dog drinks from it?
A) Seven times, one with earth
B) Three times
C) Once by pouring out the water
D) Seven times without earth

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules the su'ur of a dog as impure and requires three washes of the vessel, based on a hadith of Abu Hurayra that is considered to abrogate the earlier seven-wash command.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
The Hanafi Three-Wash Ruling for a Vessel Lapped by a Dog
Dispute between Hanafi and majority on number of washes after dog lapping

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing a vessel after a dog laps and explain the Hanafi proof from the hadith of Abu Hurairah.

Core Idea
Three washes without earth – the Hanafi school holds that the vessel must be washed three times after a dog laps, and earth is not required.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents the core Hanafi position in a dispute with the Shafi'i and Maliki schools. The disagreement hinges on which hadith is considered operative: the well-known hadith of seven washes with earth, or the hadith of Abu Hurairah commanding three washes. The Hanafi school adopts the latter, viewing it as abrogating the earlier ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
What is the act under discussion? Washing a vessel after a dog laps from it. The dispute is about the number of washes required and whether earth is used.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi position: three washes without earth. Their proof is the hadith narrated by Abu Hurairah: 'Wash the vessel from the lapping of a dog three times.'
The hadith is presented as marfu' (from the Prophet) and mawquf (from Abu Hurairah himself).
3
Analyze the chain of the Hanafi hadith
The passage gives two paths: one via al-Daraqutni with a sound chain from Ata' from Abu Hurairah, and another via al-Karabisi. The author argues that even if the second path is weak, the first is sound and Abu Hurairah's own practice confirms it.
The Hanafis place weight on the practice of the Companion as a sunnah.
4
Understand the abrogation argument
The Hanafis argue that the seven-wash hadith was abrogated because early severity against dogs was later relaxed. Abu Hurairah's practice of three washes proves he knew of the abrogation.
The passage uses Fath al-Qadir's reasoning to defend this.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The relied-upon ruling in the Hanafi school is three washes without earth. Some earlier Hanafis held no fixed number, but the majority and the texts of al-Hidayah and others adopt three.
This is the position given in fatwa today.

السابق إشكالاً لأنه . سؤر واحد في الحقيقة لكن عمله في المضاف إليه وفي الخبر مختلف فكان كعاملين، وكذا لا إشكال على تنزيل اختلاف العمل منزلة اختلاف العامل لأن العامل وهو حتى ينسخ به الكتاب إذا كان قطعي الدلالة في معناه فلزم أنه لا يتركه إلا لقطعه بالناسخ إذ القطعي لا يترك إلا لقطعي فبطل تجويز هم تركه بناء على ثبوت ناسخ في اجتهاده المحتمل للخطاً. وإذا علمت ذلك كان تركه بمنزلة روايته للناسخ بلا شبهة فيكون الآخر منسوخاً بالضرورة. كذا في فتح القدير. وقال الطحاوي: ولو وجب العمل برواية السبع ولا يجعل منسوخاً لكان ما روى عبد الله بن المغفل في ذلك عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أولى مما روى أبو هريرة لأنه زاد عليه وعفروا الثامنة بالتراب والزائد أولى من الناقص فكان ينبغي للمخالف أن يعمل بهذه الزيادة، فإن تركها لزمه ما لزم خصمه في ترك السبع، ومالك لم يأخذ بالتعفير الثابت في الصحيح مطلقاً فثبت أنه منسوخ أهـ. وحديث عبد الله بن المغفل مجمع على صحته ورواه مسلم وأبو داود فكان الأخذ بروايته أحوط، وقد روى عن أبي هريرة «إذا ولغ السنور في الإناء يغسل سبع مرات ولم يعملوا به وكل جواب لهم عن ذلك فهو جوابنا عما زاد على الثلاث، أو يحمل ما زاد على الثلاث على الاستحباب ويؤيده ما روى الدارقطني عن أبي هريرة عنه لا في الكلب يلغ في الإناء أنه يغسل ثلاثاً أو خمساً أو سبعاً، فخيره ولو كان التسبيع واجباً لما خيره . ثم اعلم أن الطحاوي والوبري نقلا أن أصحابنا لم يجدوا لغسل الإناء منه حداً بل العبرة لأكبر الرأي ولو بمرة كما هو الحكم في غسل غيره من النجاسات . ذكره الطحاوي في كتاب اختلاف العلماء وهو مخالف لما في الهداية وغيرها أنه يغسل الإناء من ولوغه ثلاثاً وهو ظاهر الحديث الذي استدلوا به وسيأتي بيان أن الثلاث هل هي شرط في إزالة الأنجاس أو لا إن شاء الله تعالى. وفي النهاية : الولوغ حقيقة شرب الكلب المائعات باطراف لسانه . وفي شرح المهذب : إن الماضي والمضارع بفتح العين تقول وَلَغَ يَلَغُ. وقد قدمنا أن سؤر الكلب نجس عند أصحابنا جميعاً، أما على القول بنجاسة عينه فظاهر، وأما على القول المصحح بطهارة عينه فلأن لحمه نجس ولعابه متولد من لحمه ولا يلزم من طهارة عينه طهارة سؤره لنجاسة لحمه ولا يلزم من نجاسة سؤره نجاسة عينه وإنما يلزم من نجاسة سؤرة نجاسة لحمه المتولد منه اللعاب كما صرح به في التنجيس وفتح القدير وغيرهما، وسيأتي أيضاحه في الكلام على سؤر السباع والمذكور في كتب الشافعية كالمهذب أنه لا فرق بين الولوغ ووضع بعض عضوه في الإناء، ولم أر هذا في كتبنا والذي يقتضيه كلامهم على القول بنجاسة عينه تنجس الماء وعلى القول بطهارة عينه عدم تنجسه أخذاً من قولهم إذا ولغ الكلب في البئر كما قدمناه لأن ماء البئر في حكم الماء القليل كماء الآنية كما قدمناه. ولا فرق بين ولوغ كلب أو كلبين في الاكتفاء بالثلاث لأن الثاني لو يوجب تنجساً كما لا يخفى . وإذا ولغ الكلب في طعام فالذي يقتضيه كلامهم أنه إن كان جامداً قدر ما حوله وأكل الباقي، وإن كان مائعاً انتفع به في غير الأبدان كما قدمناه
A dog lapped in it seven times, first or last with earth – narrated by the six imams in their books. In a wording of Muslim and Abu Dawud: 'The purification of one of your vessels when a dog laps in it is to wash it seven times.' Also narrated by Muslim from Abu Hurairah: 'When a dog laps in the vessel of one of you, let him pour it out then wash it seven times.' Malik narrated in al-Muwatta from Abu al-Zinad from al-Araj from Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When a dog drinks from the vessel of one of you, let him wash it seven times.' Ibn Abd al-Barr said: The hadith of Abu Hurairah is mutawatir in its chains and numerous. The command to pour out is evidence of impurity, likewise 'tahur' because it is a masdar meaning purity, necessitating a prior hadath or khabath, and there is no hadath in the vessel, so the second is determined. And because when a ruling alternates between being devotional and rational, making it rational is the preferred aspect due to the rarity of devotional acts and frequency of rational ones. Our proof is his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Wash the vessel from the lapping of a dog three times,' narrated from Abu Hurairah both as a deed and a saying, marfu' and mawquf, from two paths: The first: al-Daraqutni narrated with a sound chain from Ata' from Abu Hurairah: 'When a dog laps in the vessel, pour it out then wash it three times.' And with this chain from Abu Hurairah that he said: 'When a dog laps in the vessel, pour it out and wash it three times.' Shaykh Taqi al-Din said in al-Ilmam: This is a sound chain. The second path: Ibn Adi narrated in al-Kamil from al-Husayn ibn Ali al-Karabisi with his chain to Ata' from Abu Hurairah who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When a dog laps in the vessel of one of you, let him pour it out and wash it three times.' No one raised it except al-Karabisi. Ibn Adi said: Ahmad al-Husayn al-Karabisi is asked about him, and he has composed books mentioning the differences of people on issues and many reports, and he was a preserver of them, and I did not find any objection to him except this hadith. What caused Ahmad ibn Hanbal to object was due to the wording of the Quran; as for hadith, I see no harm in it. It is known that the judgment of weakness and authenticity is only in appearance; in reality, it is possible that what is judged weak in appearance is authentic, and the fact that the school of Abu Hurairah is as stated with the sound chain is evidence that this hadith is something the weak narrator excelled in. Then it opposes the hadith of seven and takes precedence over it, because with seven there is an indication of abrogation due to the knowledge of the severity concerning dogs initially until killing them was commanded, and severity in their residual water was appropriate at that time, and its abrogation has been established. So when a counter indication opposes, precedence is given to it. Even if we discard the hadith entirely, the practice of Abu Hurairah contrary to the hadith of seven and his narration are sufficient, because it is impossible that he would leave the definitive with his own opinion. This is because the zanniyyah of a solitary report is relative to other than its narrator; as for the narrator who heard it from the Prophet (peace be upon him), it is definitive for him. The previous report has a problem because it is one residual water in reality, but its action on the annex and on the report differs, so it is like two factors. Likewise, there is no problem in treating the difference of action as the difference of factor because the factor is such that it abrogates the Book if it is definitive in meaning, so it follows that he does not leave it except by being certain of the abrogator, since the definitive is not left except by the definitive. Thus their supposition that he left it based on the existence of an abrogator in his ijtihad which is liable to error is invalid. And when you know that, his leaving it is like his narration of the abrogator without doubt, so the other is abrogated necessarily. This is from Fath al-Qadir. Al-Tahawi said: If action on the narration of seven were obligatory and it is not considered abrogated, then what Abdullah ibn al-Mughaffal narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) would be more deserving than what Abu Hurairah narrated, because he added 'and smear the eighth with earth', and the extra is more deserving than the less. So the opponent should act on this addition. If he leaves it, what befell his opponent in leaving the seven befalls him. And Malik did not take the smearing with earth that is established in the Sahih at all, so it is established that it is abrogated. And the hadith of Abdullah ibn al-Mughaffal is agreed upon as authentic, narrated by Muslim and Abu Dawud, so taking his narration is more precautionary. And it is narrated from Abu Hurairah: 'When a cat laps in the vessel, wash it seven times' and they did not act on it. Whatever answer they have for that is our answer for what exceeds three. Or what exceeds three is carried on istihbab. Supporting this is what al-Daraqutni narrated from Abu Hurairah about the dog lapping in the vessel: 'Wash it three, or five, or seven times' – he left it to choice. If tashih were obligatory, he would not have left it to choice. Then know that al-Tahawi and al-Wabiri narrated that our companions did not find a fixed limit for washing the vessel from it; rather the criterion is the strongest opinion, even if once, as is the ruling in washing other impurities. Al-Tahawi mentioned this in Kitab Ikhtilaf al-Ulama, and it contradicts what is in al-Hidayah and others that the vessel from its lapping is washed three times, which is the apparent meaning of the hadith they used as evidence. The explanation of whether three are a condition for removing impurities will come later, God willing. In al-Nihaya: al-wulugh literally is the dog drinking liquids with the tip of its tongue. In Sharh al-Muhadhdhab: the past and present tense are with fatha on the 'ayn; you say walagha yalaghu. We have already stated that the residual water of a dog is impure according to all our companions. For those who hold that its essence is impure, it is obvious. For those who hold the corrected view of its essence being pure, it is because its meat is impure and its saliva is generated from its meat, and the purity of its essence does not necessitate the purity of its residual water due to the impurity of its meat, and the impurity of its residual water does not necessitate the impurity of its essence; rather, the impurity of its residual water necessitates the impurity of its meat from which the saliva is generated, as stated in al-Tanjis, Fath al-Qadir, and others. Its clarification will come in the discussion on the residual water of predators. It is mentioned in the books of the Shafi'is like al-Muhadhdhab that there is no difference between lapping and placing some of its limb in the vessel. I have not seen this in our books. What their speech requires on the view of the impurity of its essence is that water becomes impure; on the view of the purity of its essence, it does not become impure, taken from their statement when a dog laps in a well as we have presented, because well water is in the ruling of little water like vessel water as we have presented. There is no difference between the lapping of one dog or two dogs in sufficing with three, because the second does not cause any impurity, as is obvious. And when a dog laps in food, what their speech requires is that if it is solid, remove the part around it and eat the rest; if it is liquid, benefit from it in other than the body as we have presented.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the ruling on washing a vessel after a dog laps from it. The author begins by presenting the well-known hadith of seven washes with earth, narrated by the 'six imams' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i, Ibn Majah) and others. This is the position of the majority of scholars, including the Shafi'i and Maliki schools. The author then presents the Hanafi proof: the hadith narrated from Abu Hurairah commanding three washes only, supported by both marfu' and mawquf chains. The Hanafis argue that the seven-wash ruling was abrogated, as early severity against dogs was later lifted. They also point out that Abdullah ibn al-Mughaffal's hadith adds an eighth wash with earth, which the Hanafis interpret as further evidence of abrogation since Imam Malik did not adopt it. The Hanafi response to the Shafi'i argument that the seven-wash hadith is stronger is that Abu Hurairah's own practice (three washes) contradicts the seven-wash hadith he narrated, proving abrogation. The passage also discusses the definition of wulugh, the impurity of the dog's residual water, and rules for food. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position is that the vessel must be washed three times; earth is not required. Some Hanafis, like al-Tahawi, reported that there is no fixed number, but the majority view in the school is three washes.

Key Terms
ولوغ (wulugh): The dog drinking liquids by the tips of its tongue
سؤر (su'r): The residual water left after a dog drinks

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, how many times must a vessel be washed after a dog laps from it?
A) Seven times, with earth
B) Three times, with earth
C) Three times, without earth
D) One time, with strong opinion

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires three washes without earth for a vessel after a dog laps, based on the hadith of Abu Hurairah and the abrogation of earlier severity.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
The Abrogation Argument and Intra-Hanafi Variant on Dog Lapping
Expansion of the Hanafi abrogation argument and intra-madhhab differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi abrogation argument and identify the intra-Hanafi difference regarding the number of washes.

Core Idea
The seven-wash ruling was abrogated; Abu Hurairah's practice proves the abrogation. Some Hanafis said no fixed number, but the dominant view is three.

This passage delves into the reasoning behind the Hanafi position, particularly the argument that the seven-wash hadith was abrogated. It also presents a variant within the Hanafi school reported by al-Tahawi that some companions saw no fixed limit. Understanding this helps appreciate the school's methodology in handling conflicting hadiths.

Guided Path
1
Review the abrogation argument
The seven-wash hadith came from a time of severity against dogs; later, that severity was lifted. The Hanafis argue that the three-wash hadith is later and abrogates the seven.
2
Analyze the role of Abu Hurairah's practice
Abu Hurairah narrated both hadiths but practiced three washes. For a Companion to contradict his own narration would be irrational unless he knew of abrogation.
The passage uses the principle that a solitary report is definitive for its narrator.
3
Consider the Abdullah ibn al-Mughaffal hadith
This hadith commands eight washes (seven plus one with earth). Malik did not adopt it, which the Hanafis use to support that the ruling was abrogated.
If the seven-wash ruling were not abrogated, then this hadith, being extra, should be followed.
4
Examine the cat lapping analogy
A hadith from Abu Hurairah requires seven washes for a cat, but the majority did not act on it, showing inconsistency. The Hanafis use this as a parallel argument.
This strengthens the claim that the seven-wash ruling for dogs was also not acted upon.
5
Identify the intra-Hanafi variant
Al-Tahawi and al-Wabiri reported that some early Hanafis (like Ibrahim al-Nakha'i) did not fix a number; the vessel could be washed once or more until clean. But the relied-upon position in the school is three washes.
This shows the development of the school and that the mufta bihi is three.

أهـ. وحديث عبد الله بن المغفل مجمع على صحته ورواه مسلم وأبو داود فكان الأخذ بروايته أحوط، وقد روى عن أبي هريرة «إذا ولغ السنور في الإناء يغسل سبع مرات ولم يعملوا به وكل جواب لهم عن ذلك فهو جوابنا عما لسانه . وفي شرح المهذب : إن الماضي والمضارع بفتح العين تقول وَلَغَ يَلَغُ. وقد قدمنا أن سؤر الكلب نجس عند أصحابنا جميعاً، أما على القول بنجاسة عينه فظاهر، وأما على القول المصحح بطهارة عينه فلأن لحمه وغيرهما، وسيأتي أيضاحه في الكلام على سؤر السباع والمذكور في كتب الشافعية كالمهذب أنه لا فرق بين الولوغ ووضع بعض عضوه في الإناء، ولم أر هذا في كتبنا والذي يقتضيه كلامهم على القول بنجاسة عينه تنجس الماء وعلى القول بطهارة عينه عدم تنجسه أخذاً من قولهم إذا ولغ الكلب في البئر كما قدمناه لأن ماء البئر في حكم الماء القليل كماء الآنية كما قدمناه. ولا فرق بين ولوغ كلب أو كلبين في الاكتفاء بالثلاث لأن الثاني لو يوجب تنجساً كما لا يخفى . وإذا ولغ الكلب في طعام فالذي يقتضيه كلامهم أنه إن كان جامداً قدر ما حوله وأكل الباقي، وإن كان مائعاً انتفع به في غير الأبدان كما قدمناه
A dog lapped in it seven times, first or last with earth – narrated by the six imams in their books. In a wording of Muslim and Abu Dawud: 'The purification of one of your vessels when a dog laps in it is to wash it seven times.' Also narrated by Muslim from Abu Hurairah: 'When a dog laps in the vessel of one of you, let him pour it out then wash it seven times.' Malik narrated in al-Muwatta from Abu al-Zinad from al-Araj from Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When a dog drinks from the vessel of one of you, let him wash it seven times.' Ibn Abd al-Barr said: The hadith of Abu Hurairah is mutawatir in its chains and numerous. The command to pour out is evidence of impurity, likewise 'tahur' because it is a masdar meaning purity, necessitating a prior hadath or khabath, and there is no hadath in the vessel, so the second is determined. And because when a ruling alternates between being devotional and rational, making it rational is the preferred aspect due to the rarity of devotional acts and frequency of rational ones. Our proof is his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Wash the vessel from the lapping of a dog three times,' narrated from Abu Hurairah both as a deed and a saying, marfu' and mawquf, from two paths: The first: al-Daraqutni narrated with a sound chain from Ata' from Abu Hurairah: 'When a dog laps in the vessel, pour it out then wash it three times.' And with this chain from Abu Hurairah that he said: 'When a dog laps in the vessel, pour it out and wash it three times.' Shaykh Taqi al-Din said in al-Ilmam: This is a sound chain. The second path: Ibn Adi narrated in al-Kamil from al-Husayn ibn Ali al-Karabisi with his chain to Ata' from Abu Hurairah who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When a dog laps in the vessel of one of you, let him pour it out and wash it three times.' No one raised it except al-Karabisi. Ibn Adi said: Ahmad al-Husayn al-Karabisi is asked about him, and he has composed books mentioning the differences of people on issues and many reports, and he was a preserver of them, and I did not find any objection to him except this hadith. What caused Ahmad ibn Hanbal to object was due to the wording of the Quran; as for hadith, I see no harm in it. It is known that the judgment of weakness and authenticity is only in appearance; in reality, it is possible that what is judged weak in appearance is authentic, and the fact that the school of Abu Hurairah is as stated with the sound chain is evidence that this hadith is something the weak narrator excelled in. Then it opposes the hadith of seven and takes precedence over it, because with seven there is an indication of abrogation due to the knowledge of the severity concerning dogs initially until killing them was commanded, and severity in their residual water was appropriate at that time, and its abrogation has been established. So when a counter indication opposes, precedence is given to it. Even if we discard the hadith entirely, the practice of Abu Hurairah contrary to the hadith of seven and his narration are sufficient, because it is impossible that he would leave the definitive with his own opinion. This is because the zanniyyah of a solitary report is relative to other than its narrator; as for the narrator who heard it from the Prophet (peace be upon him), it is definitive for him. The previous report has a problem because it is one residual water in reality, but its action on the annex and on the report differs, so it is like two factors. Likewise, there is no problem in treating the difference of action as the difference of factor because the factor is such that it abrogates the Book if it is definitive in meaning, so it follows that he does not leave it except by being certain of the abrogator, since the definitive is not left except by the definitive. Thus their supposition that he left it based on the existence of an abrogator in his ijtihad which is liable to error is invalid. And when you know that, his leaving it is like his narration of the abrogator without doubt, so the other is abrogated necessarily. This is from Fath al-Qadir. Al-Tahawi said: If action on the narration of seven were obligatory and it is not considered abrogated, then what Abdullah ibn al-Mughaffal narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) would be more deserving than what Abu Hurairah narrated, because he added 'and smear the eighth with earth', and the extra is more deserving than the less. So the opponent should act on this addition. If he leaves it, what befell his opponent in leaving the seven befalls him. And Malik did not take the smearing with earth that is established in the Sahih at all, so it is established that it is abrogated. And the hadith of Abdullah ibn al-Mughaffal is agreed upon as authentic, narrated by Muslim and Abu Dawud, so taking his narration is more precautionary. And it is narrated from Abu Hurairah: 'When a cat laps in the vessel, wash it seven times' and they did not act on it. Whatever answer they have for that is our answer for what exceeds three. Or what exceeds three is carried on istihbab. Supporting this is what al-Daraqutni narrated from Abu Hurairah about the dog lapping in the vessel: 'Wash it three, or five, or seven times' – he left it to choice. If tashih were obligatory, he would not have left it to choice. Then know that al-Tahawi and al-Wabiri narrated that our companions did not find a fixed limit for washing the vessel from it; rather the criterion is the strongest opinion, even if once, as is the ruling in washing other impurities. Al-Tahawi mentioned this in Kitab Ikhtilaf al-Ulama, and it contradicts what is in al-Hidayah and others that the vessel from its lapping is washed three times, which is the apparent meaning of the hadith they used as evidence. The explanation of whether three are a condition for removing impurities will come later, God willing. In al-Nihaya: al-wulugh literally is the dog drinking liquids with the tip of its tongue. In Sharh al-Muhadhdhab: the past and present tense are with fatha on the 'ayn; you say walagha yalaghu. We have already stated that the residual water of a dog is impure according to all our companions. For those who hold that its essence is impure, it is obvious. For those who hold the corrected view of its essence being pure, it is because its meat is impure and its saliva is generated from its meat, and the purity of its essence does not necessitate the purity of its residual water due to the impurity of its meat, and the impurity of its residual water does not necessitate the impurity of its essence; rather, the impurity of its residual water necessitates the impurity of its meat from which the saliva is generated, as stated in al-Tanjis, Fath al-Qadir, and others. Its clarification will come in the discussion on the residual water of predators. It is mentioned in the books of the Shafi'is like al-Muhadhdhab that there is no difference between lapping and placing some of its limb in the vessel. I have not seen this in our books. What their speech requires on the view of the impurity of its essence is that water becomes impure; on the view of the purity of its essence, it does not become impure, taken from their statement when a dog laps in a well as we have presented, because well water is in the ruling of little water like vessel water as we have presented. There is no difference between the lapping of one dog or two dogs in sufficing with three, because the second does not cause any impurity, as is obvious. And when a dog laps in food, what their speech requires is that if it is solid, remove the part around it and eat the rest; if it is liquid, benefit from it in other than the body as we have presented.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the ruling on washing a vessel after a dog laps from it. The author begins by presenting the well-known hadith of seven washes with earth, narrated by the 'six imams' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i, Ibn Majah) and others. This is the position of the majority of scholars, including the Shafi'i and Maliki schools. The author then presents the Hanafi proof: the hadith narrated from Abu Hurairah commanding three washes only, supported by both marfu' and mawquf chains. The Hanafis argue that the seven-wash ruling was abrogated, as early severity against dogs was later lifted. They also point out that Abdullah ibn al-Mughaffal's hadith adds an eighth wash with earth, which the Hanafis interpret as further evidence of abrogation since Imam Malik did not adopt it. The Hanafi response to the Shafi'i argument that the seven-wash hadith is stronger is that Abu Hurairah's own practice (three washes) contradicts the seven-wash hadith he narrated, proving abrogation. The passage also discusses the definition of wulugh, the impurity of the dog's residual water, and rules for food. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position is that the vessel must be washed three times; earth is not required. Some Hanafis, like al-Tahawi, reported that there is no fixed number, but the majority view in the school is three washes.

Key Terms
ولوغ (wulugh): The dog drinking liquids by the tips of its tongue
سؤر (su'r): The residual water left after a dog drinks
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation – the later removal of a earlier ruling by a later revelation or sunnah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main evidence the Hanafis use to argue that the seven-wash hadith was abrogated?
A) The hadith itself says it was abrogated
B) The practice of Abu Hurairah who washed three times despite narrating seven
C) The fact that dogs are now considered pure animals
D) The Quran states that three washes suffice

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi abrogation argument for the dog lapping ruling relies on the practice of Abu Hurairah, showing that the seven-wash ruling was superseded.

Dispute on Washes for Dog's Vessel
Defending Hanafi position of three washes against Shafi'i seven

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi argument for three washes against the Shafi'i seven, using the principle of abrogation (naskh).

Core Idea
The definitive ruling of three washes abrogates the hadith of seven; a qat'i text is not abandoned without a qat'i abrogator.

This lesson examines a classic inter-madhhab dispute over the number of times a vessel must be washed after a dog drinks. The Hanafi school holds that three washes suffice, while the Shafi'i school requires seven, including one with dust. The dispute hinges on the usul al-fiqh principle of naskh (abrogation) and the authoritative weight of hadith. By the end, you will grasp how the Hanafis argue their position and why it remains mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of the Hanafi school: washing the vessel three times after a dog drinks, without dust.
2
Identify the opponent's view
State the Shafi'i position: seven washes, with one of them using dust.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the hadith evidence cited by the Shafi'is: the hadith of Abu Hurayra (seven washes) and the addition of dust by Abdullah ibn Mughaffal.
The dust version is stronger in wording but less widely transmitted.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Follow the Hanafi rebuttal: the seven-wash hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and conflicts with the definitive (qat'i) principle that a qat'i text is not abandoned except by another qat'i. Tahawi also argues that the dust addition, if authentic, would be more complete and should be followed, but even Malik abandoned it, proving abrogation.
The key is that the ruling of three is considered qat'i due to consensus and practice.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical difference: Hanafi performs three washes without dust; Shafi'i performs seven with one dusting.
This difference affects daily practice in purification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حتى ينسخ به الكتاب إذا كان قطعي الدلالة في معناه فلزم أنه لا يتركه إلا لقطعه بالناسخ إذ القطعي لا يترك إلا لقطعي فبطل تجويز هم تركه بناء على ثبوت ناسخ في اجتهاده المحتمل للخطاً. وإذا علمت ذلك كان تركه بمنزلة روايته للناسخ بلا شبهة فيكون الآخر منسوخاً بالضرورة. كذا في فتح القدير. وقال الطحاوي: ولو وجب العمل برواية السبع ولا يجعل منسوخاً لكان ما روى عبد الله بن المغفل في ذلك عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أولى مما روى أبو هريرة لأنه زاد عليه وعفروا الثامنة بالتراب والزائد أولى من الناقص فكان ينبغي للمخالف أن يعمل بهذه الزيادة، فإن تركها لزمه ما لزم خصمه في ترك السبع، ومالك لم يأخذ بالتعفير الثابت في الصحيح مطلقاً فثبت أنه منسوخ أهـ.
until the Book is abrogated by it, since it is definitive in meaning, it follows that he does not abandon it except for his certainty of an abrogator, because the definitive is not abandoned except by the definitive. So his allowance of abandoning it based on the existence of an abrogator in his ijtihad that is subject to error is invalid. And when you know that, his abandonment is equivalent to his narration of the abrogator without doubt, so the other is necessarily abrogated. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And al-Tahawi said: If acting upon the narration of seven was obligatory and not considered abrogated, then what was narrated by Abdullah ibn Mughaffal from the Prophet (peace be upon him) would be more deserving than what was narrated by Abu Hurayra, because he added to it: 'and sprinkle the eighth with dust,' and the more is preferable to the less. So the opponent should have acted upon this addition, and if he abandoned it, the same applies to him as applies to his opponent in abandoning the seven. And Malik did not take the dusting established in the Sahih at all, so it is proven that it is abrogated.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute defending the Hanafi position that the dog's vessel is washed three times, not seven. The argument uses usul al-fiqh principles: a definitive (qat'i) text is not abandoned except by another definitive. The Hanafis argue that the seven-wash hadith is abrogated. Al-Tahawi adds that even if it were not abrogated, the version with dusting the eighth time (from Abdullah ibn Mughaffal) is more complete and would be preferred, so the opponent's abandonment of that addition incurs the same criticism. The fact that Imam Malik did not act on the dusting in the sahih hadith further proves the ruling is abrogated.

Key Terms
قطعي الدلالة (qat'i al-dalalah): A text with definitive meaning that admits no interpretation
ناسخ (nasikh): An abrogating evidence that supersedes a previous ruling

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Seven times
B) Three times
C) Once
D) Until clean

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position of three washes is based on the principle that a definitive ruling is not abandoned except by a definitive abrogator.

Definition of Walugh and Ruling on Dog's and Pig's Su'r
Stating Hanafi positions on su'r of dog and pig with definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the su'r of a dog and a pig, and explain the definition of walugh.

Core Idea
Dog's saliva is impure; pig is intrinsically impure — their leftover water is najis.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defines the term 'walugh' and clarifies the Hanafi position on the leftover water (su'r) of dogs and pigs. It also discusses an intra-school difference regarding the number of washes for a dog's vessel.

Guided Path
1
Define walugh
Identify the literal meaning of walugh as a dog drinking liquids with the tips of its tongue. Understand that it is specific to dogs in Hanafi fiqh.
Shafi'i school extends walugh to any limb entering the vessel.
2
State the ruling on dog's su'r
According to all Hanafis, the leftover water after a dog drinks is najis (impure). Understand the basis: even if the dog's body is considered pure, its flesh is impure and saliva arises from flesh.
There is an intra-school ikhtilaf on whether the dog's essence is pure or impure.
3
Differentiate essence vs. saliva
Note that impurity of su'r does not imply impurity of the dog's body. The dog's hair and bones are pure. Only the saliva and flesh are impure.
This distinction is important for practical rulings.
4
State the ruling on pig's su'r
The pig is najis al-ayn (intrinsically impure) based on Quran 6:145. Hence its su'r is also najis.
5
Apply practical consequences
For a dog's vessel, the dominant view requires washing three times. If a dog drinks from solid food, remove the affected part; if from liquid, use it only for non-body purposes.
The opinion of no fixed number is also transmitted but marjuh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن الطحاوي والوبري نقلا أن أصحابنا لم يجدوا لغسل الإناء منه حداً بل العبرة لأكبر الرأي ولو بمرة كما هو الحكم في غسل غيره من النجاسات . ذكره الطحاوي في كتاب اختلاف العلماء وهو مخالف لما في الهداية وغيرها أنه يغسل الإناء من ولوغه ثلاثاً وهو ظاهر الحديث الذي استدلوا به وسيأتي بيان أن الثلاث هل هي شرط في إزالة الأنجاس أو لا إن شاء الله تعالى. وفي النهاية : الولوغ حقيقة شرب الكلب المائعات باطراف لسانه . وفي شرح المهذب : إن الماضي والمضارع بفتح العين تقول وَلَغَ يَلَغُ. وقد قدمنا أن سؤر الكلب نجس عند أصحابنا جميعاً، أما على القول بنجاسة عينه فظاهر، وأما على القول المصحح بطهارة عينه فلأن لحمه نجس ولعابه متولد من لحمه ولا يلزم من طهارة عينه طهارة سؤره لنجاسة لحمه ولا يلزم من نجاسة سؤره نجاسة عينه وإنما يلزم من نجاسة سؤرة نجاسة لحمه المتولد منه اللعاب كما صرح به في التنجيس وفتح القدير وغيرهما، وسيأتي أيضاحه في الكلام على سؤر السباع. والمذكور في كتب الشافعية كالمهذب أنه لا فرق بين الولوغ ووضع بعض عضوه في الإناء، ولم أر هذا في كتبنا والذي يقتضيه كلامهم على القول بنجاسة عينه تنجس الماء وعلى القول بطهارة عينه عدم تنجسه أخذاً من قولهم إذا ولغ الكلب في البئر كما قدمناه لأن ماء البئر في حكم الماء القليل كماء الآنية كما قدمناه. ولا فرق بين ولوغ كلب أو كلبين في الاكتفاء بالثلاث لأن الثاني لو يوجب تنجساً كما لا يخفى . وإذا ولغ الكلب في طعام فالذي يقتضيه كلامهم أنه إن كان جامداً قدر ما حوله وأكل الباقي، وإن كان مائعاً انتفع به في غير الأبدان كما قدمناه. وأما سؤر الخنزير فلأنه نجس العين لقوله تعالى أو لحم خنزير فإنه رجس [الأنعام: ١٤٥] والرجس النجس والضمير عائد إليه لقربه وقد بسطنا الكلام فيه في الكلام على جلده
Then know that al-Tahawi and al-Wabari transmitted that our companions did not find a limit for washing the vessel from it, rather the criterion is the greater opinion, even if once, as is the ruling in washing other impurities. Al-Tahawi mentioned this in the book Ikhtilaf al-‘Ulama’, and it contradicts what is in al-Hidayah and others, that the vessel is washed from its drinking three times, which is apparent from the hadith they used. And there will come an explanation of whether three is a condition for removing impurities or not, God willing. And in al-Nihayah: al-walugh is literally the dog drinking liquids with the tips of its tongue. And in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab: the past and present tenses have a fatha on the ‘ayn; you say walagha yalaghu. And we have already presented that the su'r of the dog is najis according to all our companions. As for the opinion of its essence being najis, it is apparent; and as for the opinion that its essence is pure, it is because its flesh is najis and its saliva is generated from its flesh. The purity of its essence does not necessitate the purity of its su'r due to the impurity of its flesh, and the impurity of its su'r does not necessitate the impurity of its essence. Rather, the impurity of its su'r necessitates the impurity of its flesh from which the saliva is generated, as explained in al-Tanjis and Fath al-Qadir and others. And it will be clarified in the discussion of the su'r of predatory animals. And it is mentioned in Shafi'i books like al-Muhadhdhab that there is no difference between drinking (walugh) and placing some part of its limb in the vessel. I have not seen this in our books. What is required from their statements on the opinion of its essence being najis is that the water becomes najis; and on the opinion of its essence being pure is that it does not become najis, taken from their statement when a dog drinks from a well as we presented, because well water is in the ruling of little water like vessel water. And there is no difference between one dog drinking or two in sufficing with three, because the second would not cause impurity as is obvious. And if a dog drinks from food, what is required from their statements is that if it is solid, one removes what is around it and eats the rest; if it is liquid, it is used for other than bodies as we presented. As for the su'r of a pig, it is najis al-‘ayn because of His statement 'or the flesh of a pig, for it is abomination' (al-An'am 145), and 'abomination' (rijs) means najis, and the pronoun refers to it due to its proximity. We have expanded the discussion on it in the discussion on its skin.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement with definitions. It presents views within the Hanafi school: al-Tahawi and al-Wabari transmitted that some Hanafis did not fix a specific number of washes for a dog's vessel, but rather it is based on the stronger opinion (istihsan), even if once. This differs from the dominant view in al-Hidayah that three washes are required. The author then defines 'walugh' literally as a dog drinking liquids with its tongue tips. The su'r (leftover water) of a dog is najis according to all Hanafis. Two opinions exist on the dog's essence (ayn): some say it is najis, others that it is pure, but even if the essence is pure, the saliva is najis because it is generated from impure flesh. The impurity of the su'r does not imply the impurity of the dog's body, but rather the body's flesh is impure. There is no difference between one dog or two dogs in requiring three washes. If a dog drinks from solid food, the affected part is removed; if from liquid, it is used for non-body purposes. For the pig, its su'r is najis because the pig itself is najis al-‘ayn, based on Quran 6:145 where pig flesh is called 'rijs' (impure).

Key Terms
الولوغ (al-walugh): Literally a dog drinking liquids with the tips of its tongue
السؤر (al-su'r): The leftover water or liquid after an animal drinks
نجس العين (najis al-ayn): Intrinsically impure entity, such as a pig

A) Pure
B) Makruh
C) Najis because the pig is najis al-ayn

The su'r of a dog and pig are najis; for a dog, the vessel should be washed three times.

Dispute on Su'r of Predatory Animals
Presenting Shafi'i position and Hanafi response on predatory animal su'r

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the su'r of predatory land animals and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds that the su'r of fanged predators is najis because prohibition of eating implies impurity, while Shafi'i proofs are weak or apply only to abundant water.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author presents the Shafi'i position that the leftover water of predatory animals is pure, citing several hadiths and the practice of Umar. The Hanafi response is then given, arguing that the prohibition of eating such animals implies impurity and that the Shafi'i hadiths are either weak or can be interpreted consistently with the Hanafi view. Understanding this dispute clarifies a key difference between the schools in rulings on water purity.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school rules the su'r of predatory land animals as najis. This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that such su'r is pure. Note the thamarah: for Hanafi, water less than two qullas becomes impure; for Shafi'i, it remains pure regardless.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i school cites hadiths: (1) Jabir's hadith about donkeys and predators, (2) the practice of Umar not inquiring about predators at a cistern, (3) the hadith of Ibn Umar about predators drinking from a pond.
These are the main Shafi'i arguments as presented in the text.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response has two parts: (a) the primary evidence from the prohibition of eating fanged predators, and (b) a critique of the Shafi'i hadiths as weak or interpretable. Also, the Hanafi use the qullatayn hadith to limit any Shafi'i evidence to large water bodies.
Note the use of the hadith of two qullas as a binding argument.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice: if a lion drinks from a small bucket of water (less than two qullas), the Hanafi says the water is najis and cannot be used for wudu; the Shafi'i says it remains pure.
This is the direct practical consequence for daily life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما سؤر سباع البهائم فقد قال الشافعي بطهارته محتجاً بما رواه البيهقي والدارقطني عن جابر قال قيل: يا رسول الله أنتوضأ بما أفضلت الحمر؟ قال: نعم وبما أفضلت السباع كلها بما رواه مالك في الموطأ أن عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه خرج في ركب فيهم عمرو بن العاص حتى وردوا حوضاً فقال عمرو بن العاص : يا صاحب الحوض هل ترد حوضك السباع؟ فقال عمر بن الخطاب : يا صاحب الحوض لا تخبره فإنا نرد على السباع وترد علينا. وبما رواه ابن ماجه عن ابن عمر قال : خرج علينا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في بعض أسفاره فسار ليلاً فمروا على رجل عند مقراة له فقال عمر : يا صاحب المقراة أو لغت السباع الليلة في مقراتك؟ فقال عليه السلام يا صاحب المقراة لا تخبره هذا مكلف لها ما حملت في بطونها ولنا ما بقي شراب وطهور. ولنا أنه نهى عن أكل كل ذي ناب من السباع والظاهر من الحرمة مع كونه صالحاً للغذاء غير مستقذر طبعاً كونه للنجاسة وخبث طباعها لا ينافيه بل ذلك يصلح مثيراً لحكم النجاسة فليكن المثير لها فيجامعها ترتيباً على الوصف الصالح للعلية مقتضاه، ولأنه ليس فيه ضرورة وعموم بلوى فيخرج السنور والفأرة، ولأن لسانه يلاقي الماء فيخرج سباع الطير لأنه يشرب بمنقاره كما سيأتي. ولم تتعارض أدلته فيخرج البغل والحمار، وأما حديث جابر فقد اعترف النووي بضعفه وأما أثر الموطأ فهو وإن صححه البيهقي وذكر أنه مرسل يحتج به على أبي حنيفة فقد ضعفه ابن معين والدارقطني وأما حديث ابن ماجه فقد ضعفه ابن عدي، وعلى تسليم الصحة يحمل على الماء الكثير أو على ما قبل تحريم لحوم السباع أو على الوحش وسباع الطير بدليل ما تمسكوا به من حديث القلتين فإنه صلى الله عليه وسلم قال «إذا بلغ الماء قلتين لم يحمل خبثاً جواباً لسؤاله عن الماء يكون في الفلاة وما ينوبه من السباع اعطاء لحكم هذا الماء الذي ترده السباع ،وغيره فإن الجواب لا بد أن يطابق أو يزيد فيندرج فيه المسؤول عنه وغيره وقد قال بمفهوم شرطه فنجس ما دون القلتين وإن لم يتغير، وحقيقة مفهوم شرطه أنه إذا لم يبلغها يتنجس من ورود السباع وهذا من الوجوه الإلزامية له
As for the su'r of predatory land animals, al-Shafi'i said it is pure, arguing with what al-Bayhaqi and al-Daraqutni narrated from Jabir: it was said, O Messenger of Allah, may we perform wudu with what the donkeys leave? He said: Yes, and with what all predatory animals leave. Also what Malik narrated in al-Muwatta that Umar ibn al-Khattab went out in a group including Amr ibn al-As until they came to a cistern, and Amr said: O owner of the cistern, do predatory animals come to your cistern? Umar said: O owner of the cistern, do not tell him, for we come to predatory animals and they come to us. Also what Ibn Majah narrated from Ibn Umar: the Messenger of Allah came out to us on one of his journeys and traveled at night, and they passed by a man at his pond. Umar said: O owner of the pond, did predatory animals drink from your pond tonight? He (peace be upon him) said: O owner of the pond, do not tell him; what they carried in their stomachs is for them, and what remains is for us, drink and pure. Our evidence is that he forbade eating every fanged predator. The apparent from the prohibition, given it is suitable for food and not naturally repulsive, is that it is due to impurity and the viciousness of their nature. That does not contradict; rather it suffices as a cause for the ruling of impurity. So the cause is that which combines them, based on the description suitable for 'illah. Also because there is no necessity and general affliction; this excludes the cat and mouse. Also because its tongue contacts water; this excludes predatory birds because they drink with their beaks as will come. And its evidences do not conflict; this excludes the mule and donkey. As for the hadith of Jabir, al-Nawawi acknowledged its weakness. As for the athar of al-Muwatta, although al-Bayhaqi authenticated it and mentioned it is mursal, arguing against Abu Hanifa, Ibn Ma'in and al-Daraqutni weakened it. As for the hadith of Ibn Majah, Ibn Adi weakened it. Even granting authenticity, it is interpreted as referring to abundant water, or to before the prohibition of eating predatory animals, or to wild animals and predatory birds, as indicated by their own evidence from the hadith of the two qullas: he (peace be upon him) said 'When water reaches two qullas, it does not carry impurity' in response to a question about water in the desert that predatory animals visit. This gives the ruling for this water visited by predators and others. The answer must correspond or add, so it includes the asked-about and others. He stated a conditional implication: water less than two qullas becomes impure from the visit of predators, even if unchanged. The reality of its conditional implication is that if it does not reach two qullas, it becomes impure from the arrival of predators. This is one of the binding arguments against him.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the su'r (leftover water) of predatory land animals (siba' al-baha'im). Imam al-Shafi'i holds it is pure, citing hadiths: the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet permitted wudu with water left by predatory animals, the practice of Umar not inquiring about predators at a cistern, and the hadith of Ibn Umar about predators drinking from a pond. The Hanafi school holds it is najis. Their evidence: the Prophet forbade eating fanged predators; the underlying cause for prohibition is impurity and vicious nature, not just prohibition of eating. Also, there is no general necessity for using such water (unlike cats and mice which are exempt due to constant presence). Predatory birds are excluded because they drink with beaks, not tongues. The Hanafis respond to the Shafi'i hadiths by declaring them weak (Jabir's hadith weak according to Nawawi; the Muwatta athar weakened by Ibn Ma'in and Daraqutni; Ibn Majah's hadith weakened by Ibn Adi). Even if authentic, they interpret them as referring to large quantities of water (two qullas or more) based on the hadith of qullatayn: water less than two qullas becomes impure from predators. This argument is binding on the Shafi'is because they themselves use the qullatayn hadith as evidence.

Key Terms
سباع البهائم (siba' al-baha'im): Predatory land animals with fangs, such as lions, wolves, etc.
القلتين (al-qullatayn): Two large water skins; a measure of water volume, approximately 200 liters

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on the su'r of a lion?
A) Pure
B) Najis
C) Makruh
D) Depends on quantity

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school considers the su'r of fanged predatory land animals as najis, but water exceeding two qullas remains pure even if a predator drinks.

Zayla'i's Critique of Hanafi Inconsistency on Su'r of Non-Edible Animals
Zayla'i identifies a logical inconsistency in Hanafi rulings on su'r

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Zayla'i's critique of the Hanafi position on su'r of non-edible animals and identify the underlying inconsistency in the reasoning.

Core Idea
If dhabh purifies the flesh, why is its su'r still impure? Zayla'i exposes a logical gap.

In this passage, the great Hanafi jurist Zayla'i (d. 762 AH) raises a penetrating objection to a well-known Hanafi ruling: the su'r (leftover water) of a non-edible predatory animal is considered impure (najis). Yet the same animal's flesh is purified by ritual slaughter (dhabh). How can the flesh be pure but its water be impure? Zayla'i dissects the reasoning and proposes a refined understanding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position on su'r of non-edible animals
The school holds that such su'r is najis because it is generated from impure flesh. But if the animal is slaughtered, the flesh becomes pure.
2
Understand Zayla'i's logical challenge
He argues: if the flesh is impure by essence (ayn), then dhabh should not purify it (like pig). If the impurity is only due to blood, then edible animals also have blood, so why differentiate their su'r?
3
Analyze the alternative view mentioned
Some scholars concluded that dhabh only purifies the skin, not the flesh, because prohibition of eating does not imply impurity.
4
Evaluate the consistency of the Hanafi position
Consider whether the standard response (su'r is impure because generated before dhabh) resolves the issue or if Zayla'i's critique stands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حمر قال الزيلعي رحمه الله : ثم اعلم أن في مذهب أصحابنا في سؤر ما لا يؤكل لحمه من السباع إشكالاً فإنهم يقولون لأنه متولد من لحم نجس ثم يقولون إذا ذكي طهر لحمه لأن نجاسته لأجل رطوبة الدم وقد خرج بالذكاة فإن كانوا يعنون بقولهم نجس عينه وجب أن لا يطهر بالذكاة كالخنزير، وإن كانوا يعنون به لأجل مجاورة الدم فالمأكول كذلك يجاوره الدم، فمن أين جاء الاختلاف بينهما في السؤر إذا كان كل واحد منها يطهر بالذكاة ويتنجس بموته حتف أنفه ولا فرق بينهما إلا في المذكي في حق الأكل والحرمة لا توجب النجاسة؟ وكم من طاهر لا يحل أكله ومن ثم قال بعضهم : لا يطهر بالذكاة إلا جلده لأن حرمة لحمه لا لكرامته
Humar. Al-Zayla'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Then know that in the madhhab of our companions regarding the su'r of what is not eaten from predatory animals, there is an inconsistency. For they say it is generated from impure flesh, then they say if it is slaughtered (dhakka), its flesh becomes pure because its impurity is due to moisture of blood, and it is removed by dhabh. If they mean by their statement that its essence (ayn) is impure, then it must not be purified by dhabh, like the pig. And if they mean it is due to the adjacency of blood, then edible animals also have blood adjacent. So where does the difference come between them in su'r, when each of them is purified by dhabh and becomes impure by natural death? There is no difference between them except in the slaughtered one concerning eating, and prohibition does not necessitate impurity. And how many pure things are not permissible to eat? Hence some said: only its skin is purified by dhabh, because the prohibition of its flesh is not due to its honor.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by Zayla'i, pointing out an apparent inconsistency in the Hanafi school's position on the su'r of non-edible predatory animals. The Hanafis say that the su'r of such animals is najis because it is generated from impure flesh. However, if the animal is slaughtered (dhabh), its flesh becomes pure because the impurity was due to the moisture of blood that is drained by slaughter. Zayla'i argues that if the animal's essence (ayn) were impure, slaughter would not purify it, just as it does not purify a pig. If, on the other hand, the impurity is only due to the blood, then edible animals also have blood, so there should be no difference. Both types become pure by dhabh and impure by natural death. The only practical difference is that the slaughtered non-edible animal is not permissible to eat, but prohibition does not entail impurity. Many things are pure but not edible, like wood. Therefore, some scholars argued that only the skin of such animals is purified by dhabh, not the flesh, because the prohibition of eating is not due to impurity but to lack of honor (karamah).

Key Terms
الذكاة (al-dhakah): Ritual slaughter that purifies the animal's meat and skin
سؤر (su'r): Leftover water or liquid after an animal drinks

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zayla'i, what is the inconsistency in the Hanafi position on non-edible predatory animals?
A) They say su'r is pure but flesh is impure
B) They say dhabh purifies the flesh but su'r remains impure, despite both being from the same animal
C) They say the animal is pure but its su'r is impure
D) They have no inconsistency

Key Takeaway
Zayla'i's critique reveals that the Hanafi ruling on su'r of non-edible animals is not self-evident and requires careful consideration of the source of impurity and the role of dhabh.

The Hanafi Position on Predator Leftover Water
Inter-madhhab dispute on purity of predator leftover water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the purity of su'r al-siba' and evaluate the Hanafi rebuttals to the Shafi'i proofs.

Core Idea
Predator leftover water is impure because the meat is prohibited, indicating impurity.

This lesson examines a classical inter-madhhab dispute: whether the leftover water of predatory land animals is pure or impure. The Hanafi school rules it impure, while the Shafi'i school considers it pure. We will analyze the proofs from both sides and the Hanafi rebuttals, focusing on the hadith of two qullas and the prohibition of fanged predators.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i position
Identify that al-Shafi'i holds the su'r is pure, and list his three proofs: the hadith of Jabir, the practice of 'Umar, and the hadith of 'do not tell him'.
Opposing school: Imam al-Shafi'i.
2
State the Hanafi position and primary proof
The Hanafi position is that su'r is najis. The primary proof is the Prophet's prohibition of eating fanged predators, which implies impurity of the meat and thus impurity of the saliva.
Also note exceptions: cat, mouse, predatory birds, mule, donkey.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal of Shafi'i proofs
The Hanafi school weakens the Shafi'i hadiths and interprets them as referring to large water quantities or before the prohibition. The hadith of two qullas is used as a strong counter-proof.
Conditional implication: water below two qullas becomes impure.
4
Apply the hadith of two qullas to the dispute
The two qullas hadith gives a clear ruling: water less than two qullas that is visited by predatory beasts becomes impure, even without change.
This is a decisive dalil for Hanafis.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis consider such water impure and invalid for purification; Shafi'is consider it pure.
