⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما سؤر سباع البهائم فقد قال الشافعي بطهارته محتجاً بما رواه البيهقي والدارقطني عن جابر قال قيل: يا رسول الله أنتوضأ بما أفضلت الحمر؟ قال: نعم وبما أفضلت السباع كلها بما رواه مالك في الموطأ أن عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه خرج في ركب فيهم عمرو بن العاص حتى وردوا حوضاً فقال عمرو بن العاص : يا صاحب الحوض هل ترد حوضك السباع؟ فقال عمر بن الخطاب : يا صاحب الحوض لا تخبره فإنا نرد على السباع وترد علينا. وبما رواه ابن ماجه عن ابن عمر قال : خرج علينا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في بعض أسفاره فسار ليلاً فمروا على رجل عند مقراة له فقال عمر : يا صاحب المقراة أو لغت السباع الليلة في مقراتك؟ فقال عليه السلام يا صاحب المقراة لا تخبره هذا مكلف لها ما حملت في بطونها ولنا ما بقي شراب وطهور. ولنا أنه نهى عن أكل كل ذي ناب من السباع والظاهر من الحرمة مع كونه صالحاً للغذاء غير مستقذر طبعاً كونه للنجاسة وخبث طباعها لا ينافيه بل ذلك يصلح مثيراً لحكم النجاسة فليكن المثير لها فيجامعها ترتيباً على الوصف الصالح للعلية مقتضاه، ولأنه ليس فيه ضرورة وعموم بلوى فيخرج السنور والفأرة، ولأن لسانه يلاقي الماء فيخرج سباع الطير لأنه يشرب بمنقاره كما سيأتي. ولم تتعارض أدلته فيخرج البغل والحمار، وأما حديث جابر فقد اعترف النووي بضعفه وأما أثر الموطأ فهو وإن صححه البيهقي وذكر أنه مرسل يحتج به على أبي حنيفة فقد ضعفه ابن معين والدارقطني وأما حديث ابن ماجه فقد ضعفه ابن . عدي، وعلى تسليم الصحة يحمل على الماء الكثير أو على ما قبل تحريم لحوم السباع أو على الوحش وسباع الطير بدليل ما تمسكوا به من حديث القلتين فإنه صلى الله عليه وسلم قال «إذا بلغ الماء قلتين لم يحمل خبثاً جواباً لسؤاله عن الماء يكون في الفلاة وما ينوبه من السباع اعطاء لحكم هذا الماء الذي ترده السباع ،وغيره فإن الجواب لا بد أن يطابق أو يزيد فيندرج فيه المسؤول عنه وغيره وقد قال بمفهوم شرطه فنجس ما دون القلتين وإن لم يتغير، وحقيقة مفهوم شرطه أنه إذا لم يبلغها يتنجس من ورود السباع وهذا من الوجوه الإلزامية له . حمر قال الزيلعي رحمه الله : ثم اعلم أن في مذهب أصحابنا في سؤر ما لا يؤكل لحمه من السباع إشكالاً فإنهم يقولون لأنه متولد من لحم نجس ثم يقولون إذا ذكي طهر لحمه لأن نجاسته لأجل رطوبة الدم وقد خرج بالذكاة فإن كانوا يعنون بقولهم نجس عينه وجب أن لا يطهر بالذكاة كالخنزير، وإن كانوا يعنون به لأجل مجاورة الدم فالمأكول كذلك يجاوره الدم، فمن أين جاء الاختلاف بينهما في السؤر إذا كان كل واحد منها يطهر بالذكاة ويتنجس بموته حتف أنفه ولا فرق بينهما إلا في المذكي في حق الأكل والحرمة لا توجب النجاسة؟ وكم من طاهر لا يحل أكله ومن ثم قال بعضهم : لا يطهر بالذكاة إلا جلده لأن حرمة لحمه لا لكرامته آية نجاسته لكن بين الجلد واللحم جلدة رقيقة تمنع تنجس الجلد باللحم وهذا هو الصحيح لأن لا وجه لنجاسة السؤر إلا بهذا الطريق أهـ. وقد ذكر في العناية حاصل هذا الإشكال وذكر أنها نكتة لا بأس بالتنبيه عليها ثم قال : وحلما أن المراد باللحم الطاهر المتولد منه اللعاب ما يحل أكله بعد الذبح وبالنجس ما يقابله وهذا لأنهما اشتركا في النجاسة المجارة بالدم المسفوح قبل الذبح فإن الشاة لا تؤكل إذا ماتت حتف أنفها واشتركا في الطهارة بعده لزوال المنجس وهو الدم فلا فرق بينهما إلا أن الشاة تؤكل بعد الذبح دون الكلب، ولا فرق بينهما أيضاً في الظاهر إلا اختلاط اللعاب المتولد من اللحم. فعلم من هذا أن اللعاب المتولد من لحم مأكول بعد الذبح طاهر بلا كراهة دون غيره إضافة للحكم إلى الفارق صيانة لحكم الشرع عن المناقضة ظاهراً. هذا ما سنح لي أهـ. ولا يخفى ما في هذا الجواب فإن قول الزيلعي والحرمة لا توجب النجاسة» يرده بل الجواب الصحيح ما في شرح الوقاية وهو أن الحرمة إذا لم تكن للكرامة فإنها آية النجاسة لكن فيه شبهة أن النجاسة لاختلاط الدم باللحم إذ لولا ذلك بل نجاسته لذاته لكان نجس العين وليس كذلك، فغير مأكول اللحم إذا كان حياً فلعابه متولد من اللحم الحرام المخلوط بالدم فيكون نجساً لاجتماع الأمرين، أما في مأكول اللحم فلم يوجد إلا أحدهما وهو الاختلاط بالدم فلم يوجب نجاسة السؤر لأن هذه العلة بانفرادها ضعيفة إذ الدم المستقر في موضعه لم يعط له حكم النجاسة في الحي. وإذا لم يكن حياً، فإن لم يكن مذكى كان نجساً، سواء كان مأكول اللحم أو غيره، لأنه صار حراماً بالموت، فالحرمة موجودة مع اختلاط الدم فيكون نجساً، فإذا كان مذكى كان طاهراً؛ أما في مأكول اللحم فلأنه لم توجد الحرمة ولا اختلاط الدم، وأما في غير مأكول اللحم فلأنه لم يوجد الاختلاط والحرمة المجردة غير كافية في النجاسة على ما مر أنها تثبت باجتماع الأمرين أهـ. فحاصله أن نجاسة اللحم لحرمته مع اختلاط الدم المسفوح به وقد فقد الثاني في المذكى من السباع فكان طاهراً واجتمعا في حالتي الموت والحياة فكان نجساً، وفقد الأول في الشاة حالة الحياة والذكاة فكان طاهراً واجتمعا حالة الموت فكان نجساً. فظهر هذا كله إن طهارة العين لا تستلزم طهارة اللحم لأن السباع طاهرة العين باتفاق اصحابنا كما نقله عضيم مع أن لحمها نجس فثبت بهذا ما قدمناه من أن الكلب طاهر العين ولحمه نجس ونجاسة سؤره لنجاسة لحمه . لكن بقي ههنا كلام وهو أن قولهم بين الجلد واللحم جلدة رقيقة تمنع على القول بأن العامل في الخبر هو الابتداء أو الابتداء والمبتدأ قوله : ولا يخفى ما في هذا الجواب الخ) أقول : يمكن إرجاع ما ذكره في العناية إلى ما قاله في شرح الوقاية من أن العلة الحرمة مع اختلاط الدم وذلك ظاهر بأدنى تأمل، فإنه بعد ما ذكر اشتراك المأكول وغيره في النجاسة المجاورة بالدم ذكر انفراد غير المأكول بالحرمة فقد اجتمع في غير المأكول الأمران بخلاف المأكول، فكانت
As for the leftover water of predatory beasts, al-Shafi'i said it is pure, using as proof what al-Bayhaqi and al-Daraqutni narrated from Jabir: it was said, 'O Messenger of Allah, do we perform wudu with what the donkeys leave?' He said: 'Yes, and with what all predatory beasts leave.' And what Malik narrated in al-Muwatta that Umar ibn al-Khattab went out in a group including Amr ibn al-As until they reached a watering hole. Amr ibn al-As said: 'O owner of the watering hole, do predatory beasts come to your watering hole?' Umar ibn al-Khattab said: 'O owner of the watering hole, do not tell him; for we go to the predatory beasts and they come to us.' And what Ibn Majah narrated from Ibn Umar: the Messenger of Allah went out on one of his journeys, traveling by night, and they passed by a man at his water trough. Umar said: 'O owner of the trough, did the predatory beasts drink from your trough tonight?' He (peace be upon him) said: 'O owner of the trough, do not tell him; they have what they carried in their bellies, and we have what remains as drink and pure.' Our evidence: it is prohibited to eat every fanged predator, and the apparent from the prohibition, while it is suitable for food and not naturally disgusting, is that it indicates impurity. The baseness of their nature does not contradict this; rather, that is suitable as a motivating factor for the ruling of impurity. So let it be the motivator for it, in conjunction with it, by ordering based on the description suitable for being a cause, as required. And because there is no necessity and general affliction, so the cat and mouse are excluded. And because its tongue contacts the water, so predatory birds are excluded because they drink with their beaks, as will come. And their evidences do not contradict, so the mule and donkey are excluded. As for the hadith of Jabir, al-Nawawi acknowledged its weakness. As for the athar of al-Muwatta, even if al-Bayhaqi authenticated it and mentioned it is mursal, using it as evidence against Abu Hanifa, Ibn Ma'in and al-Daraqutni weakened it. As for the hadith of Ibn Majah, Ibn Adi weakened it. And assuming authenticity, it is interpreted as referring to a large quantity of water, or before the prohibition of eating predator meat, or to wild animals and predatory birds, based on their proof from the hadith of two qullas: he (peace be upon him) said: 'When water reaches two qullas, it does not carry impurity' in answer to his question about water in the desert and what predatory beasts visit it, giving a ruling for this water that predatory beasts visit and others. For the answer must match or increase, so what is asked about and others are included. And he ruled by the implication of its condition: what is less than two qullas is impure even if unchanged. The reality of its conditional implication is that if it does not reach that amount, it becomes impure from the visitation of predatory beasts. This is among the compelling proofs against him. [Then] al-Zayla'i said: Know that there is an inconsistency in the school of our companions regarding the leftover water of what is not eaten from predatory beasts: they say it is generated from impure meat, then they say if it is slaughtered, its meat becomes pure because its impurity is due to blood moisture, and it is removed by slaughter. If they mean by their statement 'impure in itself', it must not be purified by slaughter like the pig. And if they mean by it due to the adjacency of blood, then the edible meat also has blood adjacent to it. So where does the difference come between them in the leftover water, if each of them is purified by slaughter and becomes impure by dying naturally, and there is no difference between them except in the slaughtered one regarding eating? Prohibition does not necessitate impurity. How many pure things are not permissible to eat? Hence some said: only its hide is purified by slaughter because the prohibition of its meat is not due to its honorableness but it is a sign of its impurity. However, between the hide and the meat there is a thin membrane that prevents the hide from being impurified by the meat, and this is correct because there is no basis for the impurity of the leftover water except by this path. And it was mentioned in al-Inayah the essence of this inconsistency, and it mentioned that it is a point worth noting, then it said: The solution is that what is meant by the pure meat from which saliva is generated is what is permissible to eat after slaughter, and by impure meat is the opposite. This is because they both share in the impurity adjacent to spilled blood before slaughter: the sheep is not eaten if it dies naturally, and they both share in purity after it due to the removal of the impurity, which is blood. So there is no difference between them except that the sheep is eaten after slaughter while the dog is not. There is also no difference externally except the mixture of saliva generated from the meat. So it is known from this that the saliva generated from edible meat after slaughter is pure without dislike, unlike others, attributing the ruling to the distinguishing factor to protect the Sharia ruling from apparent contradiction. This is what occurred to me. It is not hidden that this answer has [issues], for al-Zayla'i's statement 'Prohibition does not necessitate impurity' refutes it. Rather, the correct answer is what is in Sharh al-Wiqayah: that if the prohibition is not due to honorability, it is a sign of impurity. But there is a doubt: impurity is due to the mixing of blood with meat, for if not for that, but rather its impurity in itself, it would be impure in essence, and it is not so. So the meat of a non-edible animal when alive, its saliva is generated from the prohibited meat mixed with blood, so it is impure due to the combination of two factors. As for edible meat, only one factor exists, which is the mixing with blood, so it does not necessitate the impurity of the leftover water because this cause alone is weak, since blood settled in its place does not give it the ruling of impurity in the living animal. And if it is not alive, if it is not slaughtered, it is impure, whether the meat is edible or not, because it becomes prohibited by death. So the prohibition exists with the mixing of blood, so it is impure. If it is slaughtered, it is pure. As for edible meat, because neither prohibition nor mixing of blood exists. As for non-edible meat, because the mixing does not exist and mere prohibition is not sufficient for impurity, as it was established that it is proven by the combination of the two factors. The gist is that the impurity of meat is due to its prohibition along with mixing of spilled blood. The second factor is absent in the slaughtered predatory beast, so it is pure, and both combine in states of death and life, so it is impure. The first factor is absent in the sheep in the state of life and slaughter, so it is pure, and both combine in the state of death, so it is impure. So it is clear from all this that the purity of the animal itself does not necessitate the purity of its meat, because predatory beasts are pure in themselves by agreement of our companions, as transmitted by 'Adhim, while their meat is impure. So this proves what we previously stated: that the dog is pure in itself, its meat is impure, and the impurity of its leftover water is due to the impurity of its meat. But there remains here a statement: their saying 'between the hide and the meat there is a thin membrane that prevents' based on the view that the operative term in the predicate is the subject or the subject and the predicate is his statement: 'It is not hidden what is in this answer' etc. I say: it is possible to refer what was mentioned in al-Inayah to what was said in Sharh al-Wiqayah, that the cause is prohibition along with mixing of blood, and that is apparent with minimal reflection. For after mentioning the sharing of edible and others in the impurity adjacent to blood, it mentioned the uniqueness of the non-edible in prohibition, so in the non-edible both factors combine unlike the edible. So it was
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute and internal Hanafi refinement regarding the ruling on the leftover water (su'r) of predatory land animals (siba' al-baha'im). The passage is a critical refinement within a larger expansion of the ruling.

The author begins by stating the Shafi'i position: the su'r of predatory animals is pure (tahir). The Shafi'i school adduces several proofs: (1) A hadith narrated by al-Bayhaqi and al-Daraqutni from Jabir where the Prophet permits using the leftover water of donkeys and all predatory beasts. (2) An athar (report) from al-Muwatta showing that 'Umar ibn al-Khattab did not consider the visitation of predatory beasts to a watering hole as problematic. (3) A hadith from Ibn Majah where the Prophet tells the owner of a water trough not to reveal that beasts drank from it, implying the water remains pure.

The Hanafi position follows: the su'r of predatory land animals is impure (najis). The Hanafi proof is based on the principle that the prohibition of eating something that is otherwise suitable for food indicates its impurity. The Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited eating every fanged predator; since the meat is suitable for food and not naturally disgusting, the prohibition must be due to the impurity of the meat. The baseness (khubth) of their nature does not contradict this; rather, it supports the ruling. The Hanafi school also notes that there is no necessity (darurah) or general affliction (umum balwa) that would necessitate a dispensation, except for the cat and mouse which are excluded due to common household presence. Predatory birds are excluded because they drink with their beaks (not their tongues contacting the water). The mule and donkey are also excluded because their evidences do not conflict with the general ruling.

The text then critically evaluates the Shafi'i proofs. The hadith of Jabir is declared weak (da'if) by al-Nawawi. The athar from al-Muwatta, though authenticated by al-Bayhaqi, is weakened by Ibn Ma'in and al-Daraqutni and is mursal (discontinuous chain). The hadith of Ibn Majah is weakened by Ibn 'Adi. Even if these reports were authentic, they are interpreted as referring to a large quantity of water (reaching two qullas), or to the period before the prohibition of eating predator meat, or to wild animals and predatory birds. The hadith of two qullas is used as an alternative framework: the Prophet's answer indicates that water less than two qullas becomes impure if contacted by predatory beasts, even without change.

The passage then transitions to an internal Hanafi discussion (intra-madhhab) introduced by al-Zayla'i (the Zayla'i quote appears on page 227 but continues into page 228). Al-Zayla'i identifies an apparent inconsistency: Hanafis say su'r of non-edible meat animals is impure because it is generated from impure meat, yet they also say that if such an animal is slaughtered (dhabh), its meat becomes pure. If the meat is pure after slaughter, why is the su'r still impure? If the impurity is inherent (najis al-'ayn), slaughter cannot purify, as with pigs. If impurity is due to blood, then edible animals also have blood adjacent to their meat.

This inconsistency is resolved in subsequent commentary. The resolution from 'Inayah and Sharh al-Wiqayah distinguishes between two factors: (1) the prohibition (hurmah) of the meat and (2) the mixing of blood (ikhtilat al-dam). Impurity arises only when both factors combine. In a living predatory animal, the meat is prohibited (due to the hadith prohibiting fanged predators) and blood is present, so the meat is impure, and thus the saliva (and su'r) is impure. In a slaughtered predatory animal, the blood is removed, so only prohibition remains; since prohibition alone does not cause impurity, the meat is pure, but the saliva generated from the meat before slaughter? Actually the text specifies that after dhabh, the meat of a non-edible animal is pure, but its leftover water from before dhabh remains impure? The discussion seems to focus on the state of the animal: alive, its su'r is impure; after dhabh, the meat becomes pure but the ruling on su'r might change? The resolution from Sharh al-Wiqayah states: for a non-edible animal, when alive, its saliva is generated from prohibited meat mixed with blood, so it is impure due to both factors. For edible meat (like sheep), only blood mixing exists, so its su'r is pure (with dislike? Actually the Hanafi position is that su'r of edible animals is pure except for some like horses? The text says pure without dislike). The same logic applies to dead animals: if they die naturally, both factors exist, so impure; if slaughtered, both factors are absent (for edible) or only prohibition remains (for non-edible), so pure.

The passage concludes by emphasizing that the impurity of the su'r of a dog (as an example of non-edible animals) is due to the impurity of its meat, and that the dog's body (ayn) is pure (tahir al-'ayn) by agreement of the Hanafi school, even though its meat is impure. This clarifies that purity of the animal itself does not entail purity of its meat.

The final lines contain a marginal note or continuation that attempts to reconcile the views of 'Inayah and Sharh al-Wiqayah, but the text cuts off mid-sentence.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): The leftover water remaining in a vessel after an animal has drunk from it.
سباع البهائم (siba' al-baha'im): Predatory land animals that hunt with fangs (lions, wolves, tigers, etc.).
القلتين (al-qullatayn): A large volume of water (approximately 160-200 liters) that is not rendered impure by mere contact unless it changes.
نجاسة (najasah): Ritual impurity that prevents valid prayer without removal.
حرمة (hurmah): Prohibition (of consumption).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the leftover water of a wolf that drank from a small bucket (less than two qullas)?
A) Pure, because wolves are not explicitly mentioned in the hadith.
B) Impure, because the wolf is a fanged predator and the water is less than two qullas.
C) Pure, because the water did not change in color, taste, or smell.
D) Impure, but only if the water changed.

Key Takeaway
The leftover water of predatory land animals is impure in the Hanafi school due to the prohibition of eating their meat and the hadith of two qullas.

Taharah — Purification

15 min
The Internal Hanafi Refinement: Cause of Impurity in Su'r
Intra-Hanafi refinement on cause of impurity in su'r

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi resolution of the apparent inconsistency regarding the impurity of su'r and identify the combination of prohibition and blood mixing as the cause.

Core Idea
Impurity of su'r requires both prohibition (hurmah) and mixing of blood (ikhtilat al-dam).

This lesson delves into an intra-Hanafi discussion on the precise cause of impurity in the leftover water of non-edible animals. Al-Zayla'i identifies an apparent inconsistency: if the meat becomes pure after slaughter, why is the su'r impure? The resolution from Sharh al-Wiqayah clarifies that impurity results from the combination of prohibition and blood mixing, not from either alone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent inconsistency
Al-Zayla'i notes that Hanafis say su'r of non-edible animals is impure because it is generated from impure meat, yet they also say the meat becomes pure after slaughter. If the cause were inherent impurity, slaughter would not purify; if due to blood, edible animals also have blood.
The inconsistency is between the purity of meat after slaughter and the impurity of su'r.
2
Understand the proposed solutions
Some said only the hide is purified; the correct position is that there is a thin membrane between hide and meat. Al-Inayah suggests that the meat intended is what is permissible after slaughter versus what is not.
These are interim solutions before the final resolution.
3
State the final resolution from Sharh al-Wiqayah
Impurity requires two factors: prohibition (hurmah) and mixing of blood (ikhtilat al-dam). In a living non-edible animal, both exist, so its meat and saliva are impure. In a slaughtered non-edible animal, blood is removed, so only prohibition remains, which alone does not cause impurity in the meat. For edible animals, only blood mixing exists, so their su'r is pure.
Thus the su'r before slaughter is impure, but after slaughter the meat becomes pure, resolving the inconsistency.
4
Apply the resolution to different states
Life and death: In a living non-edible animal, both factors present → su'r impure. In a dead non-edible animal, both present → impure. In a slaughtered edible animal, both absent → pure. In a slaughtered non-edible, only prohibition remains → meat pure but su'r? Actually the su'r in question is from the living animal, so impure.
The discussion focuses on the cause of impurity in the su'r of the living animal.
5
Note the broader principle
The dog's body (ayn) is pure by Ijma, but its meat is impure due to prohibition and blood. This shows that purity of the animal itself does not entail purity of its meat.

في الحي. وإذا لم يكن حياً، فإن لم يكن مذكى كان نجساً، سواء كان مأكول اللحم أو غيره، لأنه صار حراماً بالموت، فالحرمة موجودة مع اختلاط الدم فيكون نجساً، فإذا كان مذكى كان طاهراً؛ أما في مأكول اللحم فلأنه لم توجد الحرمة ولا اختلاط الدم، وأما في غير مأكول اللحم فلأنه لم يوجد الاختلاط والحرمة المجردة غير كافية في النجاسة على ما مر أنها تثبت باجتماع الأمرين أهـ. فحاصله أن نجاسة اللحم لحرمته مع هذا كله إن طهارة العين لا تستلزم طهارة اللحم لأن السباع طاهرة العين باتفاق اصحابنا كما نقله عضيم مع أن لحمها نجس فثبت بهذا ما قدمناه من أن الكلب طاهر العين ولحمه نجس ونجاسة سؤره لنجاسة لحمه . لكن بقي ههنا كلام وهو أن قولهم بين الجلد واللحم جلدة رقيقة تمنع على القول بأن العامل في الخبر هو الابتداء أو الابتداء والمبتدأ قوله : ولا يخفى ما في هذا الجواب الخ) أقول : يمكن إرجاع ما ذكره في العناية إلى ما الأمران بخلاف المأكول، فكانت
As for the leftover water of predatory beasts, al-Shafi'i said it is pure, using as proof what al-Bayhaqi and al-Daraqutni narrated from Jabir: it was said, 'O Messenger of Allah, do we perform wudu with what the donkeys leave?' He said: 'Yes, and with what all predatory beasts leave.' And what Malik narrated in al-Muwatta that Umar ibn al-Khattab went out in a group including Amr ibn al-As until they reached a watering hole. Amr ibn al-As said: 'O owner of the watering hole, do predatory beasts come to your watering hole?' Umar ibn al-Khattab said: 'O owner of the watering hole, do not tell him; for we go to the predatory beasts and they come to us.' And what Ibn Majah narrated from Ibn Umar: the Messenger of Allah went out on one of his journeys, traveling by night, and they passed by a man at his water trough. Umar said: 'O owner of the trough, did the predatory beasts drink from your trough tonight?' He (peace be upon him) said: 'O owner of the trough, do not tell him; they have what they carried in their bellies, and we have what remains as drink and pure.' Our evidence: it is prohibited to eat every fanged predator, and the apparent from the prohibition, while it is suitable for food and not naturally disgusting, is that it indicates impurity. The baseness of their nature does not contradict this; rather, that is suitable as a motivating factor for the ruling of impurity. So let it be the motivator for it, in conjunction with it, by ordering based on the description suitable for being a cause, as required. And because there is no necessity and general affliction, so the cat and mouse are excluded. And because its tongue contacts the water, so predatory birds are excluded because they drink with their beaks, as will come. And their evidences do not contradict, so the mule and donkey are excluded. As for the hadith of Jabir, al-Nawawi acknowledged its weakness. As for the athar of al-Muwatta, even if al-Bayhaqi authenticated it and mentioned it is mursal, using it as evidence against Abu Hanifa, Ibn Ma'in and al-Daraqutni weakened it. As for the hadith of Ibn Majah, Ibn Adi weakened it. And assuming authenticity, it is interpreted as referring to a large quantity of water, or before the prohibition of eating predator meat, or to wild animals and predatory birds, based on their proof from the hadith of two qullas: he (peace be upon him) said: 'When water reaches two qullas, it does not carry impurity' in answer to his question about water in the desert and what predatory beasts visit it, giving a ruling for this water that predatory beasts visit and others. For the answer must match or increase, so what is asked about and others are included. And he ruled by the implication of its condition: what is less than two qullas is impure even if unchanged. The reality of its conditional implication is that if it does not reach that amount, it becomes impure from the visitation of predatory beasts. This is among the compelling proofs against him. [Then] al-Zayla'i said: Know that there is an inconsistency in the school of our companions regarding the leftover water of what is not eaten from predatory beasts: they say it is generated from impure meat, then they say if it is slaughtered, its meat becomes pure because its impurity is due to blood moisture, and it is removed by slaughter. If they mean by their statement 'impure in itself', it must not be purified by slaughter like the pig. And if they mean by it due to the adjacency of blood, then the edible meat also has blood adjacent to it. So where does the difference come between them in the leftover water, if each of them is purified by slaughter and becomes impure by dying naturally, and there is no difference between them except in the slaughtered one regarding eating? Prohibition does not necessitate impurity. How many pure things are not permissible to eat? Hence some said: only its hide is purified by slaughter because the prohibition of its meat is not due to its honorableness but it is a sign of its impurity. However, between the hide and the meat there is a thin membrane that prevents the hide from being impurified by the meat, and this is correct because there is no basis for the impurity of the leftover water except by this path. And it was mentioned in al-Inayah the essence of this inconsistency, and it mentioned that it is a point worth noting, then it said: The solution is that what is meant by the pure meat from which saliva is generated is what is permissible to eat after slaughter, and by impure meat is the opposite. This is because they both share in the impurity adjacent to spilled blood before slaughter: the sheep is not eaten if it dies naturally, and they both share in purity after it due to the removal of the impurity, which is blood. So there is no difference between them except that the sheep is eaten after slaughter while the dog is not. There is also no difference externally except the mixture of saliva generated from the meat. So it is known from this that the saliva generated from edible meat after slaughter is pure without dislike, unlike others, attributing the ruling to the distinguishing factor to protect the Sharia ruling from apparent contradiction. This is what occurred to me. It is not hidden that this answer has [issues], for al-Zayla'i's statement 'Prohibition does not necessitate impurity' refutes it. Rather, the correct answer is what is in Sharh al-Wiqayah: that if the prohibition is not due to honorability, it is a sign of impurity. But there is a doubt: impurity is due to the mixing of blood with meat, for if not for that, but rather its impurity in itself, it would be impure in essence, and it is not so. So the meat of a non-edible animal when alive, its saliva is generated from the prohibited meat mixed with blood, so it is impure due to the combination of two factors. As for edible meat, only one factor exists, which is the mixing with blood, so it does not necessitate the impurity of the leftover water because this cause alone is weak, since blood settled in its place does not give it the ruling of impurity in the living animal. And if it is not alive, if it is not slaughtered, it is impure, whether the meat is edible or not, because it becomes prohibited by death. So the prohibition exists with the mixing of blood, so it is impure. If it is slaughtered, it is pure. As for edible meat, because neither prohibition nor mixing of blood exists. As for non-edible meat, because the mixing does not exist and mere prohibition is not sufficient for impurity, as it was established that it is proven by the combination of the two factors. The gist is that the impurity of meat is due to its prohibition along with mixing of spilled blood. The second factor is absent in the slaughtered predatory beast, so it is pure, and both combine in states of death and life, so it is impure. The first factor is absent in the sheep in the state of life and slaughter, so it is pure, and both combine in the state of death, so it is impure. So it is clear from all this that the purity of the animal itself does not necessitate the purity of its meat, because predatory beasts are pure in themselves by agreement of our companions, as transmitted by 'Adhim, while their meat is impure. So this proves what we previously stated: that the dog is pure in itself, its meat is impure, and the impurity of its leftover water is due to the impurity of its meat. But there remains here a statement: their saying 'between the hide and the meat there is a thin membrane that prevents' based on the view that the operative term in the predicate is the subject or the subject and the predicate is his statement: 'It is not hidden what is in this answer' etc. I say: it is possible to refer what was mentioned in al-Inayah to what was said in Sharh al-Wiqayah, that the cause is prohibition along with mixing of blood, and that is apparent with minimal reflection. For after mentioning the sharing of edible and others in the impurity adjacent to blood, it mentioned the uniqueness of the non-edible in prohibition, so in the non-edible both factors combine unlike the edible. So it was
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute and internal Hanafi refinement regarding the ruling on the leftover water (su'r) of predatory land animals (siba' al-baha'im). The passage is a critical refinement within a larger expansion of the ruling.

The author begins by stating the Shafi'i position: the su'r of predatory animals is pure (tahir). The Shafi'i school adduces several proofs: (1) A hadith narrated by al-Bayhaqi and al-Daraqutni from Jabir where the Prophet permits using the leftover water of donkeys and all predatory beasts. (2) An athar (report) from al-Muwatta showing that 'Umar ibn al-Khattab did not consider the visitation of predatory beasts to a watering hole as problematic. (3) A hadith from Ibn Majah where the Prophet tells the owner of a water trough not to reveal that beasts drank from it, implying the water remains pure.

The Hanafi position follows: the su'r of predatory land animals is impure (najis). The Hanafi proof is based on the principle that the prohibition of eating something that is otherwise suitable for food indicates its impurity. The Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited eating every fanged predator; since the meat is suitable for food and not naturally disgusting, the prohibition must be due to the impurity of the meat. The baseness (khubth) of their nature does not contradict this; rather, it supports the ruling. The Hanafi school also notes that there is no necessity (darurah) or general affliction (umum balwa) that would necessitate a dispensation, except for the cat and mouse which are excluded due to common household presence. Predatory birds are excluded because they drink with their beaks (not their tongues contacting the water). The mule and donkey are also excluded because their evidences do not conflict with the general ruling.

The text then critically evaluates the Shafi'i proofs. The hadith of Jabir is declared weak (da'if) by al-Nawawi. The athar from al-Muwatta, though authenticated by al-Bayhaqi, is weakened by Ibn Ma'in and al-Daraqutni and is mursal (discontinuous chain). The hadith of Ibn Majah is weakened by Ibn 'Adi. Even if these reports were authentic, they are interpreted as referring to a large quantity of water (reaching two qullas), or to the period before the prohibition of eating predator meat, or to wild animals and predatory birds. The hadith of two qullas is used as an alternative framework: the Prophet's answer indicates that water less than two qullas becomes impure if contacted by predatory beasts, even without change.

The passage then transitions to an internal Hanafi discussion (intra-madhhab) introduced by al-Zayla'i (the Zayla'i quote appears on page 227 but continues into page 228). Al-Zayla'i identifies an apparent inconsistency: Hanafis say su'r of non-edible meat animals is impure because it is generated from impure meat, yet they also say that if such an animal is slaughtered (dhabh), its meat becomes pure. If the meat is pure after slaughter, why is the su'r still impure? If the impurity is inherent (najis al-'ayn), slaughter cannot purify, as with pigs. If impurity is due to blood, then edible animals also have blood adjacent to their meat.

This inconsistency is resolved in subsequent commentary. The resolution from 'Inayah and Sharh al-Wiqayah distinguishes between two factors: (1) the prohibition (hurmah) of the meat and (2) the mixing of blood (ikhtilat al-dam). Impurity arises only when both factors combine. In a living predatory animal, the meat is prohibited (due to the hadith prohibiting fanged predators) and blood is present, so the meat is impure, and thus the saliva (and su'r) is impure. In a slaughtered predatory animal, the blood is removed, so only prohibition remains; since prohibition alone does not cause impurity, the meat is pure, but the saliva generated from the meat before slaughter? Actually the text specifies that after dhabh, the meat of a non-edible animal is pure, but its leftover water from before dhabh remains impure? The discussion seems to focus on the state of the animal: alive, its su'r is impure; after dhabh, the meat becomes pure but the ruling on su'r might change? The resolution from Sharh al-Wiqayah states: for a non-edible animal, when alive, its saliva is generated from prohibited meat mixed with blood, so it is impure due to both factors. For edible meat (like sheep), only blood mixing exists, so its su'r is pure (with dislike? Actually the Hanafi position is that su'r of edible animals is pure except for some like horses? The text says pure without dislike). The same logic applies to dead animals: if they die naturally, both factors exist, so impure; if slaughtered, both factors are absent (for edible) or only prohibition remains (for non-edible), so pure.

The passage concludes by emphasizing that the impurity of the su'r of a dog (as an example of non-edible animals) is due to the impurity of its meat, and that the dog's body (ayn) is pure (tahir al-'ayn) by agreement of the Hanafi school, even though its meat is impure. This clarifies that purity of the animal itself does not entail purity of its meat.

The final lines contain a marginal note or continuation that attempts to reconcile the views of 'Inayah and Sharh al-Wiqayah, but the text cuts off mid-sentence.

Key Terms
نجاسة (najasah): Ritual impurity; in this lesson, the cause is the combination of hurmah and ikhtilat al-dam.
حرمة (hurmah): Prohibition (of consumption).
اختلاط الدم (ikhtilat al-dam): Mixing of blood with the meat.
ذكاة (dhabh): Ritual slaughter that removes blood.
عين (ayn): The physical substance/body of the animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the final resolution in Sharh al-Wiqayah, why is the su'r of a dog impure but the dog itself is not impure?
A) The dog's body is impure, and the su'r is also impure.
B) The dog's meat is prohibited and mixed with blood, making the su'r impure; the body remains pure.
C) The dog's saliva is impure because of fangs.
D) The dog is pure but its su'r is impure because of its fur.

Key Takeaway
The impurity of su'r from non-edible animals is due to the combination of prohibition and blood mixing, not any single factor.

Cat Saliva: Pure but Disliked? The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Karahah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the karahah of cat saliva after agreed purity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cat saliva, distinguish between karahah tahrimi and karahah tanzihi as applied in this case, and explain the role of the 'illa of tawwaf in the purity ruling.

Core Idea
Cat saliva is pure but disliked; the 'illa of tawwaf removes impurity, but karahah remains based on assumption.

In this lesson, we delve into an intra-Hanafi debate: all authorities agree that cat saliva is pure due to the cat's frequent coming and going (tawwaf) and the resulting hardship. However, they differ on whether any dislike (karahah) attaches to its use. We will examine the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Imam Muhammad, and al-Tahawi, focusing on the distinction between prohibitive dislike (karahah tahrim) and recommended dislike (karahah tanzih), and see how the hadith 'al-sinnawr sabu'' and qiyas with the sleeping person’s hand inform the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed-upon foundation
Recognize that all Hanafi authorities agree cat saliva is pure (tahir) based on the hadith of tawwaf, which necessitates removal of impurity due to hardship.
2
Locate the point of dispute
Determine whether any karahah remains after impurity is removed, and identify the level of karahah (tahrimi vs tanzihi) as argued by different scholars.
Al-Tahawi holds karahah tahrim; the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and one view of Muhammad) hold karahah tanzih; Muhammad also says no karahah with certainty.
3
Analyze the proofs
Examine the hadith 'al-sinnawr sabu'' — interpreted to indicate a ruling (hukm) not literal reality — and the qiyas with the sleeping person’s hand; see how these support karahah tanzih.
The hadith alone is ambiguous; the qiyas provides a sound original principle.
4
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi responses
Understand the objections to karahah tahrim (requires explicit evidence), the view of no karahah under certainty (Imam Muhammad), and the relied-upon position (al-ashah) of karahah tanzih.
The mufta bihi: pure but makruh tanzihan; if certain of cleanliness, no karahah.

And for them (the two - Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that there is no dispute in the removal of impurity established by the hadith due to the stated cause of frequent coming and going (tawwaf), meaning that it enters narrow places and its necessary consequence is intense mixing such that protecting vessels from it is difficult, rather protecting oneself is difficult, so due to the necessary need, impurity was removed. The discussion after this is only regarding the establishment of karahah (dislike). So if the karahah is karahah tahrim (prohibitive dislike) as al-Tahawi said, then the argument does not proceed, for if one says: impurity was removed so prohibitive dislike remains, the implication is prevented because the removal of a description or a legal ruling does not necessitate the establishment of another except with evidence. The conclusion is that establishing every legal ruling requires evidence, so establishing prohibitive dislike in this state is without evidence. And if it is karahah tanzih (recommended dislike) according to the most correct view, then it is sufficient that it does not avoid impurity, so it is disliked, like water in which a young child dipped his hand; its origin is the dislike of dipping the hand into a vessel for one who wakes up before washing them, prohibited in the hadith of the one who wakes up due to the assumption of impurity. Adhering to it according to what the author mentioned in al-Mustasfa, that he, peace be upon him, did not intend the literal meaning because he was not sent to explain realities, so what is intended is the ruling, and the ruling is types: impurity of the leftover, its dislike, and prohibition of its flesh. Then it is not free from either being attached to it (the hadith) in respect of all rulings, which is impossible because it would entail a statement of impurity of the leftover along with its dislike, and that is not allowed; or in respect of prohibition of flesh, and that is not allowed because it is established by the Prophet's prohibition of eating every predatory animal with fangs; or in respect of dislike of the leftover, which is the intended meaning; or in respect of its impurity, and that is also not allowed since impurity is negated by consensus, or by the hadith, or by necessity, so dislike remains; or in the first with the second, or the first with the third, or the second with the third, and that is not allowed for the reasons mentioned. His statement: 'or in the first with the second' is coordinate with his statement 'in respect of all rulings'. Or we say: from the beginning, it is not allowed that prohibition of flesh be intended from this hadith because it would involve making the speech of the Messenger, peace be upon him, serve repetition rather than original benefit, regardless of whether this hadith is earlier or later. Reflect and you will know.' Therefore, by this, the dislike of its leftover is established, and Abu Qatadah's act of tilting the vessel is interpreted as removing that assumption, as it was in his sight in a time when it was possible to wash its mouth from its saliva. As for according to Muhammad's opinion, it is possible that it was by observing it drinking from a lot of water or observing its return from an absence, which would allow that, but this allowance is contradicted by its having eaten something impure shortly before drinking, so it falls, and thus purity remains without karahah because (the karahah) only came from the allowance and it has fallen.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling of cat saliva. The author first establishes that under the Hanafi school, cat saliva is considered pure (tahir) based on the hadith that mentions the cat's frequent coming and going (tawwaf), which necessitates removal of impurity due to hardship. The discussion then focuses on whether any karahah (dislike) remains. Al-Tahawi held that the karahah is tahrimi (prohibitive dislike), but the author rejects this because removing impurity does not automatically establish a separate ruling without evidence. The relied-upon view (al-ashah) is that the karahah is tanzihi (recommended dislike), analogous to the dislike of a person waking up dipping his hand into water before washing due to the possibility of impurity. The text then analyzes the hadith 'The cat is a predatory animal' (al-sinnawr sabu'), explaining that it is not literal but meant to indicate a ruling, such as dislike of its leftover. The author rejects that it implies prohibition of its flesh because that is already established by other proofs. The passage concludes with a reference to Imam Muhammad's opinion: if it is certain that the cat's mouth is clean (e.g., observed drinking clean water or coming from absence), then no karahah remains because the basis for karahah (the assumption of impurity) is removed. This highlights the Hanafi principle that practical necessity (illah al-tawwaf) overrides impurity, but karahah is based on assumption (tawahhum), which can be negated by certainty.

Key Terms
الطواف (al-tawwaf): Frequent coming and going, as a characteristic of domestic cats that necessitates close contact with humans and their vessels.
السؤر (al-su'r): The leftover water or liquid after an animal drinks from a vessel.
الكراهة (al-karahah): Dislike; in this passage, discussed as either tahrimi (prohibitive) or tanzihi (recommended).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Tahir (pure) and mustahabb (recommended) to use
D) Tahir (pure) without any karahah

Key Takeaway
Cat saliva is pure due to the 'illa of tawwaf, but the majority view adds a recommended dislike (karahah tanzih), which falls away with certainty of cleanliness.

Wild Cat's Leftover Water (Su'r) is Najis Due to Absence of 'Illa
Establishes that wild cat's su'r is najis because the 'illa of tawaf is absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on wild cat's su'r and explain the role of the 'illa (effective cause) in determining purity under the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The absence of the 'illa of roaming (tawaf) makes the wild cat's leftover water impure.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains a key Hanafi principle: a ruling returns to its original state when the alleviating cause is absent. Here, the original state of any animal's su'r is impurity, but domestic cats have an exception due to their roaming. For wild cats, the exception does not apply. Let's explore how this reasoning works through a structured analysis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its original ruling
The act under discussion is the su'r (leftover water) of a cat. The Hanafi school's original ruling for any animal's su'r is that it is najis unless proven otherwise.
This original ruling is based on general principles of impurity from animal saliva.
2
Recognize the exceptional 'illa
Domestic cats' su'r is considered pure due to the 'illa of tawaf (their habit of roaming in homes). This exception is established by textual evidence (hadith).
The 'illa is what removes the original impurity.
3
Apply the absence of 'illa
Since wild cats do not roam in human dwellings, the 'illa of tawaf is absent. Therefore, the original ruling of najasah applies to their su'r.
The ruling is contingent on the existence of the 'illa.
4
Understand the usul principle
The author cites a usul principle: when a ruling is tied to a specific 'illa, the ruling stands only as long as the 'illa exists. This is illustrated by the analogy of saying 'uff' to parents—the prohibition is removed when the child does not mean disrespect.
This principle is from Kashf al-Asrar in the discussion of textual implication.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school disagrees, holding that all cats' su'r is pure, regardless of domestication. Their basis is the general hadith without restricting it via 'illa.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different usul approaches.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن قولهم إن الأصل في سؤر الهرة أن يكون نجساً وإنما سقطت النجاسة بعلة الطواف يفيد أن سؤر الهرة الوحشية نجس وإن كان النص بخلافه لعدم العلة وهي الطواف لأن العلة إذا كانت ثابتة بالنص وعرف قطعاً أن الحكم متعلق بها فالحكم يدور على وجودها لا غير كعدم حرمه التأفيف للوالدين إذا لم يعلم الولد معناه، أو استعمله بجهة الإكرام ذكره في كشف الأسرار في بحث دلالة النص.
Know that their statement that the original ruling regarding cat's leftover water is that it is najis, and that the najasah was only removed by the 'illa of tawaf (roaming), indicates that the leftover water of a wild cat is najis, even though the text [regarding domestic cat] is contrary, because the 'illa [of tawaf] is absent. For when the 'illa is established by the text and it is known with certainty that the ruling is attached to it, then the ruling revolves around its existence, not otherwise. Like the absence of the prohibition of [saying] 'uff to parents when the child does not know its meaning or uses it in a respectful manner. It was mentioned in Kashf al-Asrar in the discussion of textual implication.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, establishing the fiqh principle that the original ruling (najasah) returns when the alleviating cause ('illa) is absent. The author states that the su'r (leftover water) of a domestic cat is considered pure due to the 'illa of tawaf (the cat roaming freely). However, for a wild cat that does not roam in human dwellings, this 'illa is absent, so the original ruling of najasah applies. The proof is a usul principle: when a ruling is attached to a specific 'illa by textual evidence, the ruling is conditional upon that 'illa. The author analogizes to the case of saying 'uff to parents: the prohibition is removed if the child does not mean disrespect or uses it respectfully. This principle is from Kashf al-Asrar. The Hanafi position is that wild cat's su'r is najis, which is a ruling derived from the principle, not from an explicit text. This is a fatwa from later scholars (fatawa mutakhkhirin).

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): The leftover water that an animal has drunk from, or any liquid that remains after an animal has drunk or licked.
علة ('illa): The effective cause or attribute that necessitates a legal ruling.
طواف (tawaf): Literally 'roaming'; here it refers to the habit of domestic cats roaming in houses, which is the 'illa for declaring their su'r pure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is pure (tahir)
B) It is impure (najis)
C) It is makruh
D) It is permissible (mubah)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that wild cat su'r is najis because the exceptional 'illa of tawaf is absent, and the original ruling of impurity applies.

Su'r of Jallalah Animals and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Confinement
Intra-Hanafi dispute on interpretation of mahbusah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the su'r of jallalah animals and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over the condition of confinement (mahbusah).

Core Idea
The su'r of a jallalah chicken is makruh unless its beak is guaranteed clean, but what counts as confinement is debated.

In this lesson, we explore the legal ruling on the leftover water (su'r) of animals that habitually eat impurities, such as chickens, cows, and camels. The Hanafi school considers their su'r makruh due to probable contamination, but provides an exception when the animal is 'mahbusah' (confined). The exact meaning of this confinement is disputed within the school, and this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents two interpretations, ultimately favouring the stricter view that the animal must be prevented from all contact with filth, including its own dung.

Guided Path
1
State the default ruling
What is the Hanafi ruling on the su'r of unrestricted chickens and jallalah animals? The text states it is makruh because the beak is not free from impurities.
2
Identify the exception
When does the su'r become pure? When the animal is 'mahbusah' (confined). But what does this confinement entail?
3
Track the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Two interpretations: (1) Sheikh al-Islam: confined in a closed house with no access to any dung. (2) Hakim Abd al-Rahman: even in a closed house, if the animal roams in its own dung, it is not enough; it must be confined for fattening with its head outside to prevent access to its own dung.
4
Identify the tarjih
Which view is preferred? The author of al-Hidayah chose the second view, and it is the mufta bihi (operative ruling).
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: If a chicken is kept in a closed coop but roams in its own dung, su'r is makruh per the second view but pure per the first view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما سؤر الدجاجة المخلاة فلأنها تخالط النجاسة فمنقارها لا يخلو عن قذر، وكذا البقر الجلالة والإبل الجلالة إلا أن تكون محبوسة واختلفوا في تفسيرها فقيل هي التي تحبس في بيت ويغلق بابه وتعلف هناك لعدم النجاسة على منقارها لا من حيث الحقيقة ولا من حيث الاعتبار لأنها لا تجد عذرات غيرها حتى تجول فيها وهي في عذرات نفسها لا تجول، وإليه ذهب شيخ الإسلام في مبسوطه وحكي عن الإمام الحاكم عبد الرحمن أنه قال : لم يرد بكونها محبوسة أن تكون محبوسة في بيتها لأنها وإن كانت محبوسة تجول في عذارت نفسها فلا يؤمن من أن يكون على منقارها قذر فيكره كما لو كانت مخلاة، وإنما المراد أن تحبس في بيت لتسمن للأكل فيكون رأسها وعلفها وماؤها خارج البيت فلا يمكنها أن تجول في عذرات نفسها. كذا في معراج الدراية واختار الثاني صاحب الهداية وغيره، وفي فتح القدير: والحق أنها لا تأكله بل تلاحظ الحب بينه فتلقطه.
As for the leftover water of the unrestricted chicken (that roams freely), it is because it mixes with impurities, so its beak is not free from filth. Likewise, the cows (jallalah) and camels (jallalah) unless they are confined (mahbusah). They differed in its interpretation: some said it is the one that is confined in a house with its door closed and fed there, so there is no impurity on its beak neither in reality nor by consideration because it does not encounter others' dung and does not roam in its own dung. This view is held by Sheikh al-Islam in his Mabsut. It is narrated from Imam Hakim Abd al-Rahman that he said: By 'confined' it is not meant that it is confined in its house, because even if it is confined, it roams in its own dung, so it is not safe from having filth on its beak, thus it is makruh as if it were unrestricted. Rather the meaning is that it is confined in a house to be fattened for eating, so its head, fodder, and water are outside the house, so it cannot roam in its own dung. This is in Mi'raj al-Diraya, and the author of al-Hidaya and others chose the second opinion. In Fath al-Qadir: The truth is that it does not eat the dung, but rather it looks at the grain among it and pecks it.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of su'r for animals that eat impurities (jallalah), such as chickens, cows, and camels. The default ruling is that their su'r is makruh because their beaks or mouths are likely contaminated. However, an exception is made if they are 'mahbusah' (confined). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the interpretation of mahbusah. One view (Sheikh al-Islam) holds that it means the animal is confined in a closed house and fed there, so it never contacts outside impurities. Another view (Hakim Abd al-Rahman) argues that even if confined in a house, the animal roams in its own dung, so only if the animal is confined for fattening with its head outside the enclosure such that it cannot access its own dung does the su'r become pure. The author of al-Hidayah prefers the second view. A note from Fath al-Qadir clarifies that such animals do not actually eat dung but pick grains from among it. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that su'r of jallalah animals is makruh unless they are properly confined so that their beaks are clean.

Key Terms
الدجاجة المخلاة (al-dajajat al-mukhallah): A chicken that is left to roam freely and thus likely to come into contact with impurities.
الجلالة (al-jallalah): An animal that eats impurities (dung, filth) as part of its diet.
محبوسة (mahbusah): An animal that is confined in a way that its beak or mouth remains clean of impurities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, when does the leftover water (su'r) of a jallalah chicken become pure?
A) When it is confined in a closed house without access to outside dung
B) When it is confined for fattening with its head and fodder outside the enclosure
C) When it is left to roam but fed only grain
D) It is always pure regardless of confinement

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school deems the su'r of jallalah animals makruh unless they are confined in a manner that guarantees their beak is free from filth, with the preferred view requiring prevention of access to their own dung.

Su'r of Birds of Prey: Qiyas vs Istihsan
Intra-Hanafi dispute on su'r of birds of prey: qiyas vs istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the su'r of birds of prey, explain how istihsan overrides qiyas, and identify the mufta bihi view from Abu Yusuf's narration.

Core Idea
A bird of prey's saliva is not najis because its beak is dry bone, and istihsan overrides strict analogy.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines the ruling on the leftover water (su'r) of birds of prey. While qiyas would classify it as impure, the Hanafi school invokes istihsan to rule it merely makruh. The passage also introduces a nuance from Abu Yusuf that may even lift the kerahah entirely. Let's walk through the legal reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing methods
Recognize that qiyas (analogy) would make the su'r najis, while istihsan (juristic preference) leads to a milder ruling. The passage sets up this tension.
Qiyas here is based on the prohibition of eating the meat.
2
Understand the qiyas argument
Qiyas: since the meat of birds of prey is haram and therefore impure, their saliva (and thus su'r) should also be impure, analogous to beasts of prey.
The basis is that the prohibition of eating implies impurity of the flesh.
3
Understand the istihsan reasoning
Three reasons: (1) Birds drink with their beaks, which are dry bone, so no moist saliva contact; (2) They often eat carrion, resembling unrestricted chickens (whose su'r is makruh); (3) There is general necessity (balwa) as they swoop freely.
Istihsan overrides qiyas because of these concrete differences.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Abu Yusuf adds that the karahah is only due to possible filth on the beak, not due to the saliva. If the beak is known clean, the su'r is pure. The later scholars adopted this view as mufta bihi.
This softens the ruling further: from makruh to pure under certain conditions.
5
Determine the practical outcome
Apply the mufta bihi: For wudu, using su'r of a bird of prey is valid. It is makruh if the beak's cleanliness is unknown; it is pure if the beak is known clean.
This reflects the hybrid use of qiyas and istihsan in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما سؤر سباع الطير كالصقر والبازي فالقياس نجاسته لنجاسة لحمها لحرمة أكله كسباع البهائم، ووجه الاستحسان أن حرمة لحمها وإن اقتضت النجاسة لكنها تشرب بمنقارها وهو عظم جاف ظاهر لكنها تأكل الميتات والجيف غالباً فأشبه الدجاجة المخلاة فأورث الكراهة بخلاف سباع البهائم فإنها تشرب بلسانها وهو رطب بلعابها المتولد من لحمها وهو نجس فافترقا ولأن في سباع الطير ضرورة وبلوى فإنها تنقض من الهواء فتشرب ولا يمكن صون الأواني عنها خصوصاً في البراري وعن أبي يوسف أن الكراهة لتوهم النجاسة في منقارها لا لوصول لعابها إلى الماء حتى لو كانت محبوسة يعلم صاحبها أنه لا قذر في منقارها لا يكره التوضؤ بسؤرها واستحسن المشايخ المتأخرون هذه الرواية وأفتوا بها. كذا في النهاية. وفي التنجيس : يجوز أن يفتى بها.
As for the su'r of birds of prey such as the falcon and hawk, analogy (qiyas) dictates that it is impure because their meat is impure due to the prohibition of eating it, like beasts of prey. The basis of istihsan is that although the prohibition of their meat necessitates impurity, they drink with their beaks, which are dry bones, [so no saliva contact]. However, they often eat carrion and corpses, so they resemble the unrestricted chicken, thus [their su'r] is makruh. This is unlike beasts of prey, which drink with their tongues, which are moist with saliva generated from their flesh, which is impure, thus they differ. Also, for birds of prey there is necessity and general affliction, as they swoop from the air and drink, and it is impossible to protect vessels from them especially in wilderness. It is narrated from Abu Yusuf that the karahah is due to the possibility of impurity on their beaks, not due to their saliva reaching the water, so if they were confined and the owner knows there is no filth on their beak, then performing wudu with their su'r is not makruh. The later mashayikh considered this narration good and gave fatwa accordingly. This is in al-Nihaya. In al-Tanjis: it is permissible to give fatwa with it.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage discusses the su'r of birds of prey (like falcons and hawks). By qiyas (analogy) to beasts of prey, their su'r would be najis because their meat is haram to eat, implying impurity. However, the Hanafi school applies istihsan (juristic preference) to rule that it is only makruh, not najis. The reasons are: (1) they drink with their beaks, which are dry bone, not a wet tongue like beasts of prey; (2) they often eat carrion so they resemble the unrestricted chicken (whose su'r is makruh); (3) there is necessity because these birds are common and it is difficult to prevent them from drinking. The text also transmits a narration from Abu Yusuf that the karahah is only due to the possibility of filth on the beak, so if the bird is confined and its beak is known clean, the su'r is not even makruh. The later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) preferred this narration and gave fatwa accordingly. Thus the mufta bihi position is that the su'r of birds of prey is makruh, but it can become pure if the beak is known clean.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning that would make the su'r of birds of prey najis by analogy to beasts of prey.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that relaxes the analogy due to custom, necessity, or a stronger proof.
سباع الطير (siba' al-tayr): Birds of prey that hunt and eat meat, such as falcons and hawks.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, what is the ruling on the su'r of a falcon whose beak is known to be clean?
A) Najis
B) Makruh
C) Pure (tahir)
D) Haram to use

Key Takeaway
The su'r of birds of prey is makruh by istihsan, but if the beak is known clean, it is pure according to the mufta bihi view of Abu Yusuf.

Su'r of House-Dwelling Animals: Snakes, Mice, and the Cat Analogy
Ruling on su'r of domestic pests via qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the su'r of house-dwelling animals (snakes, mice) and explain the qiyas from the cat using the 'illa of tawaf.

Core Idea
The su'r of house-dwelling animals is makruh, not najis, by analogy to the cat due to the common 'illa of roaming.

You already know that the su'r of a cat is pure (tahir) but its use is makruh due to the possibility of impurity. But what about snakes and mice that live in our houses? Their meat is haram, which ordinarily would make their su'r najis. Yet the Hanafi school rules it only makruh. Why? Because they share the same 'illa as the cat: they roam around houses (tawaf). This lesson unpacks that qiyas and a related branch ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
What is the ruling for the su'r of snakes and mice according to the passage? State it clearly.
Hint: It's not najis, but something less severe.
2
Recognize the apparent contradiction
If the meat of these animals is haram, qiyas would normally make their su'r najis. Why is that not the case here?
3
Spot the 'illa (effective cause)
The passage mentions a 'illa that removes the impurity. What is that 'illa, and from which animal is it borrowed?
Look for the word 'tawaf' (roaming) and 'al-hurrah' (the cat).
4
Apply the qiyas
Explain step by step: the cat has the 'illa of tawaf; the snake and mouse also have tawaf; therefore the same ruling applies: impurity dropped, karahah remains.
This is a qiyas jaliy (explicit analogy).
5
Note the branch ruling
The passage cites al-Tawshih: prayer while carrying something whose su'r is makruh (like the cat) is itself makruh. Identify the reason.
Carrying an object with makruh su'r does not invalidate prayer but is discouraged.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما سؤر سواكن البيوت كالحية والفأرة فلأن حرمة اللحم أوجبت النجاسة لكنها سقطت النجاسة بعلة الطواف وبقيت الكراهة، والعلة المذكورة في الحديث في الهرة موجودة بعينها في سواكن البيوت وهي الطواف فيثبت ذلك الحكم المترتب عليها وهو سقوط النجاسة وتثبت الكراهة لتوهمها . فرع تكره الصلاة . حمل ما سؤره مكروه كالهرة كذا في التوشيح. نكنة : قيل: ست تورث النسيان: سؤر الفأرة وهي حية والبول في الماء الراكد وقطع القطار ومضغ العلك وأكل التفاح وإلقاء القملة ومنهم من ذكره حديثاً لكن قال أبو الفرج بن الجوزي : إنه حديث موضوع .
As for the su'r of domestic dwellers such as the snake and mouse, because the prohibition of [eating] their meat necessitated impurity, but the impurity is removed by the 'illa of tawaf (roaming), and the karahah remains. The 'illa mentioned in the hadith regarding the cat is exactly present in domestic dwellers, namely tawaf, so that ruling attached to it is established: the dropping of impurity and the establishment of karahah due to its possibility. Branch: prayer [while carrying something whose su'r is makruh] is makruh; carrying something whose su'r is makruh like the cat, as in al-Tawshih. A point: It is said that six things cause forgetfulness: the leftover water of mouse which is a snake? (?) and urinating in stagnant water, and cutting the qitar (a plant?), and chewing gum, and eating apples, and throwing away a louse. Some mentioned it as a hadith, but Abu al-Faraj ibn al-Jawzi said it is a fabricated hadith.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage covers two items: first, the su'r of animals that dwell in houses, like snakes and mice. Since their meat is haram, qiyas would make their su'r najis, but due to the 'illa of tawaf (they roam in houses like cats), the ruling follows that of the cat: the impurity is removed and only karahah remains because of the possibility of impurity on their mouths. The text also includes a branch ruling: performing prayer while carrying something whose su'r is makruh (like that of a cat) is itself makruh. Second, the author mentions a reported list of six things that cause forgetfulness, including the su'r of a mouse (or snake). He notes that Abu al-Faraj ibn al-Jawzi declared the hadith as fabricated. This is a separate note with no fiqh ruling.

Key Terms
سواكن البيوت (sawakina al-buyut): Animals that habitually live in human dwellings, such as snakes, mice, cats.
نكنة (nuktah): A point or remark, often an interesting or unusual piece of information.
التوشيح (al-tawshih): A Hanafi fiqh work, quoted as source for the branch ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because it is a domestic pest

Key Takeaway
The su'r of house-dwelling animals (snakes, mice) is makruh, not najis, by analogy to the cat due to the common 'illa of roaming.

Donkey and Mule Su'r: The Concept of Mashkuk
Intra-Hanafi dispute over the term 'mashkuk' for donkey/mule su'r

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi concept of 'mashkuk' as technical suspension (tawaqquf) and distinguish the positions of the majority and Abu Tahir al-Dabbas regarding donkey and mule su'r.

Core Idea
Mashkuk means suspension due to conflicting evidence, not ignorance; donkey su'r is pure but requires precautionary tayammum.

The leftover water (su'r) of domestic donkeys and mules has been debated among Hanafi scholars. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement: the majority term it 'mashkuk' (doubtful), while Abu Tahir al-Dabbas objects to calling any of Allah's rulings doubtful. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi method of dealing with conflicting evidence and the nuanced ruling on purity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Basis
Note that both the majority and Abu Tahir agree the su'r is pure (tahir). The dispute is over labeling it 'mashkuk' and the practical precaution. Identify the ruling: pure, but precaution requires tayammum when used for wudu.
The ruling is consistent; the difference is epistemological.
2
Understand the Majority's Use of 'Mashkuk'
The majority use 'shakk' to mean tawaqquf (suspension) due to conflicting evidence from hadiths, not ignorance of the ruling. They explain that the ruling itself is known: the water is pure and removes impurity, but tayammum is added out of piety.
This is a technical term in Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze Abu Tahir's Objection
Abu Tahir argues that nothing from Allah's rulings can be doubtful; if the ruling is known (pure), there is no room for doubt. He insists the su'r is definitely pure and permits its use, but adds precautionary tayammum when possible.
His objection is semantic but practical outcome is similar.
4
Resolve the Disagreement via Majority Response
The majority respond that 'shakk' is technical suspension, not ignorance. They cite conflicting hadiths on eating donkey meat—some forbid (implying impurity), others allow (implying purity). This conflict warrants tawaqquf.
The conflict is the basis for the term 'mashkuk'.
5
Apply the Precautionary Ruling
The mufta bihi: su'r is pure, but if one uses it for wudu, tayammum should also be performed (if possible) as a precaution (ihtiyat). If no other water, wudu with su'r alone is valid but makruh.
This applies when water from donkeys/mules is the only available water.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (والحمار والبغل مشكوك أي سؤرهما مشكوك فيه هذه عبارة أكثر مشايخنا، وأبو طاهر الدباس أنكر أن يكون شيء من أحكام الله تعالى مشكوكاً فيه. وقال: سؤر الحمار طاهر لو غمس فيه الثوب جازت الصلاة معه إلا أنه محتاط فيه فأمر بالجمع بينه وبين التيمم ومنع منه حالة القدرة والمشايخ قالوا : المراد بالشك التوقف لتعارض الأدلة لا أن يعني بكونه مشكوكاً الجهل بحكم الشرع لأن حكمه معلوم وهو وجوب الاستعمال وانتفاء النجاسة وضم التيمم إليه والقول بالتوقف عند تعارض الأدلة دليل العلم وغاية الورع وبيان التعارض على ما في المبسوط تعارض الأخبار في أكل لحمه فإنه روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام نهى عن أكل لحوم الحمر الأهلية يوم خيبر . وروى غالب بن أبجر قال : لم يبق لي تأويل الواجب الثابت .اهـ. ونحوه في منح الغفار قوله : (تكره الصلاة مع حمل ما سؤره مكروه الخ) وقد تقدم قبل صفحة أن الكراهة إنما هي عند التوهم فراجعه لكن يمكن الفرق بين سؤرها
His statement: 'And the donkey and mule are mashkuk (doubtful)', i.e., their leftover water is doubtful. This is the expression of most of our mashayikh. Abu Tahir al-Dabbas denied that anything from Allah's rulings can be doubtful. He said: The su'r of the donkey is pure (tahir); if a garment is dipped in it, prayer is valid with it, except that precaution is taken, so he ordered combining it with tayammum and prohibited [using it alone] when [other water] is available. The mashayikh said: What is meant by 'shakk' is suspension (tawaqquf) due to conflicting evidences, not that it means ignorance of the legal ruling, because its ruling is known: it is obligatory to use it, and purification from impurity is achieved, but tayammum is added to it. And the statement of suspension when evidences conflict is a sign of knowledge and ultimate piety. The explanation of conflict as in al-Mabsut: conflicting reports regarding eating its meat: it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade eating the meat of domestic donkeys on the day of Khaybar. And Ghalib ibn Abjar narrated: 'I have nothing left...' The interpretation of the established obligation. End. And similar in Minah al-Ghaffar: His statement: 'It is makruh to pray while carrying something whose su'r is makruh etc.' And it has preceded earlier that the karahah is only when there is possibility (tawahhum), so refer back, but possible distinction between their su'r [of cat and donkey].
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on the su'r of domestic donkeys and mules. The majority of Hanafi mashayikh describe it as 'mashkuk' (doubtful), meaning that the status is unclear due to conflicting evidence. Abu Tahir al-Dabbas objected to the notion that any of Allah's rulings could be doubtful; he declared the su'r is pure but requires precaution, so he ruled that one should combine using it with tayammum and not rely on it alone when other water is available. The majority respond that 'shakk' here means suspension (tawaqquf) because of contradicting textual evidences, not ignorance of the ruling. The conflict is between hadiths: some forbid eating donkey meat, implying impurity, while other reports allow it under necessity. The mufta bihi position is that the su'r is pure but one should also perform tayammum out of caution. The passage ends by referring back to the earlier discussion on cat's su'r, suggesting a distinction. The text cuts off but the main point is clear.

Key Terms
مشكوك (mashkuk): Doubtful; a term used for the su'r of donkey and mule due to conflicting evidences on its status.
توقف (tawaqquf): Suspension of judgment when proofs conflict; a method in Hanafi usul.
استعمال (istihsan): Not used here; but ‘ist’imal (usage) refers to using the water for wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is najis and cannot be used
B) It is pure and can be used alone
C) It is pure but one should also perform tayammum out of caution
D) It is makruh to use it

Key Takeaway
The su'r of donkeys and mules is pure, but due to conflicting evidence, precaution (ihtiyat) demands also performing tayammum when using it for wudu.
