Su'r of Birds of Prey and Domestic Pests
Ruling on leftover water of birds of prey and household pests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the su'r of birds of prey and domestic pests, explain the role of istihsan in overriding qiyas, and apply the 'illa of tawaf to analogous cases.

Core Idea
The su'r of birds of prey is not impure but makruh due to istihsan overriding qiyas, based on the dry beak and necessity.

This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling on the leftover water (su'r) of birds of prey and household pests. While qiyas would deem their su'r impure due to prohibited meat, the school employs istihsan (juristic preference) based on practical necessity (darurah) and the nature of their drinking. Understanding this distinction is key to applying Hanafi principles of taharah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the hukm on the su'r of birds of prey according to the Hanafi school? The text states it is makruh (disliked) but not impure.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Locate the dalil
What proofs are cited? Qiyas (analogy) to beasts of prey would give impurity, but istihsan (juristic preference) is used to override it. Also the 'illa of tawaf (frequenting houses) is used for pests.
The istihsan is based on the dry beak and necessity.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Why does istihsan override qiyas? Because birds of prey drink with a dry beak (not a moist tongue), and there is a practical necessity (protection of vessels is difficult).
The qiyas is based on prohibited meat, but the mode of drinking differs.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf held that the karahah is only due to the possibility of impurity on the beak; if the beak is known clean, it is not makruh. Later scholars preferred this view.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) gave fatwa according to Abu Yusuf's narration, making it the operative position.
Thus, the mufta bihi is makruh tanzih, with a qualification for known cleanliness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما سؤر سباع الطير كالصقر والبازي فالقياس نجاسته لنجاسة لحمها لحرمة أكله كسباع البهائم، ووجه الاستحسان أن حرمة لحمها وإن اقتضت النجاسة لكنها تشرب بمنقارها وهو عظم جاف ظاهر لكنها تأكل الميتات والجيف غالباً فأشبه الدجاجة المخلاة فأورث الكراهة بخلاف سباع البهائم فإنها تشرب بلسانها وهو رطب بلعابها المتولد من لحمها وهو نجس فافترقا ولأن في سباع الطير ضرورة وبلوى فإنها تنقض من الهواء فتشرب ولا يمكن صون الأواني عنها خصوصاً في البراري وعن أبي يوسف أن الكراهة لتوهم النجاسة في منقارها لا لوصول لعابها إلى الماء حتى لو كانت محبوسة يعلم صاحبها أنه لا قذر في منقارها لا يكره التوضؤ بسؤرها واستحسن المشايخ المتأخرون هذه الرواية وأفتوا بها. كذا في النهاية. وفي التنجيس : يجوز أن يفتى بها . وأما سؤر سواكن البيوت كالحية والفأرة فلأن حرمة اللحم أوجبت النجاسة لكنها سقطت النجاسة بعلة الطواف وبقيت الكراهة، والعلة المذكورة في الحديث في الهرة موجودة بعينها في سواكن البيوت وهي الطواف فيثبت ذلك الحكم المترتب عليها وهو سقوط النجاسة وتثبت الكراهة لتوهمها . فرع تكره الصلاة حمل ما سؤره مكروه كالهرة كذا في التوشيح.
As for the leftover water of birds of prey, such as the falcon and hawk, by analogy (qiyas) it is impure, due to the impurity of their meat because eating them is prohibited, like beasts of prey. However, the basis of istihsan is that the prohibition of their meat, though it necessitates impurity, they drink with their beak, which is a dry bone and apparent, but they eat dead animals and carrion predominantly, so they resemble the free-roaming hen, and that causes karahah (dislike). Unlike beasts of prey, for they drink with their tongue, which is moist with saliva generated from their meat, which is impure, so they differ. Also, because in birds of prey there is necessity and tribulation, for they swoop from the air and drink, and it is impossible to protect vessels from them, especially in deserts. And from Abu Yusuf that the karahah is due to the possibility of impurity on their beak, not due to the saliva reaching the water, so if they are confined and its owner knows there is no filth on its beak, it is not disliked to perform wudu with its leftover water. The later scholars approved this narration and gave fatwa according to it. Thus in al-Nihayah. And in al-Tanjis: it is permissible to give fatwa according to it. As for the leftover water of domestic pests, like the snake and mouse, the prohibition of the meat necessitated impurity, but the impurity is removed by the cause of tawaf (frequenting houses), and karahah remains. The cause mentioned in the hadith regarding the cat is present exactly in domestic pests, which is tawaf, so the ruling attached to it is established, namely removal of impurity, and karahah is established due to the possibility of impurity. Branch: It is disliked to pray while carrying something whose su'r is disliked, like the cat. Thus in al-Tawshih.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on the leftover water (su'r) of birds of prey (siba' al-tayr) and household pests (sawaakin al-buyut). The author begins by stating that analogy (qiyas) would render the su'r of birds of prey impure, because their meat is prohibited (haram al-akl), similar to beasts of prey. However, the Hanafi principle of istihsan (juristic preference) overrides this qiyas. The reason: birds of prey drink with their beak, which is a dry bone and does not become moist with saliva the way a beast's tongue does. Additionally, they eat carrion, resembling a free-roaming hen (dajaja mukhalla), whose su'r is also considered disliked (makruh), not impure. There is also a practical necessity (darurah) because these birds are often in the wild and it is difficult to protect vessels from them. The author then reports a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf, who distinguishes between the cause of karahah: it is due to the possibility of impurity on the beak, not the saliva. Therefore, if the bird is confined and its beak is known to be clean, there is no karahah. The later scholars preferred this view and gave fatwa accordingly. As for household pests like snakes and mice, the author explains that although their meat is prohibited (implying impurity of saliva), the impurity is removed due to the 'illa of tawaf (frequenting houses), as in the cat. The cat's su'r is pure, and by analogy, these pests' su'r is also considered 'afw (excusable) but still disliked (makruh) because of the potential for impurity on their bodies. Finally, a branch ruling: it is disliked to pray while carrying something whose su'r is disliked, such as a cat. This shows the interconnectedness of rulings in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
سباع الطير (siba' al-tayr): Birds of prey, such as falcons and hawks, that hunt and eat meat including carrion.
الكراهة (al-karahah): Legal disliking (makruh), a recommendation to avoid, without prohibition or invalidation of worship.
العلة الطواف (al-'illa al-tawaf): The effective cause of frequenting or circling around houses, which justifies excusing impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the su'r of birds of prey considered makruh rather than impure according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because their meat is not prohibited.
B) Because they drink with a dry beak and there is necessity.
C) Because all animals' su'r is pure.
D) Because they are not considered carnivores.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on su'r balances qiyas and istihsan, resulting in makruh tanzih for birds of prey and domestic pests, not impurity.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Su'r of Donkeys and Mules: The Ruling of Doubt
Detailed expansion of the ruling on su'r of donkeys and mules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school classifies the su'r of donkeys and mules as mashkuk and derive the practical ruling of combining wudu and tayammum.

Core Idea
The Hanafi classification of su'r as mashkuk is based on conflicting evidences and the principle of darurah.

In this lesson, we explore the unique Hanafi category of mashkuk (doubtful) as applied to the leftover water (su'r) of donkeys and mules. The matn states that one should perform wudu with it and also perform tayammum, and that whichever is done first is valid. The commentary unpacks the reasoning behind this unusual ruling, including the conflict of hadiths on eating donkey meat, the disagreement of Companions, and the pivotal role of necessity (darurah). Understanding this ruling sharpens your grasp of how Hanafi usul handles conflicting proofs and the intermediate category between pure and impure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its surface statement
Read the opening line of the matn and commentary: the su'r of donkey and mule is mashkuk. Note the practical ruling: use it for wudu, then do tayammum if water is lost; either can be done first.
The ruling is unique to Hanafis; other schools do not have this intermediate category.
2
Understand the intra-Hanafi debate
Compare the majority view (doubtful status) with Abu Tahir al-Dabbas's view (pure but cautious). Identify why the majority rejects the pure status and insists on doubt.
Al-Dabbas's position is a minority within the school; the majority relies on conflicting evidences.
3
Analyze the conflicting proofs: hadith and necessity
Examine the two hadiths about eating donkey meat (prohibition and permission) and the disagreement of Companions (Ibn Umar vs Ibn Abbas). Then follow the author's dismissal of these as weak bases for doubt. The real basis is the conflict between the principle of impurity of saliva (from forbidden meat) and the principle of necessity (darurah) due to donkeys living in houses.
The author prefers the necessity-based reasoning over pure textual conflict.
4
Apply the qiyas (analogy) with cats and mice
The author draws an analogy: cats and mice have strong darurah (they enter narrow spaces), so their su'r is pure. Dogs and wild beasts have no darurah, so their su'r is impure. Donkeys have intermediate darurah (they stay in courtyards but not narrow spaces), so the ruling is suspended between purity and impurity.
This is a form of qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) that leads to the mashkuk status.
5
Derive the final operative ruling and refute objections
Confirm the mufta bihi: one must use the water for wudu and also perform tayammum. The author refutes objections regarding precaution and the analogy of two vessels. Understand that the doubt is about the water's purifying quality (tahuriyya), not its essential purity (tahara).
This distinction is crucial for the ruling: the water itself is pure, but its ability to remove impurity is doubtful.

والحمار والبغل مشكوك توضأ به وتيمم إن فقد ماء وأيا قدّم صح بخلاف نبيذ التمر . قوله (والحمار والبغل مشكوك أي سؤرهما مشكوك فيه هذه عبارة أكثر مشايخنا، وأبو طاهر الدباس أنكر أن يكون شيء من أحكام الله تعالى مشكوكاً فيه. وقال: سؤر الحمار طاهر لو غمس فيه الثوب جازت الصلاة معه إلا أنه محتاط فيه فأمر بالجمع بينه وبين التيمم ومنع منه حالة القدرة والمشايخ قالوا : المراد بالشك التوقف لتعارض الأدلة لا أن زاده في مبسوطه : وهذا لا يقوى لأن لحمه حرام بلا إشكال لأنه اجتمع المحرم والمبيح فغلب المحرم على المبيح كما لو أخبر عدل بأن هذا اللحم ذبيحة مجوسي والآخر أنه ذبيحة مسلم لا يحل أكله لغلبة الحرمة فكان لحمه حراماً بلا إشكال، ولعابه متولد منه فيكون نجساً بلا إشكال . وقيل : سبب الإشكال اختلاف الصحابة فإنه روي عن ابن عمر أنه كان يكره التوضؤ بسؤر الحمار والبغل. وعن ابن عباس أنه قال : الحمار يعلف القت والتبن فسؤره طاهر . قال شيخ الإسلام : وهذا لا يقوى أيضاً لأن الاختلاف في طهارة الماء ونجاسته لا يوجب الإشكال كما في إناء أخبر عدل أنه طاهر وآخر أنه نجس فالماء لا يصير مشكلاً وقد استوى الخبران وبقي العبرة للأصل فكذا هاههنا ، ولكن الأصح في التمسك أن دليل الشك هو التردد في الضرورة فإن الحمار يربط في الدور والأفنية فيشرب من الأواني وللضرورة أثر في إسقاط النجاسة كما في الهرة والفأرة إلا أن الضرورة في الحمار دون الضرورة فيهما لدخولهما مضايق البيت بخلاف الحمار، ولو لم تكن الضرورة ثابتة أصلاً كما في الكلب والسباع لوجب الحكم بالنجاسة بلا إشكال ولو كانت الضرورة مثل الضرورة فيهما لوجب الحكم بإسقاط النجاسة، فلما ثبتت الضرورة من وجه دون وجه واستوى ما يوجب النجاسة والطهارة تساقطاً للتعارض فوجب المصير إلى الأصل والأصل هاهنا شيئان: الطهارة في جانب الماء والنجاسة في جانب اللعاب لأن لعابه نجس كما بينا وليس أحدهما بأولى من الآخر فبقي الأمر مشكلاً نجساً من وجه طاهراً من وجه فكان الإشكال عند علمائنا بهذا الطريق لا للإشكال في لحمه ولا لاختلاف الصحابة في سؤره وبهذا التقرير يندفع كثير من الأسئلة منها أن المحرم والمبيح إذا اجتمعا يغلب المحرم احتياطاً، وجوابه أن القول بالاحتياط إنما يكون في ترجيح الحرمة في غير هذا الموضع أما هاهنا الاحتياط في إثبات الشك لأنا إن رجحنا الحرمة للاحتياط يلزم ترك العمل بالاحتياط لأنه حينئذ لا يجوز استعمال سؤر الحمار احتمال كونه مطهراً باعتبار الشك فكان متيمماً عند وجود الماء في أحد الوجهين وذلك حرام، فلا يكون عملاً بالاحتياط ولا بالمباح، وما قيل إن في تغليب الحرمة تقليل النسخ فذلك في تعارض النصين لا في الضرورة ومنها أن يقال : لما وقع التعارض في سؤره وجب المصير إلى الخلف وهو التيمم كمن له إنا أن أحدهما طاهر والآخر نجس فاشتبه عليه فإنه يسقط استعمال الماء ويجب التيمم، فكذا ههنا قلنا الماء ههنا طاهر لما ذكرنا أن قضية الشك أن يبقى كل واحد على حاله ولم يزل الحدث لأنه لما كان ثابتاً بيقين فيبقى إلى أن المزيل بيقين، والماء طاهر وقع الشك في طهوريته فلا يسقط استعماله بالشك بخلاف الإناءين فإن أحدهما نجس يقيناً والآخر طاهر يقيناً لكنه عجز عن استعماله لعدم علمه فيصار إلى الخلف.
And the donkey and mule are doubtful: one performs wudu with it and performs tayammum if water is lost, and whichever is done first is valid, unlike date nabidh. His statement: (The donkey and mule are doubtful) meaning their leftover water is doubtful. This is the expression of most of our scholars. Abu Tahir al-Dabbas denied that anything of Allah's rulings could be doubtful. He said: The leftover water of the donkey is pure; if a garment is dipped in it, prayer is permitted with it, except that it is cautious, so he ordered combining it with tayammum and forbade it when able. The scholars said: What is meant by doubt is suspension due to conflicting evidences, not that it means ignorance of the legal ruling, because its ruling is known: it is obligatory to use it, and impurity is negated, and tayammum is attached to it. The statement of suspension when evidences conflict is proof of knowledge and utmost piety. The explanation of the conflict according to al-Mabsut: conflict of reports about eating its meat, for it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade eating the meat of domestic donkeys on the day of Khaybar. And Ghali ibn Abjar narrated: I had no property left except some small donkeys, so he (peace be upon him) said: 'Eat from the fat of your property.' Shaykh al-Islam Khwahar Zadeh said in his Mabsut: This is not strong, because its meat is undoubtedly forbidden, as the forbidden and permitted came together, and the forbidden prevailed over the permitted, just as if a reliable person reported that this meat is from a Magian's slaughter and another that it is from a Muslim's slaughter, it is not permissible to eat it due to the predominance of prohibition. So its meat is undoubtedly forbidden, and its saliva is generated from it, so it is undoubtedly impure. It was said: The cause of doubt is the disagreement of the Companions, for it is narrated that Ibn 'Umar disliked performing wudu with the leftover water of donkey and mule, and Ibn 'Abbas said: The donkey eats fodder and straw, so its leftover water is pure. Shaykh al-Islam said: This is also not strong, because disagreement about the purity or impurity of water does not cause doubt, just as a vessel about which a reliable person says it is pure and another says it is impure, the water does not become doubtful, and the reports are equal, and reliance is on the original state. So it is here. But the correct way to adhere is that the evidence of doubt is the hesitation regarding necessity. For the donkey is tied in houses and courtyards and drinks from vessels, and necessity has an effect in removing impurity, as in the cat and the mouse. However, the necessity in the donkey is less than the necessity in them because they enter narrow places of the house, unlike the donkey. If necessity were not established at all, as in the dog and beasts, it would be necessary to judge impurity without doubt. If necessity were like the necessity in them, it would be necessary to judge that impurity is removed. Since necessity is established in one way and not another, and what necessitates impurity and purity are equal, they cancel out due to conflict, so it is necessary to resort to the original state. The original state here is two things: purity on the side of water and impurity on the side of saliva, because its saliva is impure as we clarified, and neither is more likely than the other. So the matter remains doubtful: impure in one aspect, pure in another. So the doubt according to our scholars is in this way, not due to doubt about its meat nor due to the disagreement of the Companions about its leftover water. With this explanation, many questions are refuted. Among them is: when the forbidden and permitted come together, the forbidden prevails as a precaution. The answer is that the statement about precaution only applies when preference is given to prohibition in a place other than this. Here, precaution is in establishing doubt, because if we give preference to prohibition as a precaution, it would necessitate abandoning precaution, because then it would not be permissible to use the donkey's leftover water, due to the possibility that it may be purifying because of doubt. So he would do tayammum in the presence of water in one of the two views, and that is forbidden. So it is not acting according to precaution nor according to permission. And what is said that in giving preference to prohibition there is a reduction of abrogation applies to conflict of texts, not to necessity. And among them is that it is said: When conflict occurred regarding its leftover water, it is necessary to resort to the alternative, which is tayammum, like the one who has two vessels, one pure and one impure, and they are mixed up, then he abandons water and must do tayammum. So here we say: The water here is pure as we mentioned, because the consequence of doubt is that each thing remains in its state, and the state of ritual impurity is not removed because it was established with certainty, so it remains until something that removes it with certainty comes. The water is pure, and doubt has occurred about its purifying quality, so its use is not invalidated by doubt, unlike the two vessels, for one of them is definitely impure and the other definitely pure, but he is unable to use it due to not knowing, so he resorts to the alternative.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion of the ruling on the leftover water (su'r) of donkeys and mules. The author, al-Marghinani, begins by stating the ruling from the matn: the su'r is considered doubtful (mashkuk). This means that one should perform wudu with it if available, but also perform tayammum when water is lost; and whichever is done first is valid. The commentary then explains the nature of this doubt. Most Hanafi scholars hold that 'doubt' here means suspension due to conflicting evidences, not ignorance of the ruling. Abu Tahir al-Dabbas disagreed, arguing that nothing in Allah's law is doubtful. He held the water is pure, but combined with tayammum out of caution. The majority view is that the doubt arises from conflicting reports about eating donkey meat: a hadith of prohibition on the day of Khaybar, and another hadith from Ghali ibn Abjar permitting it. Shaykh al-Islam Khwahar Zadeh dismisses this conflict, asserting the meat is undoubtedly forbidden, so the saliva is also impure. The correct basis for doubt, he argues, is the element of necessity (darurah). Donkeys are commonly kept in houses and drink from vessels, so necessity requires leniency, but since the necessity is not as strong as for cats and mice (which enter narrow places), the ruling becomes suspended between purity and impurity. The author then refutes several hypothetical objections, such as the argument that when forbidden and permitted conflict, the forbidden should prevail as a precaution. He explains that here precaution lies in maintaining the doubt, and that the analogy with two vessels (one pure, one impure) does not apply because in that case the water is definitely impure, whereas here the water itself is pure, only its purifying quality is in doubt. This is a classic Hanafi discussion of the interplay between legal proofs and practical necessity.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): The leftover water or liquid that remains after an animal drinks from a vessel.
مشكوك (mashkuk): A legal status where the ruling is suspended due to conflicting evidences, neither pure nor impure definitively.
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity or common hardship that justifies a relaxation of the original strict ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the su'r of donkey and mule considered doubtful (mashkuk)?
A) Because their meat is definitively forbidden.
B) Because of conflicting hadiths about their meat and the necessity of their presence in houses.
C) Because there is no evidence at all.
D) Because all animals' su'r is doubtful.

Key Takeaway
The su'r of donkey and mule is mashkuk, requiring both wudu and tayammum due to conflicting evidence and moderate necessity.

Taharah — Purification
advanced
12 min
The Doubtful Leftover of a Donkey: Taharah vs. Tahuriyyah
Hanafi analysis of the doubt regarding su'r al-himar: taharah vs. tahuriyyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that the su'r of a donkey is pure but not purifying, and distinguish between the nature of doubt (shakk) in taharah versus tahuriyyah.

Core Idea
The donkey's leftover is pure but cannot purify — the doubt is about its purifying power, not its purity.

When a donkey drinks from a vessel, the leftover water is not clearly pure or impure. This lesson unpacks the sophisticated Hanafi reasoning behind this ruling. You will learn how the concept of necessity (darurah) and the equipoise of opposing factors lead to a unique classification: the water is tahir (pure) but not tahur (purifying). We will also navigate the internal Hanafi disagreement on whether the doubt lies in taharah or tahuriyyah, and why the majority view prevails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
What is the exact status of the donkey's su'r? Is it pure, impure, or something else? Read the passage to find the core ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah.
The text states it does not make things impure nor remove hadath.
2
Understand two rejected explanations
The author dismisses two incorrect reasons for the doubt: the prohibition of donkey meat and the disagreement of the Companions. Why are these insufficient?
Meat's haram does not directly determine saliva's status; Companions' disagreement does not create doubt in the water itself.
3
Grasp the correct reasoning: darurah and equipoise
The correct cause is the partial necessity (darurah) of donkeys. Compare with cats (full necessity, so su'r is pure) and dogs (no necessity, so su'r is impure). The donkey is in between, leading to conflicting evidence that cancels out, leaving two original states: water is pure, saliva is impure. Hence doubt arises.
The doubt is not about the water's own purity but about its ability to purify (tahuriyyah).
4
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some scholars said the doubt is about taharah (purity), some about tahuriyyah, some about both. Identify which view is al-ashahh (most correct) and why the majority holds it.
The majority view is that doubt is about tahuriyyah. The difference is largely verbal because the practical outcome is the same: it does not make things impure but cannot be used for wudu.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
If a donkey's leftover falls into a well, can you perform wudu with that water? The answer depends on whether the doubt is about taharah or tahuriyyah. Use the passage's distinctions to answer.
If the doubt is about tahuriyyah, the water is like used water: permissible for wudu as long as it does not predominate.

Source Text

كتاب الطهارة
مال إلا حميرات فقال عليه السلام كل من سمين مالك . قال شيخ الإسلام خواهر زاده في مبسوطه : وهذا لا يقوى لأن لحمه حرام بلا إشكال لأنه اجتمع المحرم والمبيح فغلب المحرم على المبيح كما لو أخبر عدل بأن هذا اللحم ذبيحة مجوسي والآخر أنه ذبيحة مسلم لا يحل أكله لغلبة الحرمة فكان لحمه حراماً بلا إشكال، ولعابه متولد منه فيكون نجساً بلا إشكال . وقيل : سبب الإشكال اختلاف الصحابة فإنه روي عن ابن عمر أنه كان يكره التوضؤ بسؤر الحمار والبغل. وعن ابن عباس أنه قال : الحمار يعلف القت والتبن فسؤره طاهر . قال شيخ الإسلام : وهذا لا يقوى أيضاً لأن الاختلاف في طهارة الماء ونجاسته لا يوجب الإشكال كما في إناء أخبر عدل أنه طاهر وآخر أنه نجس فالماء لا يصير مشكلاً وقد استوى الخبران وبقي العبرة للأصل فكذا هاههنا ، ولكن الأصح في التمسك أن دليل الشك هو التردد في الضرورة فإن الحمار يربط في الدور والأفنية فيشرب من الأواني وللضرورة أثر في إسقاط النجاسة كما في الهرة والفأرة إلا أن الضرورة في الحمار دون الضرورة فيهما لدخولهما مضايق البيت بخلاف الحمار، ولو لم تكن الضرورة ثابتة أصلاً كما في الكلب والسباع لوجب الحكم بالنجاسة بلا إشكال ولو كانت الضرورة مثل الضرورة فيهما لوجب الحكم بإسقاط النجاسة، فلما ثبتت الضرورة من وجه دون وجه واستوى ما يوجب النجاسة والطهارة تساقطاً للتعارض فوجب المصير إلى الأصل والأصل هاهنا شيئان: الطهارة في جانب الماء والنجاسة في جانب اللعاب لأن لعابه نجس كما بينا وليس أحدهما بأولى من الآخر فبقي الأمر مشكلاً نجساً من وجه طاهراً من وجه فكان الإشكال عند علمائنا بهذا الطريق لا للإشكال في لحمه ولا لاختلاف الصحابة في سؤره وبهذا التقرير يندفع كثير من الأسئلة منها أن المحرم والمبيح إذا اجتمعا يغلب المحرم احتياطاً، وجوابه أن القول بالاحتياط إنما يكون في ترجيح الحرمة في غير هذا الموضع أما هاهنا الاحتياط في إثبات الشك لأنا إن رجحنا الحرمة للاحتياط يلزم ترك العمل بالاحتياط لأنه حينئذ لا يجوز استعمال سؤر الحمار احتمال كونه مطهراً باعتبار الشك فكان متيمماً عند وجود الماء في أحد الوجهين وذلك حرام، فلا يكون عملاً بالاحتياط ولا بالمباح، وما قيل إن في تغليب الحرمة تقليل النسخ فذلك في تعارض النصين لا في الضرورة ومنها أن يقال : لما وقع التعارض في سؤره وجب المصير إلى الخلف وهو التيمم كمن له إنا أن أحدهما طاهر والآخر نجس فاشتبه عليه فإنه يسقط استعمال الماء ويجب التيمم، فكذا ههنا قلنا الماء ههنا طاهر لما ذكرنا أن قضية الشك أن يبقى كل واحد على حاله ولم يزل الحدث لأنه لما كان ثابتاً بيقين فيبقى إلى أن المزيل بيقين، والماء طاهر وقع الشك في طهوريته فلا يسقط استعماله بالشك بخلاف الإناءين فإن أحدهما نجس يقيناً والآخر طاهر يقيناً لكنه عجز عن استعماله لعدم علمه فيصار إلى الخلف. ومنها أن التعارض لا يوجب الشك كما في إخبار عدلين بالطهارة والنجاسة حيث يتوضأ بلا تيمم. قلنا في تعارض الخبرين وجب تساقطهما فرجحنا كون الماء مطهراً باستصحاب الحال والماء كان مطهراً قبله وههنا تعارض جهتا الضرورة فتساقطتا فأبقينا ما كان على ما كان أيضاً إلا أن ههنا ما كان ثابتاً على حاله قبل التعارض شيئان : جانب الماء وجانب اللعاب وليس أحدهما بأولى من الآخر فوجب الشك. ومنها ما قيل في استعمال الماء ترك العمل بالاحتياط من وجه آخر لأنه إن كان نجساً فقد تنجس العضو قلنا : أما على القول بأن الشك في الطهورية فظاهر، وأما على القول المرجوح من أن الشك في كونه طاهراً فالجواب أن العضو طاهر بيقين فلا يتنجس بالشك، والحدث ثابت بيقين فلا يزول بالشك فيجب ضم التيمم ضم التيمم إليه كذا في معراج الدراية وغيره.
وفي الكافي ولم يتعارض الخبر أن في سؤر الهرة إذ قوله «الهرة سبع» لا يقتضي نجاسة السؤر لما قدمنا أهـ. ثم اختلف مشايخنا فقيل الشك في طهارته، وقيل في طهوريته،
وقيل فيهما جميعاً، والأصح أنه في طهوريته وهو قول الجمهور. كذا في الكافي. هذا اتفاقهم أنه على ظاهر الرواية لا ينجس الثوب والبدن والماء ولا يرفع الحدث فلهذا قال في كشف الأسرار شرح أصول فخر الإسلام: إن الاختلاف لفظي لأن من قال الشك في طهوريته لا في طهارته أراد أن الطاهر لا يتنجس به ووجب الجمع بينه وبين التراب لا أن ليس في طهارته شك أصلاً لأن الشك في طهوريته إنما نشأ الشك من في طهارته لتعارض الأدلة في طهارته ونجاسته أهـ. وبهذا التقرير علم ضعف ما استدل به في الهداية لقول من قال الشك في طهوريته بأنه لو وجد الماء المطلق لا يجب عليه غسل رأسه فإن وجوب إنما يثبت بتيقن النجاسة والثابت الشك فيها فلا يتنجس الرأس بالشك فلا يجب. وعلم أيضاً ضعف ما في فتاوى قاضيخان تفريعاً على كون الشك في طهارته أنه لو وقع في الماء القليل أفسده لأنه لا إفساد بالشك، وفي المحيط تفريعاً على الشك في طهوريته أنه لو وقع في الماء يجوز التوضؤ به ما لم يغلب عليه لأنه طاهر غير طهور كالماء المستعمل عند محمد اهـ.
Book of Taharah. ... except that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Everyone from the family of Malik.' Shaykh al-Islam Khwahrizadeh said in his Mabsut: This is not strong because its meat is undoubtedly haram, since the prohibited and the permitted came together, and the prohibited prevails over the permitted, just as if two upright persons inform, one that this meat is from a Magian slaughter and the other that it is from a Muslim slaughter, it is not permissible to eat it due to the predominance of prohibition. So its meat is undoubtedly haram, and its saliva is produced from it, so it is undoubtedly najis. And it is said: The cause of the doubt is the disagreement of the Companions, for it is narrated from Ibn Umar that he disliked performing wudu with the leftover of a donkey and a mule, and from Ibn Abbas that he said: The donkey is fed with fodder and straw, so its leftover is tahir. Shaykh al-Islam said: This is also not strong, because disagreement about the purity or impurity of water does not cause doubt, as in the case of a vessel where one upright person says it is tahir and another says it is najis: the water does not become doubtful, the two reports cancel each other, and the original state (al-asl) is considered. So here too. But the correct approach to hold is that the evidence of doubt is the uncertainty regarding necessity (al-darurah). For the donkey is tied in houses and courtyards and drinks from vessels, and necessity has an effect in removing impurity, as in the case of the cat and the mouse. However, the necessity for the donkey is less than the necessity for them because they enter the narrow parts of the house unlike the donkey. And if necessity were not established at all, as in the case of the dog and wild beasts, the ruling of impurity would be obligatory without doubt. And if necessity were equal to that for them, the ruling of removing impurity would be obligatory. So when necessity is established from one aspect and not from another, and what necessitates impurity and purity are equal, they cancel each other due to conflict, and one must resort to the original state (al-asl). The original state here is two things: purity with respect to the water, and impurity with respect to the saliva, because his saliva is impure as we explained, and neither is more deserving than the other. So the matter remains doubtful: impure in one aspect, pure in another. Thus the doubt according to our scholars arises in this way, not due to doubt about its meat nor due to the disagreement of the Companions about its leftover. And with this explanation, many objections are repelled. Among them is that when the prohibited and the permitted come together, the prohibited prevails as a precaution (ihtiyat). The answer is that the saying of precaution is only for preferring prohibition in other than this place. Here, precaution lies in establishing doubt, because if we prefer prohibition for precaution, we would be abandoning acting on precaution, because then it would not be permissible to use the leftover of the donkey, as it might be purifying due to doubt, so one would be a mutayammim when water is present in one of the two aspects, which is haram. So it is neither an act of precaution nor of permissibility. And what is said about preferring prohibition reducing abrogation applies to conflicting texts, not to necessity. Another objection: Since conflict occurred regarding its leftover, one must resort to the alternative (al-khalaf), which is tayammum, like someone who has two vessels, one tahir and one najis, and they are confused: then the use of water is waived and tayammum is obligatory. So here too? We say: The water here is tahir because, as we mentioned, the nature of doubt is that each thing remains in its original state, and the state of hadath is not removed because it was established with certainty, so it remains until removed by certainty. The water is tahir, and doubt arose about its tahuriyyah, so its use is not waived by doubt, unlike the two vessels because one of them is certainly najis and the other is certainly tahir, but he is unable to use it due to lack of knowledge, so he resorts to the alternative. Another objection: Conflict does not necessitate doubt, as in the case of two upright witnesses reporting purity and impurity, where one performs wudu without tayammum. We say: In conflicting reports, both are dropped, and we prefer that the water is purifying by istishab al-hal, as water was purifying before. Here, the two aspects of necessity conflict and are cancelled, so we also keep things as they were, except that here there were two things established prior to the conflict: the water side and the saliva side, and neither is more deserving than the other, so doubt is necessitated. Another objection: The use of water abandons precaution from another aspect because if it is impure, the limb becomes impure. We say: As for the opinion that the doubt is about tahuriyyah, it is clear. As for the weaker opinion that the doubt is about it being tahir, the answer is that the limb is certainly tahir, so it does not become impure by doubt, and the hadath is certainly established, so it is not removed by doubt, so tayammum must be added to it. This is from Mi'raj al-Dirayah and others. And in al-Kafi: The report about the cat's leftover is not conflicting, for his statement 'The cat is a wild beast' does not necessitate the impurity of its leftover, for what we have mentioned. Then our scholars differed: Some said the doubt is about its taharah, some about its tahuriyyah, and some about both. The most correct is that it is about its tahuriyyah, which is the view of the majority. This is in al-Kafi. They agree that according to the external transmission (zahir al-riwaya), it does not make garments, bodies, or water impure, nor does it remove hadath. Therefore the author of Kashf al-Asrar said: The difference is verbal, because those who say the doubt is about tahuriyyah not about taharah mean that the pure (tahir) is not made impure by it, and one must combine it with earth, not that there is no doubt about its taharah at all, for the doubt about tahuriyyah arose from doubt about taharah due to conflicting evidence. And by this explanation, the weakness of what al-Hidayah cited for the view that the doubt is about tahuriyyah is known: that if he finds absolute water, he is not obliged to wash his head, for obligation is established by certainty of impurity, and only doubt is established, so the head does not become impure by doubt, so it is not obligatory. And also the weakness of what is in Fatawa Qadikhan is known, in a branch based on the view that the doubt is about its taharah: that if it falls into little water, it spoils it, because there is no spoiling by doubt. And in al-Muhit, in a branch based on the doubt about tahuriyyah: that if it falls into water, it is permissible to perform wudu with it as long as it does not overcome it, because it is tahir but not tahur, like used water according to Muhammad.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a detailed Hanafi investigation into the ruling on the leftover water (su'r) of a donkey. The discussion is part of the larger topic of taharah (ritual purity). The author, Ibn Nujaym, is explaining the reasoning behind the position that the su'r of a donkey is 'mushkil' (problematic) — meaning it is not clearly pure or impure, but rather a doubt exists about its status.

The passage first addresses a weaker opinion that the doubt arises from the meat of the donkey being haram, or from disagreement among the Companions. Ibn Nujaym, citing Shaykh al-Islam Khwahrizadeh, refutes these: the meat's prohibition does not directly determine the status of the saliva, and the Companions' disagreement does not create doubt in the water itself, as analogous cases show.

The core Hanafi reasoning is based on the concept of darurah (necessity). Donkeys are commonly kept in homes and drink from vessels, creating a need to tolerate their leftovers, similar to cats and mice. However, the necessity for donkeys is less than for cats and mice because cats and mice enter narrow places of the house, whereas donkeys do not. Thus, the necessity is partial: it is present enough to prevent a clear ruling of impurity (najis), but not strong enough to make the leftover clearly purifying (tahur). This equipoise leads to doubt. The analogy with the cat is used to show that when necessity is strong, impurity is removed; when absent, impurity is certain; here it is intermediate.

Because the two opposing factors (necessity vs. original impurity of saliva) cancel out, the original state (al-asl) is consulted. But there are two original states: the water itself is originally pure (tahir) from its own nature, but the donkey's saliva is originally impure. Neither overrides the other, so the leftover is considered doubtfully pure — it does not impart impurity to anything it touches, but it is also not considered purifying (tahur), meaning it cannot be used for ritual purification (wudu or ghusl). This is the relied-upon position (al-ashahh): the doubt is about tahuriyyah (the capacity to purify), not about taharah (purity per se). The majority of Hanafi scholars hold this view.

The passage then addresses several objections, demonstrating the sophistication of Hanafi usul. One key objection is that when prohibition and permission conflict, prohibition should prevail as a precaution (ihtiyat). The reply: here, the precautionary approach actually leads to abandoning precaution, because if we treat it as impure, one might avoid using it and resort to tayammum even when water is present, which is forbidden. So the true precaution is to admit doubt.

Another objection analogizes to the case of two vessels (one pure, one impure) which necessitates tayammum. The reply distinguishes: in the two-vessel case, there is certainty that one is impure, so using either is impossible. Here, the specific water is not certainly impure; only its purifying power is doubted. So wudu is still performed with it, and tayammum is not required.

The text also clarifies that the difference among Hanafi scholars about whether the doubt is in taharah or tahuriyyah is largely verbal. Those who say the doubt is in tahuriyyah do not deny some doubt in taharah; rather, they emphasize that the water is safe from making things impure, but it is not reliable for purification. The practical effect is the same: the leftover does not render things impure, but it cannot be used for wudu or ghusl.

Finally, the author critiques arguments from al-Hidayah and Fatawa Qadikhan, showing that the correct view is the one in al-Muhit: if the leftover falls into water, it is treated like used water (musta'mal) — it is tahir but not tahur, so wudu is permissible with it as long as it does not become predominant.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): Leftover water or drink that remains in a vessel after an animal or person has drunk from it.
شك (shakk): Doubt; here it refers to the uncertainty about the legal status (purity vs. impurity, or purifying capacity) of an object due to conflicting evidence of equal strength.
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity; here it means the common need or difficulty that would arise if the leftover of an animal were considered impure, leading to a relaxation in the ruling.
طهورية (tahuriyyah): The quality of being purifying (mutahhir); i.e., the capacity of water to remove ritual impurity (hadath) and filth (najis).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars, what is the nature of the doubt (shakk) regarding the leftover water (su'r) of a donkey?
A) The doubt is about its taharah (purity).
B) The doubt is about its tahuriyyah (purifying capacity).
C) The doubt is about both taharah and tahuriyyah equally.
D) There is no doubt; it is clearly impure.

Key Takeaway
The donkey's leftover water is pure (tahir) but not purifying (tahur); it does not impart impurity but cannot be used for wudu or ghusl.

The Cat's Leftover Water: Pure but Not Purifying
Ruling on cat's su'ur with proof and intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the cat's su'ur, identify the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf regarding the nature of the doubt, and apply the mufta bihi position when asked about using such water for wudhu.

Core Idea
The cat's leftover water is pure but not purifying—it does not defile, but alone cannot lift ritual impurity.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra’iq addresses the legal status of the leftover water (su'ur) of a domestic cat, a common question in daily life. The Hanafi school, while acknowledging a hadith that the cat is a beast of prey, distinguishes between purity (tahara) and purifying capacity (tahuriyya). The lesson explores the proof from conflicting evidence, the application of istishab, and the intra-madhhab disagreement about the nature of the doubt, ultimately settling on the majority view that the water is pure but not purifying. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly performing wudhu in such cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is using cat's su'ur for wudhu. The Hanafi ruling is that the water is pure (tahir) but not purifying (tuhur).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the hadith 'الهرة سبع' (the cat is a beast of prey), which could imply impurity but is interpreted otherwise due to necessity.
Sunnah ahad, zanni al-thubut wa al-dalalah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith is overridden by istihsan based on the necessity of cats being domestic animals, and by istishab of the original purity of water. Conflicting evidences lead to doubt about the water's purifying property.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Hanafi scholars differed: some said the doubt is in purity (tahara), some in purifying property (tahuriyya), some in both. The majority (al-ashahh) is that the doubt is in tahuriyya.
The practical consequence: if the doubt were in tahara, the water would be considered impure; but being in tahuriyya, it remains pure but not purifying.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi is that the cat's su'ur is tahir (pure) but not tuhur (purifying). Thus, using it for wudhu requires combining with tayammum.
This is the position in Zahir al-Riwayah, confirmed by the mashayikh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حيث يتوضأ بلا تيمم. قلنا في تعارض الخبرين وجب تساقطهما فرجحنا كون الماء مطهراً باستصحاب الحال والماء كان مطهراً قبله وههنا تعارض جهتا الضرورة فتساقطتا فأبقينا ما كان على ما كان أيضاً إلا أن ههنا ما كان ثابتاً على حاله قبل التعارض شيئان : جانب الماء وجانب اللعاب وليس أحدهما بأولى من الآخر فوجب الشك. ومنها ما قيل في استعمال الماء ترك العمل بالاحتياط من وجه آخر لأنه إن كان نجساً فقد تنجس العضو قلنا : أما على القول بأن الشك في الطهورية فظاهر، وأما على القول المرجوح من أن الشك في كونه طاهراً فالجواب أن العضو طاهر بيقين فلا يتنجس بالشك، والحدث ثابت بيقين فلا يزول بالشك فيجب ضم التيمم إليه كذا في معراج الدراية وغيره. وفي الكافي ولم يتعارض الخبر أن في سؤر الهرة إذ قوله «الهرة سبع» لا يقتضي نجاسة السؤر لما قدمنا أهـ. ثم اختلف مشايخنا فقيل الشك في طهارته، وقيل في طهوريته، وقيل فيهما جميعاً، والأصح أنه في طهوريته وهو قول الجمهور. كذا في الكافي.
Where he performs wudhu without tayammum. We said: when two reports conflict, they must cancel each other out, so we give preponderance to water being purifying by istishab of the original state, and water was purifying before him. Here, two aspects of necessity conflict, so they cancel, and we keep what was as it was. However, here before the conflict there were two things established: the side of water and the side of saliva, and neither is more deserving than the other, so doubt arose. Among them is what was said about using water: abandoning precaution from another angle because if it is impure, the limb becomes impure. We said: as for the opinion that the doubt is in its purifying property (tahuriyya), it is apparent. As for the less preponderant opinion that the doubt is in its being pure (taharah), the answer is that the limb is certainly pure, so it does not become impure by doubt, and the hadath (ritual impurity) is certainly established, so it is not removed by doubt. Therefore, tayammum must be added to it, as in Miraj al-Diraya and others. In al-Kafi: The report does not conflict that regarding the leftover water of the cat, since his statement, 'The cat is a beast of prey,' does not necessitate the impurity of its leftover water, as we have stated. End. Then our mashayikh differed: some said the doubt is in its purity (taharah), some said in its purifying property (tahuriyya), and some said in both. The most correct is that it is in its purifying property, and that is the position of the majority. As in al-Kafi.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the leftover water (su'ur) of a domestic cat. The author begins by addressing an objection: if someone uses such water for wudhu without tayammum, how can it be valid? The argument is that when evidence conflicts, we resort to istishab (presumption of continuity), and here the doubt necessitates combining tayammum. Then he quotes from al-Kafi that the hadith 'The cat is a beast of prey' does not necessitate impurity of its leftover water due to necessity. Following that, he mentions the ikhtilaf among Hanafi scholars: some say the doubt is about the water being pure (tahir), some say about it being purifying (tuhur), and some about both. The relied-upon position (al-ashahh) is that the doubt is about its purifying property, meaning the water is pure (tahir) but not purifying (ghayr tuhur). This is the position of the majority. The practical implication is that the water will not defile clothes, body, or other water, but cannot be used to lift ritual impurity without combining with tayammum.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'ur): The leftover water or liquid after an animal has drunk from it
طهورية (tahuriyya): The property of being purifying (mutahhir)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the leftover water (su'ur) of a domestic cat according to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi madhhab?
A) Najis and impure
B) Pure and purifying (tuhur)
C) Pure but not purifying
D) Disliked (makruh)

Key Takeaway
The cat's leftover water is pure (tahir) but not purifying (tuhur); it must be combined with tayammum when used for wudhu.

The Verbal Nature of the Dispute on Cat's Su'ur
Critical refinement of an intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi disagreement on the cat's leftover water is verbal (lafzi) and apply the principle that a verbal dispute has no practical effect on the ruling.

Core Idea
The cat's su'ur is a verbal dispute: all Hanafis agree on the ruling, only the description of the doubt differs.

In this passage, Ibn Nujaym (author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) clarifies that the apparent disagreement among Hanafi scholars about the cat's leftover water is merely verbal. The practical ruling is unanimously agreed upon: it does not defile and does not remove hadath without tayammum. The disagreement is only about whether the doubt pertains to its tahara (purity) or its tahuriyya (purifying property). Understanding this concept of ikhtilaf lafzi is crucial for distinguishing between substantive and verbal disagreements in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed ruling
Note that all Hanafis agree cat's su'ur does not defile clothes, body, or water, and it does not remove hadath without tayammum.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
2
Understand the two positions
Some scholars (like those cited in Fatawa Qadikhan) say the doubt is in tahara (whether it is pure). Others, such as the author of Kashf al-Asrar, say the doubt is in tahuriyya (whether it purifies).
3
Recognize the verbal nature
According to Kashf al-Asrar, the difference is only about wording (lafzi). The view that doubt is in tahuriyya does not deny doubt in tahara entirely; it merely describes the practical implication.
An ikhtilaf lafzi has no effect on the ruling.
4
Analyze the refutation of al-Hidayah's argument
Al-Hidayah argued that if the doubt were in tahuriyya, then after using cat su'ur, if one finds absolute water, they would not need to wash their head (because the hadath is already lifted). Ibn Nujaym refutes this by showing that the doubt in tahuriyya does not eliminate the need for washing due to the principle that doubt does not remove certainty.
The argument fails because it confuses the type of doubt.
5
Apply the principle of ikhtilaf lafzi
Conclude that there is no practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf), so the ruling stands: cat su'ur is pure but not purifying. A mufti can rely on either formulation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا اتفاقهم أنه على ظاهر الرواية لا ينجس الثوب والبدن والماء ولا يرفع الحدث فلهذا قال في كشف الأسرار شرح أصول فخر الإسلام: إن الاختلاف لفظي لأن من قال الشك في طهوريته لا في طهارته أراد أن الطاهر لا يتنجس به ووجب الجمع بينه وبين التراب لا أن ليس في طهارته شك أصلاً لأن الشك في طهوريته إنما نشأ من الشك في طهارته لتعارض الأدلة في طهارته ونجاسته أهـ. وبهذا التقرير علم ضعف ما استدل به في الهداية لقول من قال الشك في طهوريته بأنه لو وجد الماء المطلق لا يجب عليه غسل رأسه فإن وجوب إنما يثبت بتيقن النجاسة والثابت الشك فيها فلا يتنجس الرأس بالشك فلا يجب. وعلم أيضاً ضعف ما في فتاوى قاضيخان تفريعاً على كون الشك في طهارته أنه لو وقع في الماء القليل أفسده لأنه لا إفساد بالشك، وفي المحيط تفريعاً على الشك في طهوريته أنه لو وقع في الماء يجوز التوضؤ به ما لم يغلب عليه لأنه طاهر غير طهور كالماء المستعمل عند محمد اهـ. وكان غسله وحملها بأن السؤر فيه ضرورة بخلاف الحمل تأمل قوله : (لا يقتضي نجاسة السؤر لما قدمنا) أي من سقوطها للضرورة قوله : (بأنه لو وجد الماء المطلق الخ) بيانه كما في بعض الشروح أن من توضأ بالسؤر المشكوك إذا أحدث فقد حل الحدث بالرأس أيضاً، فإذا توضأ بعده بالماء المطلق ومسح رأسه تكون بلة الماء المطلق على رأسه مشكوكاً أيضاً لإصابته إياه فلا يرفع الحدث المتيقن لأنه مشكوك والشك لا يرفع اليقين فيجب غسل رأسه لهذا المعنى، فلما لم يجب دل على أن الشك في طهوريته لا في طهارته قوله : (وعلم أيضاً ضعف ما في فتاوى قاضيخان الخ) قال في النهر : لقائل أن يمنع قوله لأن الشك الخ بأن الشك في الطهورية لا يستلزم الشك في الطهارة بخلاف العكس كما هو ظاهر فما في الخانية له وجه وجيه اهـ لكن قول المؤلف «لأنه لا إفساد بالشك» الوجه أن يقول ما لم يساوه لما علمته في مسألة الفساقي وقد قدمنا حكم عرقه.
This is their agreement that according to Zahir al-Riwayah, it does not defile clothing, body, or water, and does not remove hadath. Therefore, it is said in Kashf al-Asrar: The difference is verbal, because whoever says the doubt is in its tahuriyya not its tahara means that the pure object does not become impure by it, and it is necessary to combine it with tayammum, not that there is no doubt in its tahara at all, because the doubt in tahuriyya arises from the doubt in tahara due to conflicting evidences on its purity and impurity. End. With this explanation, the weakness of what al-Hidayah used as evidence is known, for those who say the doubt is in tahuriyya, because if he finds absolute water, he is not obligated to wash his head; obligation is only established by certainty of impurity, and what is established is doubt, so the head does not become impure by doubt, so it is not obligatory. Also known is the weakness of what is in Fatawa Qadikhan, based on the view that the doubt is in tahara: that if it falls into a small quantity of water, it spoils it, because there is no corruption by doubt. In al-Muhit, based on the view that the doubt is in tahuriyya: that if it falls into water, it is permissible to perform wudhu with it as long as it does not overpower, because it is pure but not purifying, like used water according to Muhammad. End. And his washing and carrying it that the leftover water involves necessity contrary to carrying. Consider his statement, 'It does not necessitate impurity of the leftover water for what we have presented,' meaning due to its falling for necessity. His statement, 'That if he finds absolute water etc.' Its explanation, as in some commentaries, is that one who performs wudhu with the doubtful leftover water, if he then has hadath, the hadath has been lifted from the head as well. If he then performs wudhu with absolute water and wipes his head, the moisture of the absolute water on his head is also doubtful because it contacts it, so it does not remove the certain hadath because it is doubtful, and doubt does not remove certainty. Therefore, washing his head would be obligatory for this reason. Since it is not obligatory, it indicates that the doubt is in its tahuriyya, not in its tahara. His statement, 'And also known is the weakness of what is in Fatawa Qadikhan etc.' He said in al-Nahr: A respondent could object to his statement because doubt in tahuriyya does not entail doubt in tahara, contrary to the reverse, as is apparent, so what is in al-Khaniyya has a sound aspect. End. But the author's statement, 'Because there is no corruption by doubt,' the appropriate response is to say: as long as it does not equal it, for what you have learned in the issue of water channels, and we have already presented the ruling on his sweat.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement. The author explains that the apparent disagreement among Hanafi scholars about the cat's su'ur is actually verbal (lafzi), not substantive. All agree on the ruling: it does not defile, nor does it lift hadath without tayammum. The difference is only whether one describes the doubt as being in tahara or tahuriyya. Kashf al-Asrar clarifies that the view that the doubt is in tahuriyya does not deny any doubt in tahara; rather, the doubt in tahuriyya originates from doubt in tahara. The author then refutes the argument from al-Hidayah which tried to prove the doubt is in tahuriyya by saying that if absolute water is available, one does not need to wash the head after using cat su'ur. The refutation shows that the argument fails because the doubt in tahuriyya does not entail certainty of impurity. Similarly, the author critiques the fatwa of Qadikhan that if cat su'ur falls into a small amount of water, it spoils it, arguing that doubt does not corrupt certainty. The passage ends with a response about water channels and sweat, continuing the scholarly debate.

Key Terms
اختلاف لفظي (ikhtilaf lafzi): A verbal disagreement; the dispute is only about wording, not the substantive ruling.
طهارة (tahara): Purity; the state of being ritually clean.
طهورية (tahuriyya): The property of being able to remove hadath (ritual impurity) – i.e., being purifying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the nature of the Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the cat's leftover water?
A) About whether it is pure or impure
B) About whether it is purifying or not
C) A verbal difference only
D) A disagreement about the hadith's authenticity

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ikhtilaf on cat's su'ur is a verbal difference (lafzi) with no practical effect; the ruling is agreed: tahir, not tuhur.

Taharah — Purification

Rulings on Cat's Milk, Donkey Su'ur, and Mule Su'ur
Rulings on purity and consumption of cat's milk and su'ur of donkey and mule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the purity and consumption of cat's milk, donkey's leftover water, and mule's leftover water, and explain the key intra-madhhab disputes and their proofs.

Core Idea
Purity does not automatically imply permissibility; the Hanafi school distinguishes tahara from halal.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a set of rulings on three related taharah issues: the milk of a domestic cat, the leftover water (su'ur) of a donkey, and that of a mule. Each ruling involves intra-Hanafi disputes that test your ability to distinguish between ritual purity (taharah) and permissibility of consumption (halal), and to trace how the lineage of an animal affects its ruling. The author cites proofs from earlier Hanafi masters and resolves the ikhtilaf with a clear mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
First, note that the passage discusses three separate items: cat's milk, donkey su'ur, and mule su'ur. Identify the mufta bihi (relied-upon) ruling for each according to the author: cat's milk is tahir but not halal; donkey su'ur is najis; mule su'ur is najis if mother is donkey, doubtful if mother is horse.
The mufta bihi may differ from the Zahir al-Riwayah position; be attentive to the author's tarjih.
2
Analyze the proof for cat's milk
The passage uses a proof from al-Mabsut (Imam Muhammad) to show that purity and permissibility are not necessarily linked. Examine the analogy: urine of halal-meat animals is pure and permissible to drink, but dung is not permissible to eat even if pure. This illustrates that tahara does not entail halal.
This proof is a qawl of Imam Muhammad, a key Hanafi authority.
3
Examine the dispute on donkey su'ur
Some early Hanafis differentiated between male donkey (himar) and female donkey (atan), claiming the male's mouth becomes impure by smelling urine. The passage rejects this as fanciful and not prevalent. Follow Qadikhan's ruling that there is no difference: both are najis.
This dispute is resolved by the principle that fanciful possibilities do not remove an established ruling.
4
Apply the offspring rule to mule
The mule is the offspring of a donkey and a horse. The general rule is that the offspring follows the mother (al-walad li al-firash). However, if the offspring overwhelmingly resembles the father, the father's ruling takes precedence. For the mule, if the mother is a donkey, its su'ur is najis like a donkey. If the mother is a horse, there is doubt, and the su'ur becomes mashkuk (doubtful).
Al-Zayla'i raised an objection based on maternal lineage, but the author resolves it via resemblance.
5
Synthesize the mufta bihi
Consolidate: For cat's milk, the relied-upon position is tahir but not halal (al-Hidayah). For donkey su'ur, it is najis regardless of gender (Qadikhan). For mule su'ur, if the mother is a donkey, it is najis; if the mother is a horse, it is doubtful (Miraj al-Diraya).
These mufta bihi rulings are derived from later tarjih; earlier positions (e.g., cat's milk as najis) are acknowledged but not operative for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما لبنها فاختار في الهداية أنه طاهر ولا يؤكل وصححه في منية المصلي، وبه اندفع ما في النهاية أنه لم أحد، يرجحه وعن البزدوي أنه يعتبر فيه الكثير الفاحش، وصححه التمرتاشي، وصحح بعضهم أنه نجس نجاسة غليظة وفي المحيط : إنه نجس في ظاهر الرواية ومقتضى القول بطهارته القول بحل أكله وشربه يدل عليه ما في المبسوط : قيل لمحمد لم قلت بطهارة بول ما يؤكل لحمه ولم تقل بطهارة روثه؟ قال : لما قلت بطهارة بوله أبحت شربه، ولو قلت بطهارة روثه لأبحت أكله وأحد لا يقول بها .اهـ. فإن ظاهره أن الطهارة والحل متلازمان يلزم من القول بأحدهما القول بالآخر . ومن المشايخ من قال بنجاسة سؤر الحمار دون الأتان لأن الحمار ينجس فمه بشم البول، وفي البدائع : وهذا غير سديد لأنه أمر موهوم لا يغلب وجوده فلا يؤثر في إزالة الثابت وقال قاضيخان والأصح أنه لا فرق بينهما، ولما ثبت الحكم في الحمار ثبت في البغل لأنه من نسله فيكون بمنزلته. قال الزيلعي : هذا إذا كانت أمه أتاناً فظاهر لأن الأم هي المعتبرة في الحكم، وإن كانت فرساً ففيه إشكال لما ذكرنا أن العبرة للأم ألا ترى أن الذئب لو نزا على شاة فولدت ذئباً حل أكله ويجزئ في الأضحية، فكان ينبغي أن يكون مأكولاً عندهما وطاهراً عند أبي حنيفة اعتبار اللام وفي الغاية : إذا نزا الحمار على الرمكة لا يكره لحم البغل المتولد منهما عند محمد، فعلى هذا لا يصير سؤره مشكوكاً اهـ. الفرس وهي البرذونة تتخذ للنسل. كذا في المغرب. ويمكن الجواب عن الإشكال بأن البغل لما كان متولداً من الحمار والفرس فصار سوره كسور الفرس والحمار فصار مشكوكاً. ذكره في معراج الدراية وغيره، وذكر مسكين في شرح الكتاب سؤالاً فقال : فإن قلت أين ذهب قولك الولد يتبع الأم في الحل والحرمة قلت : ذلك إذا لم يغلب شبهه بالأب أما إذا غلب شبهه فلا أهـ. وبهذا سقط أيضاً إشكال الزيلعي كما لا يخفى. وقال جمال الدين الرازي شارح الكتاب : البغال أربعة : بغل يؤكل بالإجماع وهو المتولد من حمار وحشي وبقرة، وبغل لا يؤكل بالإجماع وهو المتولد من أتان أهلي وفحل، وبغل يؤكل عندهما وهو المتولد من فحل وأتان حمار وحشي، وبغل ينبغي أن يؤكل عندهما وهو المتولد من رمكة وحمار أهلي أهـ وفي النوازل: لا يحل شرب ما شرب منه الحمار.
As for its milk, al-Hidayah preferred that it is pure (tahir) and not eaten, and it was corrected in Munyat al-Musalli. With this, what is in al-Nihaya is repelled: that no one gave preponderance. From al-Bazdawi: that he considers it a gross impurity, and al-Tamartashi corrected it, and some corrected that it is impure with gross impurity. In al-Muhit: it is impure in Zahir al-Riwayah. And the implication of the statement that it is pure leads to saying that its eating and drinking are permissible, as indicated in al-Mabsut: It was said to Muhammad, 'Why did you say that the urine of an animal whose meat is eaten is pure, but did not say that its dung is pure?' He said: 'When I said its urine is pure, I made its drinking permissible. If I said its dung is pure, I would make its eating permissible, and no one says that.' End. So its apparent meaning is that purity and permissibility are concomitant: one entails the other. Among the mashayikh, some said the su'ur of the donkey is impure but not that of the she-donkey, because the donkey's mouth becomes impure by smelling urine. In al-Bada'i: This is not sound because it is a fanciful matter, not prevalent, so it does not remove what is established. Qadikhan said, and the most correct is that there is no difference between them. And when the ruling is established for the donkey, it is established for the mule because it is from its offspring, so it is like it. Al-Zayla'i said: This is if its mother is a she-donkey, then it is apparent because the mother is considered in the ruling. If it is a mare, then there is a problem because we have mentioned that the criterion is the mother. Do you not see that if a wolf mounts a sheep and gives birth to a wolf, its meat is permissible and it suffices for sacrifice? So it should be that it is permissible according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and pure according to Abu Hanifa, considering the mother. In al-Ghayah: if the donkey mounts the mare, the meat of the resulting mule is not disliked according to Muhammad. On this basis, its su'ur does not become doubtful. End. The mare is the burdhuna (pack horse), used for breeding. Thus in al-Mughrib. And it is possible to answer the problem that since the mule is born from a donkey and a mare, its su'ur becomes like the su'ur of a mare and a donkey, so it becomes doubtful. Mentioned in Miraj al-Diraya and others. And Miskeen mentioned in his Sharh of the book a question: 'If you say, where did your statement go that the offspring follows the mother in permissibility and prohibition?' He said: 'That is if it does not overwhelmingly resemble the father. If it does, then no.' End. With this, the problem of al-Zayla'i falls away, as is not hidden. And Jamal al-Din al-Razi, commentator of the book, said: Mules are of four types: a mule that is permissible to eat by consensus, which is born from a wild donkey and a cow; a mule that is not permissible to eat by consensus, which is born from a domestic she-donkey and a stallion; a mule that is permissible to eat according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), which is born from a stallion and a wild she-donkey; and a mule that should be permissible according to them, which is born from a mare and a domestic donkey. End. In al-Nawazil: It is not permissible to drink what the donkey has drunk from.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage contains multiple rulings. First, the cat's milk: al-Hidayah says it is pure (tahir) but not permissible to eat. This is corrected in Munyat al-Musalli. There is disagreement: al-Bazdawi says it is consider a gross impurity, while al-Tamartashi and others correct that it is impure with gross impurity. Al-Muhit says it is impure in Zahir al-Riwayah. The passage notes that purity and permissibility are linked: if something is pure, its consumption is allowed. The example of Muhammad al-Shaybani is cited: he ruled that urine of halal-meat animals is pure and thus drinking it is permissible, but he did not extend that to dung because eating dung is not permissible. Second, the su'ur of the donkey: some scholars differentiate between male and female, but the correct view (as stated by Qadikhan) is that both are impure. Third, the mule: since it is from the donkey's offspring, its su'ur is also impure according to the ruling of its father, but there is a problem if the mother is a mare. The maternal lineage is generally considered, but if the offspring resembles the father, it overrides. The passage ends with a classification of mules by Jamal al-Din al-Razi and a ruling from al-Nawazil that one cannot drink from what a donkey has drunk.

Key Terms
لبن الهرة (laban al-hirra): The milk of a domestic cat
سؤر الحمار (su'ur al-himar): The leftover water of a donkey
سؤر البغل (su'ur al-baghl): The leftover water of a mule
الطهارة والحل (al-tahara wa al-hill): Ritual purity and permissibility of consumption

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between ritual purity (tahara) and permissibility of consumption; cat's milk is pure but not halal, while donkey and mule su'ur are impure (with the mule's status depending on the mother).

The Legal Status of Donkey's Leftover Water (Su'r) in the Hanafi School
Ruling on donkey's leftover water with proof and intra-school dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on donkey's leftover water, explain the intra-school dispute, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Donkey's leftover water is impure in Zahir al-Riwayah, but treated as doubtful in fatwa requiring precaution.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq opens the discussion on the purity of leftover water (su'r) from donkeys and mules. While the outward narration declares it impure, a strong current within the school considers it doubtful (mashkuk), leading to the combined purification method. Understanding this dispute is essential for correctly applying the ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the initial ruling
The passage begins by referencing the ruling on donkey's milk and sweat, then focuses on its leftover water. Note that the initial ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah is that the water is impure.
The ruling extends to mules because they descend from donkeys.
2
Locate the proof from al-Mabsut
Imam Muhammad's reasoning links purity and permissibility: if urine of a halal animal is pure, its drinking is permissible; if dung were pure, eating it would be implied, which is impermissible. Thus, donkey's leftover is impure.
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) based on the link between purity and permissibility.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., al-Bazdawi, al-Tamartashi) consider the leftover pure in large quantities, while others uphold heavy impurity. The passage also mentions a view that only the male donkey's su'r is impure, but al-Bada'i' rejects it.
Qadi Khan affirms no difference between male and female donkeys.
4
Examine the ruling for the mule
Since the mule is born from a donkey and a horse, its leftover water becomes doubtful due to mixed parentage. The text cites classifications by Jamal al-Din al-Razi detailing four types of mules based on parentage and ruling.
Al-Zayla'i raised an issue: if the mother is a mare, the mule should follow the mother's ruling, but the answer relies on predominant resemblance.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative position for fatwa is that the donkey's leftover water is doubtful (mashkuk). This is the basis for the combined method of wudu and tayammum mentioned later.
The tarjih is from Fatawa Qadi Khan and al-Hidayah, preferring the precautionary approach.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
