يعتبر فيه الكثير الفاحش، وصححه التمرتاشي، وصحح بعضهم أنه نجس نجاسة غليظة وفي المحيط : إنه نجس في ظاهر الرواية ومقتضى القول بطهارته القول بحل أكله وشربه يدل عليه ما في المبسوط : قيل لمحمد لم قلت بطهارة بول ما يؤكل لحمه ولم تقل بطهارة روثه؟ قال : لما قلت بطهارة بوله أبحت شربه، ولو قلت بطهارة روثه لأبحت أكله وأحد لا يقول بها .اهـ. فإن ظاهره أن الطهارة والحل متلازمان يلزم من القول بأحدهما القول بالآخر . ومن المشايخ من قال بنجاسة سؤر الحمار دون الأتان لأن الحمار ينجس فمه بشم البول، وفي البدائع : وهذا غير سديد لأنه أمر موهوم لا يغلب وجوده فلا يؤثر في إزالة الثابت وقال قاضيخان والأصح أنه لا فرق بينهما، ولما ثبت الحكم في الحمار ثبت في البغل لأنه من نسله فيكون بمنزلته. قال الزيلعي : هذا إذا كانت أمه أتاناً فظاهر لأن الأم هي المعتبرة في الحكم، وإن كانت فرساً ففيه إشكال لما ذكرنا أن العبرة للأم ألا ترى أن الذئب لو نزا على شاة فولدت ذئباً حل أكله ويجزئ في الأضحية، فكان ينبغي أن يكون مأكولاً عندهما وطاهراً عند أبي حنيفة اعتبار اللام وفي الغاية : إذا نزا الحمار على الرمكة لا يكره لحم البغل المتولد منهما عند محمد، فعلى هذا لا يصير سؤره مشكوكاً اهـ. الفرس وهي البرذونة تتخذ للنسل. كذا في المغرب. ويمكن الجواب عن الإشكال بأن البغل لما كان متولداً من الحمار والفرس فصار سوره كسور فرس الحمار فصار مشكوكاً. ذكره في معراج الدراية وغيره، وذكر مسكين في شرح الكتاب سؤالاً فقال : فإن قلت أين ذهب قولك الولد يتبع الأم في الحل والحرمة قلت : ذلك إذا لم يغلب شبهه بالأب أما إذا غلب شبهه فلا أهـ. وبهذا سقط أيضاً إشكال الزيلعي كما لا يخفى. وقال جمال الدين الرازي شارح الكتاب : البغال أربعة : بغل يؤكل بالإجماع وهو المتولد من حمار وحشي وبقرة، وبغل لا يؤكل بالإجماع وهو المتولد من أتان أهلي وفحل، وبغل يؤكل عندهما وهو المتولد من المتولد من فحل وأتان حمار وحشي، وبغل ينبغي أن يؤكل عندهما وهو المتولد من رمكة وحمار أهلي أهـ وفي النوازل: لا يحل شرب ما شرب منه الحمار. وقال ابن والرمكة هي اختلط بسور بقي وارداً لأنه حيث حكم عليه بالشك في الطهارة كيف يفسد الماء الثابتة طهارته بيقين على أنه مخالف لما ذكره المؤلف أولاً من اتفاقهم أنه على ظاهر الرواية لا ينجس الماء اللهم إلا إن يراد بما في أنه يفسد الماء أي يرفع طهوريته تأمل. ثم رأيت التصريح بهذا للتأويل في التتارخانية معزياً إلى بعض المشايخ. قوله : ( وبه اندفع ما في النهاية الخ) قال في النهر : ولا يخفى أن الدفع إنما يتم على تقدير سبق المنية على الهداية وفيه تردد قوله : (وذكر مسكين في شرح الكتاب الخ) قال . الخانية من في في مقاتل : لا بأس به. قال الفقيه أبو الليث هذا خلاف قول أصحابنا، ولو أخذ إنسان بهذا القول أرجو أن لا يكون به بأس والاحتياط أن لا يشرب كذا في فتح القدير. وفرع في المحيط على كون سؤر الحمار مشكوكاً ما لو اغتسلت بسؤر الحمار تنقطع الرجعة ولا تحل للأزواج لأنه مشكوك فيه فإن كان طاهراً فلا رجعة وإن كان نجساً لم يكن مطهراً فله الرجعة فإذا احتمل انقطعت احتياطاً ولا تحل لغيره احتياطاً اهـ . . يعني قوله (توضأ به وتيمم إن فقد ماء) أي توضأ بسؤرهما وتيمم إن لم يجد ماء مطلقاً . يجمع بينهما، والمراد بالجمع أن لا تخلو الصلاة الواحدة عنهما وإن لم يوجد الجمع في حالة واحدة حتى لو توضأ بسؤر الحمار وصلى ثم أحدث وتيمم وصلى تلك الصلاة أيضاً جاز لأنه جمع بين الوضوء والتيمم في حق صلاة واحدة وهو الصحيح. كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان . فأفاد أن فيها اختلافاً وفي الجامع الصغير للمحبوبي وعن نصير بن يحيى في رجل لم يجد إلا سؤر الحمار قال : يهريق ذلك السؤر حتى يصير عادماً للماء ثم يتيمم. فعرض قوله هذا على القاسم الصفار فقال : هو قول جيد. وذكر محمد في نوادر الصلاة: لو توضأ بسؤر الحمار وتيمم ثم أصاب ماء نظيفاً ولم يتوضأ به حتى ذهب الماء ومعه سؤر الحمار فعليه إعادة التيمم وليس عليه إعادة الوضوء بسؤر الحمار لأنه إذا كان مطهراً فقد توضأ به، وإن كان نجساً فليس عليه الوضوء لا في المرة الأولى ولا في الثانية. كذا في النهاية. وفي الخلاصة : ولو تيمم وصلى ثم أراق سؤر الحمار يلزمه إعادة التيمم والصلاة لأنه يحتمل أن سؤر الحمار كان طهوراً أهـ. فإن قيل ؛ هذا الطريق يستلزم أداء الصلاة بغير طهارة في إحدى المرتين لا محالة وهو مستلزم للكفر لتأديه إلى الاستخفاف بالدين فينبغي أن لا يجوز ويجب الجمع في أداء واحد قلنا : ذلك فيما أدى بغير طهارة بيقين فأما إذا كان أداؤه بطهارة من وجه فلا، لانتفاء الاستخفاف لأنه عمل بالشرع من وجه وههنا كذلك لأن كل واحد من السؤر والتراب مطهر من وجه دون وجه فلا يكون الأداء بغير طهارة من كل وجه فلا يلزم منه الكفر كما لو صلى حنفي بعد الفصد أو الحجامة لا تجوز صلاته ولا يكفر لمكان الاختلاف، وهذا أولى بخلاف ما لو صلى بعد البول. كذا في معراج الدراية . قوله (وأيا قدم صح) أي من المذكورين وهما الوضوء والتيمم أياً بدأ به جاز حتى لو توضأ ثم تيمم جاز بالاتفاق، وإن عكس جاز عندنا خلافاً لزفر لأنه لا يجوز المصير إلى التيمم مع وجود ماء واجب الاستعمال فصار كالماء المطلق ولنا وهو الأصح أن الماء إن كان طهوراً فلا معنى للتيمم، تقدم أو تأخر، وإن لم يكن طهوراً فالمطهر هو التيمم، تقدم أو هو النهر أقول : لو صح ما قاله مسكين لحرم أكل الذئب الذي ولدته الشاة لغلبة شبه الأب وقد مر أنه حلال، وما في المعراج بعدان الاعتبار للام ممنوع والظاهر أن جواز الأكل يستلزم طهارة السؤر .
The aspect is to say: what is not equal to it, because you know it in the issue of aqueducts, and we have already presented the ruling of its sweat. As for its milk, it is chosen in al-Hidayah that it is pure but not eaten, and it was verified in Munyat al-Musalli, and by it is repelled what is in al-Nihayah that it is not [something] I found, preferring it. And from al-Bazdawi that he considers [it] in the case of much excessive [quantity], and al-Tamartashi verified it. And some verified that it is impure with heavy impurity. And in al-Muhit: It is impure in the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah). And the implication of saying it is pure is the saying that eating and drinking it is permissible, as indicated in al-Mabsut: It was said to Muhammad: Why did you say the urine of what is eaten meat is pure but did not say the purity of its dung? He said: When I said its urine is pure, I permitted drinking it, and if I said its dung is pure, I would permit eating it, and no one says that. So its apparent meaning is that purity and permissibility are inseparable, necessitating one from the other. And among the mashayikh, some said the leftover water (su'r) of the donkey is impure but not of the female donkey, because the donkey contaminates its mouth by smelling urine. And in al-Bada'i': This is not sound because it is a hypothetical matter whose existence is not predominant, so it does not affect removing the established [purity]. And Qadi Khan said: The correct is that there is no difference between them. And since the ruling is established for the donkey, it is established for the mule because it is from its offspring, thus it is like it. Al-Zayla'i said: This is if its mother is a female donkey, so it is apparent because the mother is considered in the ruling. But if it is a mare, there is an issue because we mentioned that the consideration is for the mother. Do you not see that if a wolf mounts a sheep and gives birth to a wolf, its meat is permissible and qualifies for sacrifice. So it should be permissible according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and pure according to Abu Hanifa, considering the father. And in al-Ghayah: If the donkey mounts the mare, the meat of the mule resulting from them is not disliked according to Muhammad. Thus, on this, its leftover water is not doubtful. The mare is the one used for breeding. So in al-Maghrib. And it is possible to answer the issue by saying that since the mule is born from a donkey and a mare, its leftover water becomes like the leftover water of a mare and a donkey, so it becomes doubtful. Mentioned in Mi'raj al-Dirayah and others. And Miskin mentioned in his commentary a question and said: If you say, 'Where did your statement go that the child follows the mother in permissibility and prohibition?' I say: That is when its resemblance to the father is not predominant; but if its resemblance to the father is predominant, then not. And by this, the issue of al-Zayla'i also falls. And Jamal al-Din al-Razi, the commentator of the book, said: The mules are four: a mule permissible by consensus, which is born from a wild donkey and a cow; a mule not permissible by consensus, which is born from a domestic female donkey and a stallion; a mule permissible according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), which is born from [the offspring] of a stallion and a female donkey of a wild donkey; and a mule that should be permissible according to them, which is born from a mare and a domestic donkey. And in al-Nawazil: It is not permissible to drink what the donkey has drunk from. And Ibn said: The mare is what mixed with leftover water remained entering because when it is judged as doubtful in purity, how can it spoil water whose purity is established with certainty? This contradicts what the author first mentioned of their agreement that according to Zahir al-Riwayah it does not make water impure, unless it is meant by 'it spoils water' that it removes its purifying property. Then I saw explicit mention of this interpretation in al-Tatarkhaniyah attributed to some mashayikh. His statement: (And by it is repelled what is in al-Nihayah etc.) He said in al-Nahr: It is not hidden that the repelling is only complete on the assumption that al-Munyah preceded al-Hidayah, and there is hesitation. His statement: (And Miskin mentioned in the commentary etc.) He said: al-Khaniyah from in in Muqatil: There is no harm in it. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: This is contrary to the statement of our scholars, and if a person adopts this statement, I hope there is no harm in it, and caution is not to drink. So in Fath al-Qadir. And he branched from al-Muhit on the basis of the donkey's leftover water being doubtful: If a woman performs ghusl with the donkey's leftover water, the right to return (ruj'ah) is cut off and she is not permissible to husbands because it is doubtful. If it is pure, there is no return; if it is impure, it is not purifying, so he has the right to return. So when it is probable, it is cut off as a precaution, and she is not permissible for others as a precaution. He means his statement: (Perform wudu with it and perform tayammum if water is not found), i.e., perform wudu with their leftover water and perform tayammum if he does not find absolute water. He combines them, and the meaning of combining is that a single prayer should not be free from both, even if the combination does not occur in one state. So even if he performs wudu with the donkey's leftover water and prays, then he breaks his wudu and performs tayammum and prays that same prayer, it is permissible because he combined wudu and tayammum for one prayer, and this is the correct view. So in Fatawa Qadi Khan. He indicated that there is difference in it. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir for al-Mahbubi: From Nasir ibn Yahya, regarding a man who finds only the donkey's leftover water, he said: He should spill that leftover water until he becomes devoid of water, then perform tayammum. This statement was presented to al-Qasim al-Saffar, and he said: It is a good statement. And Muhammad mentioned in Nawadir al-Salah: If he performs wudu with donkey's leftover water and performs tayammum, then he finds clean water but does not perform wudu with it until the water is gone and with him is the donkey's leftover water, he must repeat the tayammum and does not have to repeat the wudu with donkey's leftover water because if it is purifying, he has performed wudu with it; if it is impure, he is not required to perform wudu in the first time nor in the second. So in al-Nihayah. And in al-Khulasah: If he performs tayammum and prays, then he spills the donkey's leftover water, he must repeat the tayammum and the prayer because it is probable that the donkey's leftover water was purifying. If it is said: This method necessarily entails performing prayer without purity in one of the two times, and it entails disbelief because it leads to disrespect for the religion, so it should not be permissible, and the combination must be in a single performance. We say: That is when he performs without purity with certainty. But if his performance is with purity from one aspect, then no, because disrespect is not established because he acted according to the Shari'ah from one aspect. And here it is likewise because each of the leftover water and earth is purifying from one aspect and not from another aspect, so the performance is not without purity from every aspect, so disbelief does not follow, just as if a Hanafi prays after phlebotomy or cupping, his prayer is not valid but he does not disbelieve because of the difference of opinion. This is more appropriate, unlike the case if he prays after urination. So in Mi'raj al-Dirayah. His statement: (And whichever he begins, it is valid), i.e., from the two mentioned, which are wudu and tayammum, whichever he begins with is permissible. So even if he performs wudu then tayammum, it is permissible by agreement; and if he reverses, it is permissible according to us, contrary to Zufar, because he does not permit resorting to tayammum in the presence of water that must be used, so it becomes like absolute water. And for us, the correct view is that if the water is purifying, there is no meaning for tayammum, whether it precedes or follows; and if it is not purifying, then the purifier is tayammum, whether it precedes or is: al-Nahr: I say: If what Miskin said were correct, the wolf born from a sheep would be forbidden due to the resemblance to the father, but it has been stated that it is permissible. And what is in al-Mi'raj that the consideration is for the mother is denied, and the apparent is that the permissibility of eating entails the purity of the leftover water.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the rulings related to the leftover water (su'r) of a donkey and its hybrid offspring, the mule, and the method of performing wudu and tayammum when only such doubtful water is available. The text begins by discussing the milk and sweat of a donkey: according to al-Hidayah, donkey's milk is pure but not permissible to drink, though some scholars consider it impure with heavy impurity. The author notes that the ruling on purity and permissibility are linked, as stated by Imam Muhammad in al-Mabsut: if urine of a halal animal is pure, its drinking is permissible; but if dung were pure, it would imply eating it, which no one allows. Then attention turns to the donkey's leftover water. Some early scholars (mashayikh) said only the male donkey's leftover is impure because it contaminates its mouth from smelling urine, but al-Bada'i' rejects this as baseless, and Qadi Khan affirms no difference between male and female. The ruling extends to the mule: since it descends from the donkey, its leftover is like that of the donkey. However, al-Zayla'i raises an issue: if the mother is a mare, the mule should follow the mother's ruling, implying it would be permissible to eat (according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and its leftover pure (according to Abu Hanifa). The text offers several answers: one based on resemblance to the father, another that the mule's leftover becomes doubtful due to mixed parentage. A classification of mules by Jamal al-Din al-Razi is quoted, distinguishing four types based on parentage. The text then addresses a practical branch: if a woman performs ghusl with donkey's leftover water, her right to return (ruj'ah) is severed as a precaution because the water's purity is doubtful. The core ruling comes next: if a person has only donkey's leftover water and no pure water, he must perform both wudu with that water and tayammum, combining them for one prayer. The combination means that one prayer cannot be performed without both acts, though they may occur at different times. For example, if he performs wudu with the leftover, prays, then breaks wudu, performs tayammum, and prays the same prayer again, it is valid. This is from Fatawa Qadi Khan. Another opinion from Nasir ibn Yahya suggests spilling the leftover water to become waterless and then performing tayammum only. Muhammad's Nawadir al-Salah discusses a scenario where after such combination, clean water becomes available: he must repeat the tayammum but not the wudu. An objection arises: this method could lead to praying without complete purity at some point, possibly causing disbelief due to disrespect. The answer is that one is acting according to a valid legal opinion (hanafi), so there is no disbelief, just as praying after phlebotomy (which invalidates wudu according to some) does not cause disbelief because of ikhtilaf. Finally, the text discusses the order: one may begin with either wudu or tayammum; both orders are valid, contrary to Zufar who argues that tayammum is not allowed when any water exists. The Hanafi reasoning is that if the water is purifying, tayammum is meaningless; if not, then tayammum is the actual purifier regardless of order. The passage ends with a criticism from al-Nahr of Miskin's earlier argument about resemblance.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): The leftover water in a vessel after an animal or human drinks from it; the legal status depends on the purity of the drinker.
طهورية (tahuriyyah): The quality of being purifying; water that is both pure and can remove ritual impurity.
مشكوك (mashkuk): Doubtful; a legal category where the purity of something is uncertain, leading to precautionary measures (ihtiyat).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mufta bihi, what is the ruling on donkey's leftover water?
A) Pure and can be used for wudu alone.
B) Impure, so only tayammum is needed.
C) Doubtful, so both wudu with it and tayammum must be performed.
D) Pure only if the donkey is female, otherwise impure.

Key Takeaway
Donkey's leftover water is treated as doubtful in Hanafi fatwa, requiring the combination of wudu and tayammum for prayer.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
The Method of Combining Wudu and Tayammum with Doubtful Water
Practical method of combining wudu and tayammum for doubtful water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method of combining wudu and tayammum when only donkey's leftover water is available, and explain the validity of both orders and the response to the objection of disbelief.

Core Idea
When water is doubtful, perform both wudu with it and tayammum – and either order is valid.

After establishing that donkey's leftover water is doubtful (mashkuk), the text turns to the practical method: the worshipper must perform both wudu (with that water) and tayammum for the same prayer. This lesson unpacks the meaning of 'combining', the permissibility of beginning with either act, and the crucial answer to the objection that such a prayer might involve performing prayer without complete purity.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the required acts
The scenario: a person has only donkey's leftover water and no other water. The text rules that he must perform wudu with that water and also perform tayammum.
The combination is for one single prayer; the two acts need not be simultaneous.
2
Explain the meaning of 'combining' (al-jam')
The combination means that a single prayer cannot be performed without both wudu and tayammum being done for it. For example, if he performs wudu, prays, then breaks wudu, performs tayammum, and prays the same prayer again, it is valid.
The combination is for the same prayer, not for multiple prayers.
3
Analyze the order: which comes first?
The text states 'Whatever he begins with, it is valid' – he may start with either wudu or tayammum. This is contrary to Zufar who argued that tayammum is only allowed when no water at all is available.
The Hanafi reasoning: if the water is purifying, tayammum is irrelevant; if not, tayammum is the actual purifier, so order doesn't matter.
4
Address the objection of disbelief (kufr)
One might object that this method leads to praying without complete purity in one of the two performances, which could be disrespectful and cause disbelief. The answer: the prayer is not done without any purity; each act has a valid aspect (wudu from one perspective, tayammum from another). Acting on a valid legal opinion prevents disbelief.
The analogy: a Hanafi praying after phlebotomy (which some scholars consider nullifies wudu) does not disbelieve because of the ikhtilaf.
5
Consider other opinions on dealing with the water
Some scholars (Nasir ibn Yahya) said to spill the water to become 'waterless' and then perform tayammum only. The text also mentions a case from Nawadir al-Salah: if after combining, clean water becomes available, he must repeat the tayammum but not the wudu.
These show the range of precaution within the school.

بول ما يؤكل لحمه ولم تقل بطهارة روثه؟ قال : لما قلت بطهارة بوله أبحت شربه، ولو قلت بطهارة روثه لأبحت أكله وأحد لا يقول بها .اهـ. فإن ظاهره أن الطهارة والحل متلازمان يلزم من القول بأحدهما القول بالآخر بينهما، ولما ثبت الحكم في الحمار ثبت في البغل لأنه من نسله فيكون بمنزلته. قال الزيلعي : هذا إذا كانت أمه أتاناً فظاهر لأن الأم هي المعتبرة في الحكم، وإن كانت فرساً ففيه إشكال لما ذكرنا أن العبرة للأم ألا ترى أن الذئب لو نزا على شاة فولدت ذئباً حل أكله ويجزئ في الأضحية، فكان ينبغي أن يكون مأكولاً عندهما وطاهراً عند أبي حنيفة اعتبار اللام وفي الغاية : إذا نزا الحمار على الرمكة لا يكره لحم البغل المتولد منهما عند محمد، فعلى هذا لا يصير سؤره مشكوكاً اهـ. الفرس وهي البرذونة تتخذ للنسل. كذا في المغرب. ويمكن الجواب عن الإشكال بأن البغل لما كان متولداً من الحمار والفرس فصار سوره كسور فرس الحمار فصار مشكوكاً. ذكره في معراج الدراية وغيره، وذكر مسكين في شرح الكتاب سؤالاً فقال : فإن قلت أين ذهب قولك الولد يتبع الأم في الحل والحرمة قلت : ذلك إذا لم يغلب شبهه بالأب أما إذا غلب شبهه فلا أهـ. وبهذا سقط أيضاً إشكال الزيلعي كما لا يخفى. وقال جمال الدين الرازي شارح الكتاب : البغال أربعة : بغل يؤكل بالإجماع وهو المتولد من حمار وحشي وبقرة، وبغل لا يؤكل بالإجماع وهو المتولد من أتان أهلي وفحل، وبغل يؤكل عندهما وهو المتولد من المتولد من فحل وأتان حمار وحشي، وبغل ينبغي أن يؤكل عندهما وهو المتولد من رمكة وحمار أهلي أهـ وفي النوازل: لا يحل شرب ما شرب منه الحمار. وقال ابن والرمكة هي اختلط بسور بقي وارداً لأنه حيث حكم عليه بالشك في الطهارة كيف يفسد الماء الثابتة طهارته بيقين على أنه مخالف لما ذكره المؤلف أولاً من اتفاقهم أنه على ظاهر الرواية لا ينجس الماء اللهم إلا إن يراد بما في أنه يفسد الماء أي يرفع طهوريته تأمل. ثم رأيت التصريح بهذا للتأويل في التتارخانية معزياً إلى بعض المشايخ. قوله : ( وبه اندفع ما في النهاية الخ) قال في النهر : ولا يخفى أن الدفع إنما يتم على تقدير سبق المنية على الهداية وفيه تردد قوله : (وذكر مسكين في شرح الكتاب الخ) قال . الخانية من في في مقاتل : لا بأس به. قال الفقيه أبو الليث هذا خلاف قول أصحابنا، ولو أخذ إنسان بهذا القول أرجو أن لا يكون به بأس والاحتياط أن لا يشرب كذا في فتح القدير. وفرع في المحيط على كون سؤر الحمار مشكوكاً ما لو اغتسلت بسؤر الحمار تنقطع الرجعة ولا تحل للأزواج لأنه مشكوك فيه فإن كان طاهراً فلا رجعة وإن كان نجساً لم يكن مطهراً فله الرجعة فإذا احتمل انقطعت احتياطاً ولا تحل لغيره احتياطاً اهـ . . يعني قوله (توضأ به وتيمم إن فقد ماء) أي توضأ بسؤرهما وتيمم إن لم يجد ماء مطلقاً . يجمع بينهما، والمراد بالجمع أن لا تخلو الصلاة الواحدة عنهما وإن لم يوجد الجمع في حالة واحدة حتى لو توضأ بسؤر الحمار وصلى ثم أحدث وتيمم وصلى تلك الصلاة أيضاً جاز لأنه جمع بين الوضوء والتيمم في حق صلاة واحدة وهو الصحيح. كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان . فأفاد أن فيها اختلافاً وفي الجامع الصغير للمحبوبي وعن نصير بن يحيى في رجل لم يجد إلا سؤر الحمار قال : يهريق ذلك السؤر حتى يصير عادماً للماء ثم يتيمم. فعرض قوله هذا على القاسم الصفار فقال : هو قول جيد. وذكر محمد في نوادر الصلاة: لو توضأ بسؤر الحمار وتيمم ثم أصاب ماء نظيفاً ولم يتوضأ به حتى ذهب الماء ومعه سؤر الحمار فعليه إعادة التيمم وليس عليه إعادة الوضوء بسؤر الحمار لأنه إذا كان مطهراً فقد توضأ به، وإن كان نجساً فليس عليه الوضوء لا في المرة الأولى ولا في الثانية. كذا في النهاية. وفي الخلاصة : ولو تيمم وصلى ثم أراق سؤر الحمار يلزمه إعادة التيمم والصلاة لأنه يحتمل أن سؤر الحمار كان طهوراً أهـ. فإن قيل ؛ هذا الطريق يستلزم أداء الصلاة بغير طهارة في إحدى المرتين لا محالة وهو مستلزم للكفر لتأديه إلى الاستخفاف بالدين فينبغي أن لا يجوز ويجب الجمع في أداء واحد قلنا : ذلك فيما أدى بغير طهارة بيقين فأما إذا كان أداؤه بطهارة من وجه فلا، لانتفاء الاستخفاف لأنه عمل بالشرع من وجه وههنا كذلك لأن كل واحد من السؤر والتراب مطهر من وجه دون وجه فلا يكون الأداء بغير طهارة من كل وجه فلا يلزم منه الكفر كما لو صلى حنفي بعد الفصد أو الحجامة لا تجوز صلاته ولا يكفر لمكان الاختلاف، وهذا أولى بخلاف ما لو صلى بعد البول. كذا في معراج الدراية . قوله (وأيا قدم صح) أي من المذكورين وهما الوضوء والتيمم أياً بدأ به جاز حتى لو توضأ ثم تيمم جاز بالاتفاق، وإن عكس جاز عندنا خلافاً لزفر لأنه لا يجوز المصير إلى التيمم مع وجود ماء واجب الاستعمال فصار كالماء المطلق ولنا وهو الأصح أن الماء إن كان طهوراً فلا معنى للتيمم، تقدم أو تأخر، وإن لم يكن طهوراً فالمطهر هو التيمم، تقدم أو هو النهر أقول : لو صح ما قاله مسكين لحرم أكل الذئب الذي ولدته الشاة لغلبة شبه الأب وقد مر أنه حلال، وما في المعراج بعدان الاعتبار للام ممنوع والظاهر أن جواز الأكل يستلزم طهارة السؤر .
The aspect is to say: what is not equal to it, because you know it in the issue of aqueducts, and we have already presented the ruling of its sweat. As for its milk, it is chosen in al-Hidayah that it is pure but not eaten, and it was verified in Munyat al-Musalli, and by it is repelled what is in al-Nihayah that it is not [something] I found, preferring it. And from al-Bazdawi that he considers [it] in the case of much excessive [quantity], and al-Tamartashi verified it. And some verified that it is impure with heavy impurity. And in al-Muhit: It is impure in the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah). And the implication of saying it is pure is the saying that eating and drinking it is permissible, as indicated in al-Mabsut: It was said to Muhammad: Why did you say the urine of what is eaten meat is pure but did not say the purity of its dung? He said: When I said its urine is pure, I permitted drinking it, and if I said its dung is pure, I would permit eating it, and no one says that. So its apparent meaning is that purity and permissibility are inseparable, necessitating one from the other. And among the mashayikh, some said the leftover water (su'r) of the donkey is impure but not of the female donkey, because the donkey contaminates its mouth by smelling urine. And in al-Bada'i': This is not sound because it is a hypothetical matter whose existence is not predominant, so it does not affect removing the established [purity]. And Qadi Khan said: The correct is that there is no difference between them. And since the ruling is established for the donkey, it is established for the mule because it is from its offspring, thus it is like it. Al-Zayla'i said: This is if its mother is a female donkey, so it is apparent because the mother is considered in the ruling. But if it is a mare, there is an issue because we mentioned that the consideration is for the mother. Do you not see that if a wolf mounts a sheep and gives birth to a wolf, its meat is permissible and qualifies for sacrifice. So it should be permissible according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and pure according to Abu Hanifa, considering the father. And in al-Ghayah: If the donkey mounts the mare, the meat of the mule resulting from them is not disliked according to Muhammad. Thus, on this, its leftover water is not doubtful. The mare is the one used for breeding. So in al-Maghrib. And it is possible to answer the issue by saying that since the mule is born from a donkey and a mare, its leftover water becomes like the leftover water of a mare and a donkey, so it becomes doubtful. Mentioned in Mi'raj al-Dirayah and others. And Miskin mentioned in his commentary a question and said: If you say, 'Where did your statement go that the child follows the mother in permissibility and prohibition?' I say: That is when its resemblance to the father is not predominant; but if its resemblance to the father is predominant, then not. And by this, the issue of al-Zayla'i also falls. And Jamal al-Din al-Razi, the commentator of the book, said: The mules are four: a mule permissible by consensus, which is born from a wild donkey and a cow; a mule not permissible by consensus, which is born from a domestic female donkey and a stallion; a mule permissible according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), which is born from [the offspring] of a stallion and a female donkey of a wild donkey; and a mule that should be permissible according to them, which is born from a mare and a domestic donkey. And in al-Nawazil: It is not permissible to drink what the donkey has drunk from. And Ibn said: The mare is what mixed with leftover water remained entering because when it is judged as doubtful in purity, how can it spoil water whose purity is established with certainty? This contradicts what the author first mentioned of their agreement that according to Zahir al-Riwayah it does not make water impure, unless it is meant by 'it spoils water' that it removes its purifying property. Then I saw explicit mention of this interpretation in al-Tatarkhaniyah attributed to some mashayikh. His statement: (And by it is repelled what is in al-Nihayah etc.) He said in al-Nahr: It is not hidden that the repelling is only complete on the assumption that al-Munyah preceded al-Hidayah, and there is hesitation. His statement: (And Miskin mentioned in the commentary etc.) He said: al-Khaniyah from in in Muqatil: There is no harm in it. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: This is contrary to the statement of our scholars, and if a person adopts this statement, I hope there is no harm in it, and caution is not to drink. So in Fath al-Qadir. And he branched from al-Muhit on the basis of the donkey's leftover water being doubtful: If a woman performs ghusl with the donkey's leftover water, the right to return (ruj'ah) is cut off and she is not permissible to husbands because it is doubtful. If it is pure, there is no return; if it is impure, it is not purifying, so he has the right to return. So when it is probable, it is cut off as a precaution, and she is not permissible for others as a precaution. He means his statement: (Perform wudu with it and perform tayammum if water is not found), i.e., perform wudu with their leftover water and perform tayammum if he does not find absolute water. He combines them, and the meaning of combining is that a single prayer should not be free from both, even if the combination does not occur in one state. So even if he performs wudu with the donkey's leftover water and prays, then he breaks his wudu and performs tayammum and prays that same prayer, it is permissible because he combined wudu and tayammum for one prayer, and this is the correct view. So in Fatawa Qadi Khan. He indicated that there is difference in it. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir for al-Mahbubi: From Nasir ibn Yahya, regarding a man who finds only the donkey's leftover water, he said: He should spill that leftover water until he becomes devoid of water, then perform tayammum. This statement was presented to al-Qasim al-Saffar, and he said: It is a good statement. And Muhammad mentioned in Nawadir al-Salah: If he performs wudu with donkey's leftover water and performs tayammum, then he finds clean water but does not perform wudu with it until the water is gone and with him is the donkey's leftover water, he must repeat the tayammum and does not have to repeat the wudu with donkey's leftover water because if it is purifying, he has performed wudu with it; if it is impure, he is not required to perform wudu in the first time nor in the second. So in al-Nihayah. And in al-Khulasah: If he performs tayammum and prays, then he spills the donkey's leftover water, he must repeat the tayammum and the prayer because it is probable that the donkey's leftover water was purifying. If it is said: This method necessarily entails performing prayer without purity in one of the two times, and it entails disbelief because it leads to disrespect for the religion, so it should not be permissible, and the combination must be in a single performance. We say: That is when he performs without purity with certainty. But if his performance is with purity from one aspect, then no, because disrespect is not established because he acted according to the Shari'ah from one aspect. And here it is likewise because each of the leftover water and earth is purifying from one aspect and not from another aspect, so the performance is not without purity from every aspect, so disbelief does not follow, just as if a Hanafi prays after phlebotomy or cupping, his prayer is not valid but he does not disbelieve because of the difference of opinion. This is more appropriate, unlike the case if he prays after urination. So in Mi'raj al-Dirayah. His statement: (And whichever he begins, it is valid), i.e., from the two mentioned, which are wudu and tayammum, whichever he begins with is permissible. So even if he performs wudu then tayammum, it is permissible by agreement; and if he reverses, it is permissible according to us, contrary to Zufar, because he does not permit resorting to tayammum in the presence of water that must be used, so it becomes like absolute water. And for us, the correct view is that if the water is purifying, there is no meaning for tayammum, whether it precedes or follows; and if it is not purifying, then the purifier is tayammum, whether it precedes or is: al-Nahr: I say: If what Miskin said were correct, the wolf born from a sheep would be forbidden due to the resemblance to the father, but it has been stated that it is permissible. And what is in al-Mi'raj that the consideration is for the mother is denied, and the apparent is that the permissibility of eating entails the purity of the leftover water.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the rulings related to the leftover water (su'r) of a donkey and its hybrid offspring, the mule, and the method of performing wudu and tayammum when only such doubtful water is available. The text begins by discussing the milk and sweat of a donkey: according to al-Hidayah, donkey's milk is pure but not permissible to drink, though some scholars consider it impure with heavy impurity. The author notes that the ruling on purity and permissibility are linked, as stated by Imam Muhammad in al-Mabsut: if urine of a halal animal is pure, its drinking is permissible; but if dung were pure, it would imply eating it, which no one allows. Then attention turns to the donkey's leftover water. Some early scholars (mashayikh) said only the male donkey's leftover is impure because it contaminates its mouth from smelling urine, but al-Bada'i' rejects this as baseless, and Qadi Khan affirms no difference between male and female. The ruling extends to the mule: since it descends from the donkey, its leftover is like that of the donkey. However, al-Zayla'i raises an issue: if the mother is a mare, the mule should follow the mother's ruling, implying it would be permissible to eat (according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and its leftover pure (according to Abu Hanifa). The text offers several answers: one based on resemblance to the father, another that the mule's leftover becomes doubtful due to mixed parentage. A classification of mules by Jamal al-Din al-Razi is quoted, distinguishing four types based on parentage. The text then addresses a practical branch: if a woman performs ghusl with donkey's leftover water, her right to return (ruj'ah) is severed as a precaution because the water's purity is doubtful. The core ruling comes next: if a person has only donkey's leftover water and no pure water, he must perform both wudu with that water and tayammum, combining them for one prayer. The combination means that one prayer cannot be performed without both acts, though they may occur at different times. For example, if he performs wudu with the leftover, prays, then breaks wudu, performs tayammum, and prays the same prayer again, it is valid. This is from Fatawa Qadi Khan. Another opinion from Nasir ibn Yahya suggests spilling the leftover water to become waterless and then performing tayammum only. Muhammad's Nawadir al-Salah discusses a scenario where after such combination, clean water becomes available: he must repeat the tayammum but not the wudu. An objection arises: this method could lead to praying without complete purity at some point, possibly causing disbelief due to disrespect. The answer is that one is acting according to a valid legal opinion (hanafi), so there is no disbelief, just as praying after phlebotomy (which invalidates wudu according to some) does not cause disbelief because of ikhtilaf. Finally, the text discusses the order: one may begin with either wudu or tayammum; both orders are valid, contrary to Zufar who argues that tayammum is not allowed when any water exists. The Hanafi reasoning is that if the water is purifying, tayammum is meaningless; if not, then tayammum is the actual purifier regardless of order. The passage ends with a criticism from al-Nahr of Miskin's earlier argument about resemblance.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): The leftover water in a vessel after an animal or human drinks from it; the legal status depends on the purity of the drinker.
مشكوك (mashkuk): Doubtful; a legal category where the purity of something is uncertain, leading to precautionary measures (ihtiyat).
الجمع (al-jam'): The combination of wudu and tayammum for the same prayer, such that the prayer is not performed without both acts having been done for it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Fatawa Qadi Khan, what is the valid order of performing wudu and tayammum when only donkey's leftover water is available?
A) Wudu first, then tayammum.
B) Tayammum first, then wudu.
C) Either order is valid.
D) Both must be done simultaneously.

Key Takeaway
When only donkey's leftover water is available, the mufta bihi is to perform both wudu and tayammum for the same prayer, in either order.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Precautionary Ruling on Ghusl with Donkey's Su'r After Revocable Divorce
Derives a precautionary ruling from doubtful purity of donkey's su'r.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of ihtiyat (precaution) to a case of doubtful purity and state the resulting ruling on revocable divorce and remarriage.

Core Idea
When doubt exists, precaution may sever revocable divorce rights and block remarriage simultaneously.

This passage from al-Muhit presents a legal branch (far') that illustrates how the Hanafi school handles a case of dual uncertainty. A woman who has received a revocable divorce performs ghusl using water left by a donkey (su'r al-himar), whose purity is doubtful. The ruling applies precaution in two opposite directions, affecting both the husband's right of return and the woman's eligibility for other men. Understanding this ruling deepens your grasp of how ihtiyat operates when a single act has two possible legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the doubt
Recognize that the act is ghusl performed with the su'r (leftover water) of a donkey. The key is that this su'r is of doubtful purity in the Hanafi school—its ruling is neither definitively pure nor impure.
Donkey su'r is mashkuk fih (doubtful) according to the relied-upon position.
2
State the two possible legal realities
If the water were pure, the ghusl would be valid and the revocable divorce would become irrevocable (no raj'ah). If it were impure, the ghusl would be invalid and the husband would still have the right to take her back.
This is the foundation of the doubt—two mutually exclusive outcomes.
3
Apply the principle of ihtiyat (precaution)
Since we cannot know which reality holds, precaution is taken in both directions: we treat the ghusl as valid (cutting off raj'ah) to avoid a potentially invalid marriage, and we treat her as still in iddah (not allowing other marriage) to avoid a potentially invalid marriage to another.
This is a double precaution: inqita' (cutting off) for one side, and hurma (forbidding) for the other.
4
Derive the final ruling
The ruling is: the revocable period is considered terminated (so the husband cannot take her back without a new marriage), and she is not permissible for other men (so she must remain in iddah).
This shows that ihtiyat can impose restrictions on both parties simultaneously.
5
Extract the principle of ihtiyat in doubtful acts
Generalize: when a required act (here ghusl for purification from janabah) is performed with a doubtfully pure substance, the effect on linked rights may be resolved through precaution, leaning toward the more restrictive outcome to safeguard the inviolability of marriage.
This principle appears in other fiqh chapters as well.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفرع في المحيط على كون سؤر الحمار مشكوكاً ما لو اغتسلت بسؤر الحمار تنقطع الرجعة ولا تحل للأزواج لأنه مشكوك فيه فإن كان طاهراً فلا رجعة وإن كان نجساً لم يكن مطهراً فله الرجعة فإذا احتمل انقطعت احتياطاً ولا تحل لغيره احتياطاً اهـ
And a branch in al-Muhit based on the su'r of a donkey being doubtful: if a woman performed ghusl with the su'r of a donkey, the revocable divorce is cut off and she is not permissible for other husbands because it is doubtful. For if it is pure, then there is no revocable divorce; and if it is impure, it is not purifying, so he has the revocable divorce. So when it is possible, it is cut off as a precaution, and she is not permissible for others as a precaution. End.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage from al-Muhit discusses a legal branch derived from the doubtful status of the su'r (leftover water) of a donkey. The scenario involves a woman who has been given a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) and then performs ghusl using such water. The ruling is that the revocable period is considered cut off, meaning the husband cannot take her back without a new marriage, and she is not allowed to marry other men either. The reasoning is based on the uncertainty: if the water is pure (tahir), then the ghusl is valid and the divorce becomes irrevocable; if it is impure, the ghusl is invalid and the revocable period remains intact. Since we cannot know which is the case, precaution (ihtiyat) is taken in both directions: we assume the period is cut off to avoid a possible invalid marriage, and we also assume she remains in iddah to avoid a possible valid marriage to someone else. This precautionary approach is typical in cases of doubt in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): The remaining water in a vessel after a person or animal drinks.
رجعة (raj'ah): The right of a husband to take back his wife during the waiting period of a revocable divorce.
احتياط (ihtiyat): Precautionary measure in cases of doubt, leaning towards the more restrictive option to ensure compliance with the Shariah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a revocably divorced woman performs ghusl with the su'r of a donkey, what is the precautionary ruling regarding her revocable period?
A) The revocable period is cut off, so the husband cannot take her back.
B) The revocable period continues, so the husband can take her back.
C) She is free to marry another man immediately.
D) The ghusl is invalid and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
In cases of doubtful purity, Hanafi ihtiyat may impose dual precautionary restrictions, cutting off the husband's reunion rights while also preventing remarriage, to safeguard the inviolability of marriage.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Combining Wudu and Tayammum with Doubtful Su'r of a Donkey
Explains the obligation to combine wudu and tayammum when only doubtful su'r is available.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining wudu and tayammum when only su'r of a donkey is available, and explain the reasoning that either order is valid and the response to the kufr objection.

Core Idea
Precaution requires both wudu and tayammum when water purity is uncertain.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling on purification when only the su'r (leftover water) of a donkey is available. Since the su'r is of doubtful purity, the school obligates combining wudu with that water and tayammum for the same prayer. We will explore what combining means, the dispute over order, and why this practice does not lead to disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognise that when no absolute water is available and only su'r of a donkey (or mule) is present, the Shar'i ruling is that one must perform both wudu with that su'r and tayammum. This is considered wajib (obligatory) as a precaution.
This is the mukharraj position from the six books of Imam Muhammad.
2
Understand the meaning of combining (jam')
The combination does not require both acts to be performed simultaneously. A single prayer must be preceded by both wudu (with su'r) and tayammum at some point. For example, if you prayed after wudu, then had an event, and later performed tayammum and repeated the same prayer, that still counts as combining.
The combination is conceptual, not necessarily sequential at the same moment.
3
Analyse the dispute on order (Zufar vs. the majority)
The majority (including Abu Hanifa) holds that either wudu or tayammum may be performed first. Zufar argues that wudu must precede tayammum, because he considers the su'r equivalent to absolute water whose use is obligatory, thus tayammum is impermissible while that water is available.
The majority responds that the su'r's purity is uncertain, so its obligation is not certain; hence tayammum is allowed.
4
Evaluate the objection of kufr and the response
An objection is raised: combining in two separate performances might lead to praying without valid purification in one of them, which could be mockery and cause kufr. The response is that since both wudu (if su'r is pure) and tayammum (if su'r is impure) are valid purification from one aspect, there is no certainty of praying without purification, so no kufr. This is analogous to a Hanafi praying after phlebotomy.
The principle is that acting upon a valid scholarly opinion, even if mistaken, prevents kufr.

His statement (Perform wudu with it and perform tayammum if he loses water): meaning perform wudu with their su'r and perform tayammum if he finds no absolute water. He combines between them. The meaning of combining is that a single prayer is not devoid of them, even if the combination does not occur in one state. So if he performed wudu with the su'r of a donkey and prayed, then had an event, and performed tayammum and prayed that same prayer again, it is permissible because he combined wudu and tayammum with respect to one prayer, and this is the correct view. Thus in Fatawa Qadikhan. So it indicates that there is difference in it. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir of al-Mahbubi, from Nasir ibn Yahya regarding a man who finds only the su'r of a donkey: he said, "He should spill that su'r until he becomes devoid of water, then perform tayammum." This statement was presented to al-Qasim al-Saffar, and he said, "It is a good statement." And Muhammad mentioned in Nawadir al-Salah: If he performed wudu with the su'r of a donkey and performed tayammum, then found clean water and did not perform wudu with it until the water was gone and he had the su'r of a donkey, he must repeat the tayammum and he is not required to repeat the wudu with the su'r of the donkey because if it is purifying, he has already performed wudu with it, and if it is impure, he is not required to perform wudu neither the first time nor the second. Thus in al-Nihayah. And in al-Khulasah: If he performed tayammum and prayed, then spilled the su'r of the donkey, he must repeat the tayammum and the prayer because it is possible that the su'r of the donkey was purifying. End. If it is said: this method necessarily leads to performing prayer without purification in one of the two times, which leads to disbelief (kufr) because it leads to mockery of the religion; therefore it should not be permissible and combination must be in a single performance. We say: That is the case when he performs without purification with certainty. As for when he performs it with purification from one aspect, then no [kufr], because there is no mockery since he acted according to the Shariah from one aspect. And here it is similar because each of the su'r and the dust is purifying from one aspect and not from another, so the performance is not without purification from every aspect, so it does not lead to kufr. This is similar to when a Hanafi prays after phlebotomy or cupping: his prayer is not valid but he is not a disbeliever due to the difference of opinion. This is more appropriate, unlike the case if he prays after urination. Thus in Mi'raj al-Dirayah. His statement (Whichever he begins, it is valid): meaning from the two mentioned, namely wudu and tayammum, whichever he begins with, it is permissible. So if he performed wudu then tayammum, it is permissible by agreement, and if he reversed, it is permissible according to us, contrary to Zufar, because it is not permissible to resort to tayammum when there is water whose use is obligatory, so it becomes like absolute water. Our proof (and it is the most correct) is that if the water is purifying, there is no meaning for tayammum, whether it comes before or after; and if it is not purifying, then the purifier is tayammum, whether it comes before or after. The existence and non-existence of this water are of the same degree. The combination is only due to lack of certain knowledge of which is the purifier, so precaution is in combining, not in ordering. Similarly, the difference in performing ghusl with it: according to us, it is not required to precede it, contrary to him, but the preference is to precede wudu and ghusl with it according to us. And in al-Khulasah: They differed regarding the intention in wudu with the su'r of a donkey, and the precaution is to intend. End.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq comments on the matn from Kanz al-Daqaiq: 'Perform wudu with it and perform tayammum if he loses water.' The commentator explains that when a person only has the su'r (leftover water) of a donkey or mule, which is doubtful in purity, he must perform both wudu with that water and tayammum for the same prayer. The combination means that a single prayer is not devoid of either purification method, even if they are performed at different times (e.g., wudu then prayer, then later tayammum for the same prayer after an event). This is the correct view according to the Hanafi school, though there is disagreement. Some scholars like Nasir ibn Yahya recommend spilling the su'r to become devoid of water and then performing tayammum only. Imam Muhammad mentions in Nawadir al-Salah that if after performing wudu and tayammum, one finds pure water, he must repeat the tayammum but not the wudu. The passage then addresses an objection: combining wudu and tayammum might lead to praying without valid purification in one of the two prayers, which could be tantamount to disbelief. The response is that since each method is considered purifying from one aspect (wudu if the water is pure, tayammum if it is impure), there is no certainty of praying without purification, so it is not disbelief. This is similar to the case of a Hanafi praying after phlebotomy (a difference of opinion on its nullification of wudu). Regarding the order, the school holds that either wudu or tayammum may come first, contrary to Zufar who requires wudu first. The preferred order is to perform wudu first. The passage concludes with a note on intention: it is precautionary to make an intention for wudu when using the su'r.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): The remaining water in a vessel after a person or animal drinks.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with pure earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or cannot be used.
جمع (jam'): Performing both wudu and tayammum for the same prayer, not necessarily simultaneously.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person performs tayammum first, then wudu with the su'r of a donkey, for the same prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid because wudu must precede tayammum.
B) The prayer is valid according to the majority, but invalid according to Zufar.
C) The prayer is invalid because tayammum cannot be after wudu.
D) The person must repeat both acts in the correct order.

Key Takeaway
When water purity is doubtful, the Hanafi school requires combining wudu (with that water) and tayammum, and either order is valid.

Taharah — Purification

Principles for Conflicting Reports on Purity and Permissibility
Distinguishes three scenarios of conflicting testimonies and explains the legal principle behind each.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of istishab to resolve conflicting testimonies about purity and permissibility, and distinguish the rulings for meat, water, and food based on their original states before the reports.

Core Idea
When two reports conflict and cancel out, the pre-report original state governs: permissibility stays, prohibition stays.

This cautionary note from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents three scenarios where two trustworthy reports conflict: meat (Magian vs Muslim slaughter), water (impure vs pure), and food (haram vs halal). At first glance, they might seem similar, but the Hanafi jurists derive different rulings based on the original state (istishab) before the reports. Understanding this principle is essential for any mufti or student dealing with contradictory evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting reports
Read each scenario: what are the two conflicting testimonies? For meat: one says Magian slaughter, one says Muslim slaughter. For water: one says impure, one says pure. For food: one says halal, one says haram.
All involve two trustworthy (adil) witnesses.
2
Determine the original state before the reports
Ask: what was the legal status of the item before any report came? For water and food, the original default is permissibility (ibaha). For meat before slaughter, the original default is prohibition (because meat is not halal without proper slaughter).
This is the key differentiator.
3
Apply the principle of istishab
Since the two reports cancel each other out (tasqut), we return to the original state. For water: permissibility and purity remain → water is ruled pure. For food: permissibility remains → ruled halal. For meat: prohibition remains → ruled not permissible to eat.
The original state is preserved because certainty is not removed by doubt.
4
Consider the refinement by al-Khabbazi
For the water case, al-Khabbazi suggests that the witness reporting purity may have knowledge of the water source (e.g., flowing river) that could preponderate his report. If he can provide a basis, his report is given weight, avoiding conflict. If not, impurity may be preferred.
This intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf shows that the principle is applied flexibly.
5
Distinguish the meat case from the other two
The meat case differs because the original state before the reports is prohibition (not permissibility). Thus, even though the reports cancel, the prohibition remains. This is why the ruling is different from water and food.
Always ask: what was the default before the evidence arrived?

والثابت قبله حرمة الأكل لأنه إنما يحل أكله بالذبح شرعاً، وإذا لم يثبت السبب المبيح لوقوع التعارض في سبب الإباحة بقي حراماً كما كان فظهر الفرق بين الثلاث، لكن ذكر الإمام جلال الدين الخبازي في حاشية ثمة لأنه أمكن ترجيح أحدهما فإن المخبر عن الطهارة لو استقصى الأشياء قوله : (تقليلاً للنسخ الذي هو خلاف الأصل) بيانه أن قبل البعثة كان الأصل في الإباحة فلو جعلنا المبيح متأخراً يلزم تكرار النسخ لأن Cautionary note: In it are three issues: The first is what we presented: if a trustworthy person reports that this meat is from the sacrifice of a Magian, and another trustworthy person reports that it is from the sacrifice of a Muslim, then it is not permissible to eat it. The second is what we presented: if a trustworthy person reports the impurity of water and another trustworthy person reports its purity, then rulings of purity are applied. The third is what Muhammad mentioned in Kitab al-Istihsan, as transmitted in al-Tawshih: if a trustworthy person reports the permissibility of a food and another reports its prohibition, then it is ruled permissible. This cautionary note is to explain the difference between the three, as they might be confused. The principle in them is that when two reports conflict, they cancel each other out, and what was established before the reports remains as it was. So in the case of water, before the report, the established fact was the permissibility of drinking it and its purity. When the two proofs conflict, they cancel each other out, and what remains is the permissibility and purity. Similarly for food, because the original ruling is permissibility, so it must be acted upon. If the side of prohibition were preferred, that would require preferring one of two equals without a preponderator, while abandoning the original ruling. It is not permissible to prefer prohibition by precaution because it necessitates disbelieving the report of permissibility without evidence. As for when proofs of Shariah conflict regarding permissibility and prohibition of food, that necessitates preferring prohibition to minimize abrogation (naskh), which is contrary to the original [principle], and to act by precaution, which is the original in matters of religion when there is no impediment. As for the first meat issue, when the two proofs also cancel each other by conflict, what remains is what was established before slaughter. And what was established before it was the prohibition of eating, because it only becomes permissible by slaughter according to Shariah. When the cause of permissibility is not established due to conflict regarding the cause of permissibility, it remains prohibited as it was. Thus the difference between the three becomes clear. But Imam Jalal al-Din al-Khabbazi mentioned in his gloss on al-Hidayah a fine detail regarding the water issue that puts the soul at rest and the heart inclines to it. He said: if it is said: when a trustworthy person reports the impurity of water and another trustworthy person reports its purity, why does the water not become doubtful given the conflict between the two reports? We say: There is no conflict there because it is possible to give preponderance to one, since the one reporting purity, if he investigated things... His statement (to minimize abrogation which is contrary to the original): its explanation is that before the [Prophet's] mission, the original [principle] was permissibility. So if we make the permissibility later, it necessitates repeating abrogation because the prohibition abrogates the original permissibility, then the permissibility abrogates the prohibition. And if we make the prohibition later, it necessitates only one abrogation, because the permissibility is to remain on the original permissibility, and the prohibition abrogates it, and the original principle is no repetition. And there is extended discussion on this in our commentaries on Sharh al-Manar. His statement: (But Imam Jalal al-Din mentioned...) I say: Sadr al-Shariah followed him in al-Tanqih. And in the Tahrir of the investigator Ibn al-Humam, it is necessary to ask about his basis to act accordingly if questioning is not difficult. The expression of Sadr al-Shariah is: 'If one reports the purity and impurity of water, then purity [is given], even though it is a negation, but it is possible that he knows by evidence, so he is asked; if he explains the face of his proof, it is like affirmation, if he does not explain, then impurity is preponderant.' And it is said in al-Tawdih: 'This is similar to...'
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This cautionary note (tanbih) from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the legal principle behind three scenarios where two trustworthy reports conflict. The first scenario is meat: one witness says it is from a Magian sacrifice, another says it is from a Muslim sacrifice. The ruling is that it is not permissible to eat. The second scenario is water: one witness says it is impure, another says it is pure. The ruling is that it is considered pure. The third scenario is food: one witness says it is halal, another says haram. The ruling is that it is considered halal. The key to understanding the difference is the principle: when two reports cancel each other out, we return to the original state (istishab) before the reports. For water and food, the original state is permissibility (ibaha), so we stay on that. For meat, the original state before slaughter is prohibition (because meat is not permissible without valid slaughter), so we stay on prohibition. The passage then discusses a refinement by Imam Jalal al-Din al-Khabbazi regarding the water issue: he argues that there is no real conflict because the witness reporting purity can be cross-examined about his knowledge; if he can provide a basis (e.g., seeing the water from a spring), his report is given weight. If not, then impurity is preponderant. Sadr al-Shariah and Ibn al-Humam also discuss this. The passage ends with a note about abrogation (naskh) in the context of conflicting Shariah proofs on halal/haram: to minimize abrogation, prohibition is preferred.

Key Terms
تعارض (ta'arud): Conflict between two evidence (reports or proofs) that are equal in strength.
استصحاب (istishab): Presumption of continuity of a ruling or state until evidence indicates change.
احتياط (ihtiyat): Precautionary measure; preferring the more restrictive ruling in cases of doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of conflicting reports about meat from a Magian vs. Muslim slaughter, what is the original state before the reports that determines the ruling?
A) Permissibility, because all meat is originally halal.
B) Prohibition, because meat is not permissible without valid slaughter.
C) Doubt, because we have no knowledge of the slaughter.
D) Permissibility, because the majority of slaughterers are Muslims.

Key Takeaway
When two trustworthy reports conflict and cancel each other, the ruling returns to the original state (istishab): permissibility for water and food, prohibition for meat before valid slaughter.

The Principle of Ta'āruḍ and Istishāb: When Conflicting Reports Cancel and the Original Prevails
Explaining three cases of conflicting reports and the principle of retaining the original state

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for three cases of conflicting reports on purity and food, and apply the principle that the original state remains when proofs cancel.

Core Idea
Conflicting reports cancel; the pre-existing ruling (original) remains.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq illustrates how Hanafi law resolves contradictory testimony in matters of purity and food. The key principle is ta‘āruḍ (conflict) and suqūṭ (falling): when two reliable reports contradict each other without preponderance, both are discarded, and the original state before the reports is restored. We examine three distinct cases—meat, water, and food—to see how this principle works and why the outcomes differ.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three cases
Locate the three scenarios in the text: (1) meat reported as slaughter of a Magian vs. Muslim, (2) water reported as impure vs. pure, (3) food reported as forbidden vs. permissible.
Each case involves two ʿadl witnesses giving opposing reports.
2
State the ruling for each
From the passage: (1) meat is not eaten, (2) water is ruled pure, (3) food is ruled permissible. Write down these outcomes.
3
Apply the principle of taʿāruḍ and suqūṭ
In each case, the two reports conflict, so they both fall (tasāqaṭā). What remains is the original ruling (al-aṣl) that existed before the reports. For water and food, the original is permissibility (ibāḥa). For meat, the original is prohibition because before lawful slaughter, meat is not halal.
The original state differs because meat requires a specific cause (sabab) for permissibility, while water and food have general permissibility.
4
Distinguish the meat case from water/food
The meat case: before the conflicting reports, the meat was not proven to be slaughtered Islamically, so the original is prohibition. In water and food, the original is permissibility because no prior prohibition existed.
The passage explicitly warns against confusing the three cases.
5
Consider the refinement by al-Khabbazi
Imam Jalal al-Din al-Khabbazi adds that if the witness for purity can explain his evidence (e.g., direct observation), his report may be preferred over the report of impurity. If he cannot explain, the original (purity) prevails. Sadr al-Shariʿa and Ibn al-Humam provide similar details.
This refinement applies when one report is based on sense perception (mushāhadah) and the other on istiṣḥāb.

وعبارة صدر الشريعة هكذا إذا أخبر بطهارة الماء ونجاسته فالطهارة، وإن كانت نفياً لكنه يحتمل المعرفة بالدليل فيسأل؛ فإن بين وجه دليله كان كالإثبات وإن لم يبين فالنجاسة أولى. وقال في التوضيح: هذا نظير في Delayed... and the existence of this water and its absence are equal, but they are combined due to lack of knowledge of which is purifying; thus caution is in combining, not ordering. Similarly the difference in bathing with it: according to us, precedence is not necessary, contrary to him, but it is better to perform wudu and bathe with it according to us. In al-Khulasa: they differed regarding intention in wudu with the leftover of a donkey; the precaution is to intend. End. (Note) In it are three issues: First: what we mentioned earlier: if a reliable witness reports that this meat is the slaughter of a Magian and another reliable witness reports that it is the slaughter of a Muslim, then it is not permissible to eat it. Second: what we mentioned earlier: if a reliable witness reports the impurity of water and another reliable witness reports its purity, then it is ruled pure. Third: what Muhammad mentioned in Kitab al-Istihsan, as quoted in al-Tawshih: if a reliable witness reports the permissibility of food and another its prohibition, then it is ruled permissible. This note is to clarify the difference between the three, for they may be confused. The principle in them is that when two reports conflict, they both fall, and what was established before the report remains as it was. For water, before the report, the established permissibility of drinking and purity; when the two proofs conflict, they both fall, and what remained of permissibility and purity. For food likewise, because the original is permissibility, so action upon it is obligatory. For if the side of prohibition prevailed, it would require preferring one of two equals without a preponderator while abandoning the original; it is not permissible to prefer prohibition by precaution because it necessitates denying the report of permissibility without proof. But as for conflicting legal proofs regarding permissiblity and prohibition of food, it requires preferring prohibition to minimize abrogation, which is contrary to the original, and as a precaution, which is the original in religious matters when there is no obstacle. As for the first meat case, when the two proofs fell due to conflict, what was established before slaughter remained; established before it was prohibition of eating, because it is only made permissible by slaughter legally. When the permissive cause is not established due to conflict in the cause of permissibility, it remains prohibited as before; so the difference between the three became clear. However, Imam Jalal al-Din al-Khabbazi mentioned in Hashiyat al-Hidayah a good detail regarding the water case that satisfies the soul and inclines the heart. He said: If it is said: when a reliable witness reports impurity of water and another reports its purity, why does the water not become doubtful with the conflict between the two reports? We say: there is no conflict there because it is possible to preponderate one; for the one reporting purity, if he investigates thoroughly... His statement: (to minimize abrogation which is contrary to the original). Its explanation: before the prophetic mission, the original was permissibility. If we make the permissive later, it necessitates repeated abrogation because the prohibitive abrogates the original permissibility, then the permissive abrogates the prohibitive. If we make the prohibitive later, it only requires one abrogation because the permissive maintains the original permissibility and the prohibitive is an abrogator; the original is absence of repetition. There is detailed discussion in our glosses on Sharh al-Manar. His statement: (But Imam Jalal al-Din mentioned...). I say: Sadr al-Shari'a followed this in al-Tanqih. In Tahrir of Ibn al-Humam, it is necessary to ask about its basis to act accordingly if asking is not difficult. The expression of Sadr al-Shari'a is thus: If one reports purity of water and another its impurity, then purity [is preferred] even if it is a negation, but it may be based on knowledge by evidence; so ask. If he explains the basis of his evidence, it is like affirmation; if he does not explain, impurity is better. In al-Tawdih it is said: This is similar to that where he said: I took this water from the river and closed the mouth of this vessel, and nothing mixed with it at all - we prefer his report for being supported by the original. If his report is based on istishab and he said it was pure and remains so, we prefer the report of impurity because he reported on a tangible thing observed, and that preponderates over istishab. End. What appears to me is that the words of the scholars are to be carried on the case where he does not explain the basis of his report; if he does not explain, one acts on the original, which is purity; if he explains, then the criterion is this detail.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the ruling regarding conflicting testimonies on purity and food, based on the principle of istishab (presumption of continuity). The author begins by discussing a prior issue about combining water due to caution, then moves to a note (تنبيه) containing three specific rulings. In the first, if one reliable witness says meat is from a Magian's slaughter and another says from a Muslim's, the meat is not eaten because the original state before slaughter is prohibition. In the second, if one reports water impure and another pure, the water is ruled pure because the original is permissibility. In the third, if one reports food permissible and another prohibited, it is ruled permissible because the original is permissibility. The unifying principle: when two reports conflict, they cancel each other out, and the previous ruling (the original) remains. The author then explains the difference between these cases: in the meat case, the original before the conflicting reports is prohibition (since slaughter was not yet proven), while in water and food, the original is permissibility. A detailed refinement from Imam Jalal al-Din al-Khabbazi is quoted, explaining that if the witness for purity can show his evidence (e.g., direct observation), his testimony may be preferred; otherwise, the original prevails. Sadr al-Shari'a's view is similar: ask the witnesses for their basis; if they provide evidence, act on it; if not, prefer impurity for water because it is based on a tangible observation, which preponderates over istishab. The comment concludes that the scholars' statements should be understood as when the basis is not explained; if explained, follow the detail.

Key Terms
تعارضا (ta'āraḍā): When two reports or proofs conflict and oppose each other such that they cannot both be true or acted upon.
تساقطا (tasāqaṭā): They both fall; the legal effect of both conflicting evidences is nullified, and the original state (al-aṣl) remains.
الأصل (al-aṣl): The original state or ruling that existed before the conflicting reports; a foundational principle (istishāb).
الاستصحاب (al-istishāb): Presumption of continuity: a ruling remains unchanged until a change is proven.
عدل (ʿadl): A reliable, upright witness whose testimony is legally acceptable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a reliable witness reports water to be impure and another reliable witness reports it to be pure, what is the Hanafi ruling according to the simple principle (before the refinement)?
A) The water is ruled impure because the report of impurity is based on tangible observation.
B) The water is ruled pure because the original state is purity.
C) The water becomes doubtful and tayammum is required.
D) The two reports cancel out and the water is considered impure by caution.

Key Takeaway
When conflicting testimonies cancel, the original ruling (istishāb) governs, whether it is permissibility or prohibition.
