Wudu with Nabidh al-Tamar: Definition, Timing, and Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Combining
Commentary defining nabidh and discussing timing and three narrations on combining

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of nabidh al-tamar, identify the three narrations from Abu Hanifa regarding combining it with tayammum, and explain the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Core Idea
Wudu with nabidh al-tamar is a unique rukhsa; it is permitted only when water is absent and only with date-nabidh, not other nabidhs.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the phrase 'contrary to nabidh al-tamar' in Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author clarifies that when absolute water is unavailable, one may perform wudu with nabidh al-tamar without combining tayammum — unlike the case of a donkey's leftover. The discussion is structured into three parts: definition, timing, and ruling. We will focus on the definitional conditions and the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether to also perform tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Define nabidh al-tamar
Identify the three conditions: it must be thin, sweet, non-intoxicating, and uncooked. Note that if cooked or intoxicating, wudu with it is invalid.
The definition is critical because other nabidhs (raisin, honey) are not permitted.
2
Understand the timing condition
Abu Hanifa rules that wudu with nabidh is permissible only when tayammum itself is permissible (i.e., when water is absent and the person is in a situation where tayammum is allowed).
If tayammum is not allowed (e.g., at home with a valid excuse?), then nabidh cannot be used.
3
Identify the three narrations from Abu Hanifa
The passage mentions the first narration: perform wudu and also perform tayammum. The second and third narrations are not fully stated here but are known in the school.
The author of Kanz explicitly rules against combining, which becomes the mufta bihi.
4
Analyze the dispute on combining
Muhammad al-Shaybani (according to some reports) held that one must combine wudu with tayammum due to doubt about the purity of nabidh. The commentator explains why the author rejects this.
The thamarah al-khilaf: if you follow the first narration, you do two acts; if you follow the author, you do only wudu.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a traveler who has only date-nabidh and no water: what is the Hanafi ruling? Perform wudu with it without tayammum (mufta bihi).
If water becomes available later, wudu with nabidh is invalidated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (بخلاف نبيذ التمر) يعني إن فقد ماء مطلقاً ولم يجد إلا نبيذ التمر فإنه يتوضأ ولا يجمع بينه وبين التيمم، وذكر هذه المسألة هنا إما لأنه مما يجوز الوضوء به على رأي أو لأن محمداً لما أوجب الجمع صار عنده مشكوكاً فيه فشابه سؤر الحمار . كذا قيل لكن لا يخفى ضعف الثاني لأن المصنف جعله مخالفاً لسؤر الحمار . ثم اعلم أن الكلام ههنا في ثلاثة مواضع الأول في تفسيره الثاني في وقته الثالث في حكمه. أما الأول فهو أن يلقي في الماء تميرات فيصر رقيقاً يسيل على الأعضاء حلواً غير مسكر ولا مطبوخ. وإنما قلنا حلواً لأنه لو توضأ به قبل خروج الحلاوة يجوز بلا خلاف وإنما قلنا غير مسكر لأنه لو كان مسكراً لا يجوز الوضوء به بلا خلاف لأنه حرام، وإنما قلنا غير مطبوخ لأنه لو طبخ فالصحيح أنه لا يتوضأ به إذ النار قد غيرته حلواً كان أو مشتداً كمطبوخ الباقلاء كذا في المبسوط والمحيط يعني بلا خلاف بین الثلاثة الأليق بما قدمناه وهو أن الماء من يصير مقيداً بالطبخ إذا لم يقصد به المبالغة في التنظيف وبه يظهر ضعف ما صححه في المفيد والمزيد أنه يجوز الوضوء به بعدما طبخ. وقد ذكر الزيلعي أن صاحب الهداية وقع منه تناقض فإنه ذكر هنا أن النار إذا غيرته يجز الوضوء به عند أبي حنيفة لجواز شربه، وذكر في بحث المياه أنه لا يجوز الوضوء بما تغير بالطبخ أهـ. ولا يخفى ثبوت الخلاف في هذه المسألة لأن اختلاف التصحيح ينبئ عنه فكان فيه روايتان، فيحتمل أن يكون مراد صاحب الهداية نقل الرواية في الموضعين فلا تناقض حيث أمكن التوفيق، وأما سائر الأنبذة فإنه لا يجوز الوضوء بها عند عامة العلماء وهو الصحيح لأن جواز التوضؤ بنبيذ التمر ثابت بخلاف القياس بالحديث ولهذا لا يجوز عند القدرة على الماء المطلق فلا يقاس عليه غيره. كذا في غاية البيان. وأما الثاني قال أبو حنيفة : كل وقت يجوز التيمم فيه يجوز التوضؤ به وإلا فلا. كذا في معراج الدراية. وأما الثالث ففيه ثلاث روايات عن أبي حنيفة : الأولى وهو قوله الأول أنه يتوضأ به جزماً ويضيف التيمم إليه
His statement: (Contrary to nabidh al-tamar) means that if one completely lacks water and finds only nabidh al-tamar, he performs wudu with it and does not combine it with tayammum. This issue is mentioned here either because it is permissible to perform wudu with it in one view, or because Muhammad, when he obliged combining, it became doubtful in his view and thus resembled the leftover of a donkey. So it is said, but the weakness of the second is not hidden because the author made it contrary to the leftover of a donkey. Then know that the discussion here is on three points: first, its definition; second, its timing; third, its ruling. As for the first: it is that dates are thrown into water so that it becomes thin, flowing over the limbs, sweet, non-intoxicating, and uncooked. We said sweet because if he performs wudu with it before the sweetness emerges, it is permissible without dispute. We said non-intoxicating because if it were intoxicating, wudu with it is not permissible without dispute because it is forbidden. We said uncooked because if it is cooked, the correct view is that wudu with it is not permissible because fire has changed it, whether sweet or strong, like cooked beans. So in al-Mabsut and al-Muhit: meaning without dispute among the three [imams], more appropriate to what we have presented: that water becomes restricted by cooking if it is not intended for excessive cleaning. By this, the weakness of what was declared correct in al-Mufid and al-Mazid appears: that wudu with it after cooking is permissible. Al-Zayla'i mentioned that the author of al-Hidayah fell into contradiction: he mentioned here that if fire changes it, wudu with it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa because drinking it is permissible, and he mentioned in the discussion of waters that wudu with what is changed by cooking is not permissible. End. The existence of disagreement in this issue is not hidden because the difference in correction indicates it; thus there are two narrations. It is possible that the intention of the author of al-Hidayah is to transmit the narration in both places, so there is no contradiction where reconciliation is possible. As for other nabidhs, wudu with them is not permissible according to the generality of scholars, and that is correct because the permissibility of wudu with nabidh al-tamar is established contrary to analogy by hadith, and thus it is not permissible when one has access to absolute water, so others are not analogized to it. So in Ghayat al-Bayan. As for the second: Abu Hanifa said: Every time tayammum is permissible, wudu with it is permissible; otherwise not. So in Mi'raj al-Diraya. As for the third: there are three narrations from Abu Hanifa: the first is his initial statement that he performs wudu with it absolutely and adds tayammum to it.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the Kanz al-Daqa'iq phrase 'بخلاف نبيذ التمر' (contrary to nabidh al-tamar). The author explains that when no absolute (mutlaq) water is available, one may perform wudu with nabidh al-tamar (date liquor) and does not combine it with tayammum. This is different from the case of the donkey's leftover water, where combining is prescribed. The discussion is structured into three parts: definition, timing, and ruling. Definition: nabidh al-tamar is made by soaking dates in water until it becomes thin, sweet, non-intoxicating, and uncooked. If it becomes intoxicating, it is haram and cannot be used. If cooked, the correct view (al-sahih) is that it is not permissible because fire changes its nature, except perhaps if the fire is not intended for cleaning. The permissibility of using cooked nabidh is disputed among later authorities. Timing: Abu Hanifa rules that wudu with nabidh is only permissible when tayammum would be permissible (i.e., when water is absent and travel or illness allows tayammum). If tayammum is not permitted (e.g., because one is at home with no valid excuse), then nabidh cannot be used. Ruling: there are three narrations from Abu Hanifa. The first narration (initial view) is that one performs wudu with it absolutely and also performs tayammum (i.e., combines the two). The second and third narrations are not fully given in this passage but the author hints at a difference of opinion. The passage also clarifies that other nabidhs (e.g., from raisins, honey) are not permitted for wudu, as the hadith only specifies date nabidh, and analogy does not extend it.

Key Terms
نبيذ التمر (nabīdh al-tamar): A liquid made by soaking dates in water until it becomes thin and sweet; it is not intoxicating and not cooked.
سؤر الحمار (su'ru al-ḥimār): The leftover water from a donkey's drinking, which is considered pure but requires combining with tayammum for wudu.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with earth as a substitute for wudu when water is unavailable or harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on performing wudu with cooked nabidh al-tamar (dates that have been boiled)?
A) It is permissible because cooking does not change its legal status.
B) It is not permissible because fire has changed its nature, similar to cooked beans.
C) It is permissible at all times, like uncooked nabidh.
D) It is permissible only if the cooking was not intended for cleaning.

Key Takeaway
Wudu with nabidh al-tamar is a rukhsa unique to dates, permitted only when water is absent and the nabidh meets the specified conditions; the mufta bihi does not require combining with tayammum.

Sensory Evidence Over Istishab in Water Purity
Resolving conflicting testimonies about water purity between sensory evidence and istishab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that sensory evidence outweighs istishab when resolving conflicting testimonies about water purity.

Core Idea
Sensory evidence trumps istishab because direct observation is more certain than presumption.

When two reliable individuals testify about the purity of water, one based on direct sight and the other on the presumption that things remain as they were (istishab), the Hanafi jurist must decide which report to accept. This lesson examines the classical ruling that the sensory witness is preferred because it reports something actually seen, and traces the reasoning behind this hierarchy of proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of evidence
Recognize the distinction between a report based on sensory observation (hiss) — e.g., 'I saw impurity enter the water' — and a report based on istishab — e.g., 'It was pure before, so it remains pure'.
2
State the Hanafi principle
Recall that in Hanafi usul, sensory evidence is considered more certain than istishab because it is based on direct experience. This is a rational preference (tarjih bil-hiss).
The text says: 'رجحنا خبر النجاسة لأنه أخبر عن محسوس مشاهد'
3
Apply to conflicting reports
If the purity-reporter relies solely on istishab, and the impurity-reporter gives sensory evidence, prefer the report of impurity. The sensory report outweighs the presumption.
4
Note the exception when basis is clarified
If the purity-reporter clarifies that his report is based on direct sensory observation (e.g., he personally sealed the vessel), then his report is preferred because it is supported by both sensory evidence and the original state (al-asl).
The commentator mentions this detail as the position of the scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في ذلك بأن قال أخذت هذا الماء من النهر وسددت فم هذا الإناء ولم يخالطه شيء أصلاً رجحنا خبره لتأيده بالأصل، وإن بني خبره على الاستصحاب وقال كان طاهراً فيبقى كذلك رجحنا خبر النجاسة لأنه أخبر عن محسوس مشاهد وأنه راجح على الاستصحاب أهـ. والذي ظهر لي أنه يحمل كلام المشايخ على ما إذا لم يبين مستند اخباره فإذا لم يبين يعمل بالأصل وهو الطهارة، وإن بين فالعبرة لهذا التفصيل. النفي الذي يحتمل معرفته بالدليل ويحتمل بناؤه على العدم الأصلي لأن طهارة الماء قد تدرك بظاهر الحال وقد تدرك عياناً بأن غسل الإناء بماء السماء أو بالماء الجاري وملأه بأحدهما ولم يغب عنه أصلاً ولم يلاقه شيء نجس، فإذا أخبر واحد بنجاسة الماء والآخر بطهارته فإن تمسك بظاهر الحال فأخبار النجاسة أولى، وإن تمسك بالدليل كان مثل الإثبات .اهـ. قوله : (فإذا لم يبين العمل بالأصل) أي
Regarding that: If someone says, 'I took this water from the river, sealed the mouth of this vessel, and nothing at all mixed with it,' we would prefer his report because it is supported by the original state (al-asl). And if his report is based on istishab and he says, 'It was pure, so it remains as such,' we would prefer the report of impurity because he is reporting something sensory and witnessed, and that outweighs istishab. What appears to me is that the words of the scholars should be interpreted for when he does not clarify the basis of his report. If he does not clarify, we act on the original state, which is purity. If he clarifies, then consideration is given to this detail. The negation that may be known by evidence and may be based on the original non-existence, because the purity of water can be perceived by apparent circumstance and can be perceived by direct sight: he washed the vessel with rainwater or flowing water and filled it with one of them, and he did not turn away from it at all, and no impurity touched it. So if one reports the impurity of the water and another reports its purity, then if he holds to the apparent circumstance, the report of impurity is preferable. If he holds to evidence, it is like affirmation. Then he said: 'If he does not clarify, we act on the original state, meaning...'
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory expansion (sharh) on how to resolve conflicting testimonies regarding water purity. The author discusses two scenarios: if the person reporting purity states that he personally observed the water's history (sensory evidence), his report is preferred because it is supported by the original ruling (istishab). If he merely relies on istishab (the principle that things remain as they were), then the report of impurity is preferred because it is based on direct sensory observation, which is stronger than istishab. The commentator then clarifies that if the reporter does not specify the basis of his report, we default to the original state of purity. The discussion aligns with Hanafi usul where sensory evidence outweighs mere presumption. The reliance on 'asl' (original state) and 'istishab' reflects classical Hanafi methodology in matters of taharah.

Key Terms
الاستصحاب (al-istishab): Presumption of continuity: that a state (e.g., purity) remains until proven otherwise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two people report on water in a vessel: one says it is pure based on istishab (it was originally pure), and another says it is impure from direct observation, which report is preferred according to this passage?
A) The report of purity (istishab) is preferred.
B) The report of impurity (sensory) is preferred.
C) Both are equally valid and we act on the original state.
D) We combine both reports and take the more cautious view.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, sensory evidence outweighs istishab when determining water purity in cases of conflicting testimony.

Defaulting to Original Purity When Basis is Unstated
Defaulting to original purity when the basis of testimony is not clarified.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when a reporter of purity does not clarify the basis of his report, we default to the original state of purity.

Core Idea
When a witness does not specify his evidentiary basis, the default ruling is the original state – purity in water.

In the previous lesson, we learned that sensory evidence outweighs istishab when both are explicitly presented. But what if the person claiming purity does not clarify whether his evidence is sensory or based on istishab? This lesson explores the default rule: we act upon the original state (al-asl), which is purity, until a contrary basis is clearly established.

Guided Path
1
Understand the default rule
The default rule in Hanafi fiqh is that things are presumed to retain their original state until proven otherwise. This is known as the principle of istishab or acting upon the 'asl'.
In taharah, the original state of water is purity (taharah).
2
Identify the condition for this default
This default applies specifically when the person reporting purity does not clarify the basis (mustanad) of his report. He does not say whether he is relying on direct observation or simply assuming continuity.
3
Apply the rule
If the purity reporter does not explain his basis, we act upon the original state and rule that the water is pure. The impurity report is not automatically preferred because we lack a clear contradiction.
The text says: 'فإذا لم يبين يعمل بالأصل وهو الطهارة'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Regarding that: If someone says, 'I took this water from the river, sealed the mouth of this vessel, and nothing at all mixed with it,' we would prefer his report because it is supported by the original state (al-asl). And if his report is based on istishab and he says, 'It was pure, so it remains as such,' we would prefer the report of impurity because he is reporting something sensory and witnessed, and that outweighs istishab. If he clarifies, then consideration is given to this detail. So if one reports the impurity of the water and another reports its purity, then if he holds to the apparent circumstance, the report of impurity is preferable. If he holds to evidence, it is like affirmation. Then he said: 'If he does not clarify, we act on the original state, meaning...'

Commentary

If he merely relies on istishab (the principle that things remain as they were), then the report of impurity is preferred because it is based on direct sensory observation, which is stronger than istishab. Key Terms
الاستصحاب (al-istishab): Presumption of continuity: that a state (e.g., purity) remains until proven otherwise.
الأصل (al-asl): The original state or default ruling (e.g., purity of water) that is assumed until evidence proves otherwise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a person reports water as pure but does not explain the basis (mustanad) of his report, what is the ruling according to the passage?
A) We reject his report and rule water impure.
B) We act on the original state, which is purity.

Key Takeaway

Wudu with Nabidh al-Tamr: Definition, Timing, and the Three Narrations
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wudu with nabidh al-tamr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define nabidh al-tamr, identify the time in which wudu with it is considered, and state the three narrations from Abu Hanifa along with the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Wudu with nabidh al-tamr is not valid in the relied-upon Hanafi position; tayammum is required.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explores the detailed ruling on performing wudu with date nectar (nabidh al-tamr) in the absence of pure water. It first defines the substance, then discusses the time conditions, and finally presents three narrations from Abu Hanifa, culminating in the adopted school position that wudu with nabidh is impermissible.

Guided Path
1
Define Nabidh al-Tamr
Identify the characteristics of nabidh al-tamr: made by soaking dates in water until sweet, non-intoxicating, and uncooked. Note the disagreement on cooked versions.
The definition excludes intoxicating or cooked forms, as those are unanimously invalid for wudu.
2
Examine the Timing Rule
According to Abu Hanifa, wudu with nabidh is considered permissible only when tayammum would be permissible; otherwise, it is not.
This ties the ruling to the availability of pure water.
3
Map the Three Narrations
List the three narrations: (1) wudu only, with tayammum recommended; (2) combine wudu and tayammum; (3) tayammum only. Understand the evolution of Abu Hanifa's view.
The third narration is the final and relied-upon position.
4
Analyze the Evidence
Evaluate the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (weak chain, possible abrogation) versus the Qur'anic verse of tayammum (5:6). Understand why the hadith is not considered strong enough to override the verse.
The hadith is controversial due to unknown narrator Abu Zayd and historical uncertainty about the night of the jinn.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is non-permissibility of wudu with nabidh; one must perform tayammum. This aligns with Abu Yusuf, al-Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad, and the majority.
The three Imams outside the Hanafi school also agree with this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (بخلاف نبيذ التمر) يعني إن فقد ماء مطلقاً ولم يجد إلا نبيذ التمر فإنه يتوضأ ولا يجمع بينه وبين التيمم، وذكر هذه المسألة هنا إما لأنه مما يجوز الوضوء به على رأي أو لأن محمداً لما أوجب الجمع صار عنده مشكوكاً فيه فشابه سؤر الحمار . كذا قيل لكن لا يخفى ضعف الثاني لأن المصنف جعله مخالفاً لسؤر الحمار . ثم اعلم أن الكلام ههنا في ثلاثة مواضع الأول في تفسيره الثاني في وقته الثالث في حكمه. أما الأول فهو أن يلقي في الماء تميرات فيصر رقيقاً يسيل على الأعضاء حلواً غير مسكر ولا مطبوخ. وإنما قلنا حلواً لأنه لو توضأ به قبل خروج الحلاوة يجوز بلا خلاف وإنما قلنا غير مسكر لأنه لو كان مسكراً لا يجوز الوضوء به بلا خلاف لأنه حرام، وإنما قلنا غير مطبوخ لأنه لو طبخ فالصحيح أنه لا يتوضأ به إذ النار قد غيرته حلواً كان أو مشتداً كمطبوخ الباقلاء كذا في المبسوط والمحيط يعني بلا خلاف بین الثلاثة الأليق بما قدمناه وهو أن الماء من يصير مقيداً بالطبخ إذا لم يقصد به المبالغة في التنظيف وبه يظهر ضعف ما صححه في المفيد والمزيد أنه يجوز الوضوء به بعدما طبخ. وقد ذكر الزيلعي أن صاحب الهداية وقع منه تناقض فإنه ذكر هنا أن النار إذا غيرته يجز الوضوء به عند أبي حنيفة لجواز شربه، وذكر في بحث المياه أنه لا يجوز الوضوء بما تغير بالطبخ أهـ. ولا يخفى ثبوت الخلاف في هذه المسألة لأن اختلاف التصحيح ينبئ عنه فكان فيه روايتان، فيحتمل أن يكون مراد صاحب الهداية نقل الرواية في الموضعين فلا تناقض حيث أمكن التوفيق، وأما سائر الأنبذة فإنه لا يجوز الوضوء بها عند عامة العلماء وهو الصحيح لأن جواز التوضؤ بنبيذ التمر ثابت بخلاف القياس بالحديث ولهذا لا يجوز عند القدرة على الماء المطلق فلا يقاس عليه غيره. كذا في غاية البيان. وأما الثاني قال أبو حنيفة : كل وقت يجوز التيمم فيه يجوز التوضؤ به وإلا فلا. كذا في معراج الدراية. وأما الثالث ففيه ثلاث روايات عن أبي حنيفة : الأولى وهو قوله الأول أنه يتوضأ به جزماً ويضيف التيمم إليه استحباباً. والثانية يجب الجمع بينه وبين التيمم كسور الحمار وبه قال محمد واختاره في غاية البيان ورجحه والثالثة أنه يتيمم ولا يتوضأ به وهو قوله الآخر وقد رجع إليه وهو الصحيح، وبه قال أبو يوسف والشافعي ومالك وأحمد وأكثر العلماء واختاره الطحاوي. وحكي عن أبي طاهر الدباس أنه قال : إنما اختلفت أجوبة أبي حنيفة لاختلاف الأسئلة فإنه سئل عن التوضؤ به إذا كانت الغلبة للحلاوة قال بتيمم ولا يتوضأ به، وسئل مرة إذا كان الماء والحلاوة سواء قال يجمع بينهما، وسئل مرة إذا كانت الغلبة للماء فقال يتوضأ به ولا يتيمم. وبالجملة فالمذهب المصحح المختار المعتمد عندنا هو عدم الجواز موافقة للأئمة الثلاث فلا حاجة إلى الاشتغال بحديث ابن مسعود الدال على الجواز من قوله عليه السلام له ليلة الماء هذا فإن قيل : نسخ السنة بالكتاب لا يجوز عند الشافعي، فكيف يستقيم القول بأنه منسوخ بآية التيمم ؟ أجيب بأن ذلك جواب أبي يوسف خاصة والمشترك بينهما هو العمل بآية التيمم، وعند محمد يجمع بينهما لأن في الحديث اضطراباً لأن مداره على أبي زيد مولى عمرو بن الحرث وأبو زيد كان مجهولاً عند النقلة، ولأنه روي عن أبي عبيدة بن عبد الله بن مسعود قيل: هل كان أبوك مع النبي ليلة الجن؟ فقال: لو كان أبي مع النبي ليلة الجن لكان فخراً عظيماً ومنقبة له ولعقبه بعده، فأنكر كون أبيه مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولو كان لما خفي على ابنه، وفي التاريخ جهالة تامة. ثم اختلفوا في انتساخ هذا الحديث لجهالة التاريخ؛ فقال بعضهم نسخ ذلك بآية التيمم، وقال بعضهم لم ينسخ فيجب احتياطاً . قلنا: ليلة الجن كانت غير واحدة يعني أنها تكررت قال في التيسير إن الجن أتوا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم دفعتين فيجوز أن تكون الدفعة الثانية في المدينة بعد آية التيمم فلا يصح دعوى النسخ، والحديث مشهور عملت به الصحابة كعلي الله عنه روي عنه الحديث أنه قال : الوضوء بنبيذ التمر وضوء من لم يجد الماء. وروي عن عبد رضي أنه
His statement: 'Unlike date nectar (nabidh al-tamr)' means that if pure water is absent and he finds only date nectar, then he performs wudu with it and does not combine it with tayammum. This issue is mentioned here either because it is one of those substances with which wudu is permitted according to one opinion, or because when Muhammad (al-Shaybani) required combining, it became doubtful in his view and thus similar to the leftover of a donkey. But the weakness of the second is clear because the author made it different from the leftover of a donkey. Know that the discussion here is in three places: first, its definition; second, its time; third, its ruling. As for the first: it is to throw a few dates into water, so it becomes thin, flows on the limbs, sweet, not intoxicating, and not cooked. We said sweet because if he performs wudu with it before sweetness emerges, it is permissible without disagreement. We said not intoxicating because if it were intoxicating, wudu with it would not be permissible without disagreement since it is haram. We said not cooked because if it is cooked, the correct view is that wudu with it is not permissible since fire has changed it, whether sweet or strong, like cooked broad beans. So in al-Mabsut and al-Muhit, meaning without disagreement among the three [scholars]. The more appropriate view is what we have presented, that water becomes restricted by cooking if cleaning excess is not intended. This shows the weakness of what was deemed correct in al-Mufid and al-Mazid that wudu with it after cooking is permissible. Al-Zayla'i mentioned that the author of al-Hidayah contradicted himself: he mentioned here that if fire changes it, wudu with it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa because drinking it is permissible, and in the section on waters he said wudu with water changed by cooking is not permissible. So there is indeed a difference in this issue, as differing in what is considered correct indicates; thus there are two narrations. It is possible that the author of al-Hidayah intended to transmit the narration in both places, so there is no contradiction when reconciliation is possible. As for other nectars (anbidha), wudu with them is not permissible according to most scholars, and that is correct, because the permissibility of wudu with date nectar is established by hadith contrary to analogy, so it is not permissible when pure water is available, and other nectars cannot be analogized to it. So in Ghayat al-Bayan. As for the second: Abu Hanifa said: Whenever tayammum is permissible, wudu with it is permissible; otherwise not. So in Mi'raj al-Diraya. As for the third: there are three narrations from Abu Hanifa: First, his first statement that he performs wudu with it absolutely and adds tayammum to it as a recommendation. Second, he must combine it with tayammum like the leftover of a donkey; this is the view of Muhammad and he selected it in Ghayat al-Bayan and favored it. Third, he performs tayammum and does not perform wudu with it; this is his other statement to which he returned, and it is correct. This is the view of Abu Yusuf, al-Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad, and most scholars, and al-Tahawi selected it. It is narrated from Abu Tahir al-Dabbas that he said: The answers of Abu Hanifa differed only due to differing questions: he was asked about wudu with it when sweetness predominates, and he said tayammum and no wudu; he was asked when water and sweetness are equal, and he said combine both; he was asked when water predominates, and he said wudu with it and no tayammum. In summary, the corrected, chosen, and relied-upon madhhab with us is non-permissibility, in agreement with the three Imams, so there is no need to engage with the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud indicating permissibility from his statement (peace be upon him) to him on the night of the jinn: 'This water...' If it is said: Abrogation of the Sunnah by the Qur'an is not permissible according to al-Shafi'i, so how can it be said that it is abrogated by the verse of tayammum? The answer: That is the response of Abu Yusuf specifically, and common between them is acting on the verse of tayammum. According to Muhammad, he combines both because the hadith is problematic: its chain depends on Abu Zayd, the freed slave of Amr ibn al-Harith, and Abu Zayd was unknown to the narrators. Also, it is narrated from Abu Ubayda ibn Abd Allah ibn Mas'ud: it was said, 'Was your father with the Prophet on the night of the jinn?' He said, 'If my father had been with the Prophet on the night of the jinn, it would have been a great honor and distinction for him and his descendants after him.' So he denied that his father was with the Prophet, and if he had been, it would not have been hidden from his son. There is complete ignorance of history. Then they differed regarding the abrogation of this hadith due to ignorance of history. Some said it was abrogated by the verse of tayammum; some said it was not abrogated, so precaution is necessary. We say: The night of the jinn was not one; it is said to have been repeated. In al-Taysir, it is said that the jinn came to the Messenger of Allah twice, so it is possible that the second time was in Medina after the verse of tayammum, so the claim of abrogation is not valid. The hadith is famous and the companions acted upon it, like Ali (may Allah be pleased with him); it is narrated from him that he said: 'Wudu with date nectar is the wudu of one who does not find water.' And it is narrated from Abd... that he...
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion on the ruling of wudu with date nectar (nabidh al-tamr) when pure water is unavailable. The author (al-Bahr al-Raiq) comments on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq. The discussion is structured into three parts: definition, time, and ruling. The definition specifies that nabidh is made by soaking dates in water until it becomes sweet, non-intoxicating, and uncooked. There is a dispute about whether cooking changes the ruling; the correct view is that it prevents wudu because fire alters the water. The time of wudu with nabidh is tied to the time tayammum is permissible, according to Abu Hanifa. The ruling itself has three narrations from Abu Hanifa: (1) wudu alone is sufficient, with tayammum recommended; (2) must combine wudu and tayammum (Muhammad's view); (3) only tayammum without wudu (the final view of Abu Hanifa, also of Abu Yusuf, and the majority). The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is non-permissibility (tayammum only), aligning with the three other Imams. The passage then discusses the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud about the night of the jinn, which reportedly supports permissibility. The author addresses objections: the hadith's chain is weak due to Abu Zayd being unknown, and there is historical uncertainty about whether the event occurred before or after the revelation of the tayammum verse. Abu Yusuf argues the verse abrogates the hadith, Muhammad argues for combining due to doubt, but the preferred view is that the hadith is not reliable enough to override the verse.

Key Terms
نبيذ التمر (nabidh al-tamr): A drink made by soaking dates in water until sweet, non-intoxicating, and uncooked; it is a type of 'water' used for wudu in the absence of pure water.
سؤر الحمار (su'r al-himar): The leftover water from a donkey; used as an analogy for combining wudu with tayammum (Muhammad's view).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, what should a person do if they have no pure water but have date nectar (nabidh al-tamr)?
A) Perform wudu with the date nectar.
B) Perform tayammum without wudu.
C) Combine wudu with date nectar and tayammum.
D) It is optional: either wudu with date nectar or tayammum is valid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that wudu with nabidh al-tamr is invalid; tayammum is obligatory in its place.

Taharah — Purification

Wudu with Date Nabidh: Internal Hanafi Dispute and the Principle of Ruju'
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wudu with nabidh, retraction, and abrogation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi on wudu with date nabidh and explain why Abu Hanifa's initial permissibility was retracted due to abrogation (naskh).

Core Idea
Wudu with date nabidh is impermissible: Abu Hanifa retracted his initial view, abrogated by the verse of tayammum.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a complex internal Hanafi dispute about performing wudu (and ghusl) with date nabidh when water is unavailable. The author navigates between an earlier permissibility attributed to Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Abbas, the initial view of Abu Hanifa, and the later relied-upon ruling that it is forbidden. The key legal mechanism here is not the weakness of the hadith but its abrogation (naskh) by the Quranic verse of tayammum. You will learn how the Hanafi school resolves such ikhtilaf and why the muqallid must follow the later position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the contested ruling
The act is performing wudu (and ghusl) with date nabidh. The disputed issue is whether it is permissible when water is absent. Identify the initial permissibility and the later impermissibility.
The text mentions both wudu and ghusl, but the main focus is wudu.
2
Locate the two positions within the Hanafi school
Abu Hanifa initially permitted wudu with nabidh based on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud about the Night of the Jinn. Later, he retracted and deemed it impermissible. Muhammad al-Shaybani had a different view: combine nabidh and tayammum. Abu Yusuf followed the later view.
The text also mentions that on the first view, nabidh takes precedence over the remnant of a donkey; on the later view, donkey remnant is superior.
3
Analyze the Hanafi tarjih mechanism
The later position (mufta bihi) is impermissibility. The basis for this tarjih is Abu Hanifa's retraction (ruju'), which means his earlier statement is no longer operative. The verse of tayammum is argued to abrogate the hadith-based allowance.
The author notes that after a mujtahid retracts, it is not permissible to act on his earlier statement.
4
Examine the dalil: Quran vs. Hadith
The Hanafi dalil for impermissibility is the verse of tayammum (5:6), which commands tayammum when no water is found, implying no other substitute is valid. The opposing dalil is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud. The Hanafi response is that the Quranic verse abrogates the hadith.
The text includes a long defense of the hadith's authenticity for Abu Hanifa, but concludes that since the hadith is zanni and the verse is qati, abrogation is valid.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
If a person has no water but has date nabidh, according to the mufta bihi, he must perform tayammum. He cannot use nabidh. If he starts prayer with tayammum and then finds nabidh, he continues; he does not break the prayer.
This is the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

يبني شيئاً في دين الله تعالى على ما لا أصل له بل له أصل أصيل عنده، فالحديث بالنسبة إليه صحيح وإن كان بالنسبة إلى غيره ضعيفاً فالعبرة في هذا الباب برأي المجتهد لا برأي غيره. وقوله «لا أصل له مردود لأنه بعده وكم في كتب الفقه من الاحتجاج بمثل ذلك على أن من تكلم في الحديث المذكور كالدارقطني أبهم الجرح والصحيح عدم قبوله ما لم يفسر ، فلولا نقل رجوع الإمام عنه لأفتينا بوجوب الوضوء منه عند عدم الماء. فإن قلت : حيث كان الحديث ثابتاً فما سبب رجوعه عنه؟ قلت : أمر ظهر للمجتهد من النظر إلى الدليل ألا ترى أن الشافعي رحمه الله رجع عن مذهب مستقل بعد تدوينه؟ وغاية ما يقال هنا إنه ظهر له أن آية التيمم متأخرة عن ليلة الجن فهي ناسخة له اهـ. ملخصاً.
When it is known that wudu with it is not permissible, it is known that ghusl with it is not permissible. They differed on the view of the one who permits wudu with it regarding the permissibility of ghusl with it: in al-Mabsut, its permissibility is declared sahih, and in al-Mufid, its impermissibility is declared sahih. There is no benefit in these two sahih declarations after the madhhab turned to impermissibility for both minor and major impurities, because when a mujtahid retracts from a statement, it is not permissible to act upon it, as stated in al-Tawshih. Intention is required for it according to the view that permits wudu with it. It is not hidden that the remnant of a donkey is given precedence over it in the madhhab, while on the first view, nabidh is given precedence. According to Muhammad, both are combined with tayammum. If one enters prayer with tayammum then finds it (water), it is considered non-existent in the madhhab; on the first view he breaks it; according to Muhammad, he continues and repeats it with wudu using it, just as if he found the remnant of a donkey—he continues and repeats it with it by agreement. If not for the expression of al-Wafi, the source of the book, I would have explained that what is meant is that nabidh is contrary to the remnant of a donkey in that wudu with it is not permissible at all, so that which is in the book becomes the relied-upon position. Indeed, Imam al-Tahawi was fair— God, water— and they [؟] Ibn Mas'ud that he permitted wudu with date nabidh when water was unavailable. Ikrimah narrated from Ibn Abbas that he said: 'Perform wudu with date nabidh.' It is narrated from him by various chains that he permitted wudu with date nabidh when water was unavailable. The great scholars of fatwa, so their statement [is]... except with it and the like is added to the book. Abu Hanifa said: If it is doubted whether Abdullah ibn Mas'ud was with the Messenger of God on the Night of the Jinn, we say: In this chapter, there is enough to rely upon, and that is the narration of these great Companions. His statement 'Abu Zayd is unknown' we say: No, rather he is among the great Tabi'un and was well-known. Muhammad ibn Isma'il al-Bukhari said: The presence of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud with the Prophet is established by twelve aspects. The meaning of his son's statement that he was not with him is that he was not with him at the time of address and invitation, but rather was inside the line. The proof that he was with him is what is narrated that Ibn Mas'ud saw people playing in Kufa and said: 'I have not seen a people more similar to the jinn whom I saw with the Messenger of God on the Night of the Jinn than these.' This is in Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam and al-Jami' al-Saghir of al-Mahbubi, similarly in al-Nihayah and al-Inayah. ... Finished. His statement: 'Indeed, Imam al-Tahawi was fair...' Allamah Nuh Afandi said in his glosses on al-Durr after quoting al-Tahawi: I say: Far be it, far be it, far be it from him to build something in the religion of God on something that has no basis. Rather, it has a solid basis with him. The hadith is authentic in his view, even if it is weak in the view of others. The criterion in this chapter is the opinion of the mujtahid, not the opinion of others. His statement 'it has no basis' is rejected because it suggests that it is fabricated, but that is not the case. The most that has been said about it is that it is weak, which is not equivalent to fabricated. Indeed, authenticity, soundness, and weakness are based on the chain of transmission as a matter of probability, according to the correct view. As for reality, it is possible for a sound hadith to be weak and a weak one to be sound. So we do not definitively declare a sound hadith as sound nor a weak one as weak, because reality may differ. Moreover, a single hadith may be sound according to some and weak according to others. It then circles back to the ijtihad of the mujtahid. If he builds a ruling on a hadith, his muqallid must accept it and not pay attention to the statement of someone who declares it weak after him. How many times in books of fiqh is there argumentation with things like this? Indeed, the one who spoke about the aforementioned hadith, like al-Daraqutni, expressed a general criticism, and the correct view is that it is not accepted unless specified. If not for the report of the Imam's retraction, we would have given fatwa on the obligation of wudu with it when water is unavailable. If you say: Since the hadith is established, what is the reason for his retraction? I say: An issue appeared to the mujtahid from examining the evidence. Do you not see that al-Shafi'i retracted an entire madhhab after its compilation? The utmost that can be said here is that it appeared to him that the verse of tayammum is later than the Night of the Jinn, so it abrogates it. Summarized.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on performing wudu (and ghusl) with date nabidh (a drink made from soaked dates) when water is unavailable. The author presents the internal Hanafi dispute on this issue. Initially, some Hanafis allowed it based on a hadith from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud regarding the Night of the Jinn, but later the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it is not permissible. The text explains that even among those who initially permitted wudu with nabidh, there is a difference on whether ghusl is also allowed, but this becomes irrelevant once the general ruling shifted. The author also discusses the precedence between nabidh and the remnant of a donkey (su'r al-himar) and the ruling when one starts prayer with tayammum then finds nabidh. The passage includes a lengthy defense of the authenticity of the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, arguing that it was considered authentic by Abu Hanifa and that his retraction was due to the verse of tayammum abrogating it. The commentator, Nuh Afandi, defends Imam al-Tahawi's criticism and emphasizes that a mujtahid's ruling based on a hadith must be accepted by his muqallid, even if later scholars deem the hadith weak.

Key Terms
نبيذ التمر (nabidh al-tamr): A drink made by soaking dates in water until it becomes sweet, used in pre-Islamic times and early Islam as a beverage.
سؤر الحمار (su'r al-himar): The leftover water or liquid from which a donkey has drunk. It is considered impure (najis) and cannot be used for wudu.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation: a later revealed ruling supersedes an earlier one. Here, the verse of tayammum is argued to abrogate the permissibility of wudu with nabidh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on wudu with date nabidh?
A) It is permissible and recommended.
B) It is impermissible because the verse of tayammum abrogates any earlier allowance.
C) It is permissible only for ghusl, not wudu.
D) It is permissible if water is scarce.

Key Takeaway
Wudu with date nabidh is prohibited in the later Hanafi school because the verse of tayammum abrogated the earlier hadith-based allowance, and Abu Hanifa's retraction makes the earlier view non-operative.

Definition, Components, and Proofs of Tayammum
Defining tayammum linguistically and legally, listing its components, and providing its proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of tayammum, identify its pillars, and explain its proofs from the Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Tayammum is a valid purification with pure earth, substituting for wudu when water is absent.

Tayammum is a divine license for this ummah, allowing purification with earth when water is unavailable. This lesson unpacks its linguistic and legal definitions, its integral components (arkan), and the scriptural proofs that establish it.

Guided Path
1
1. Distinguish linguistic and legal definitions
Identify the two definitions: tayammum as absolute intention (linguistic) vs. wiping face and hands on pure earth (legal). The author critiques other definitions, settling on the one that includes both action and intention.
The author criticizes definitions that omit action or restrict earth to a part.
2
2. Identify the pillars (rukn)
The rukn consists of two things: two strikes (one for face, one for hands to elbows) and complete coverage of those limbs.
There is discussion about the first strike, deferred later.
3
3. Note the conditions (shurut) and ruling (hukm)
Conditions of permissibility are not detailed here; they will come later. The ruling is that tayammum makes permissible what is otherwise impermissible without purification.
4
4. Understand the reason for legislation
The verse of tayammum was revealed during the expedition of Banu al-Mustaliq when Aisha lost her necklace and no water was available for prayer.
This is the sabab al-shar'iyyah (cause of legislation).
5
5. Examine the proofs from Quran and Sunnah
The proof from Quran is in two verses (al-Nisa' 4:43 and al-Ma'idah 5:6). From Sunnah, the hadith of Ammar ibn Yasir is cited, where the Prophet showed that one strike suffices for hands and face.
The passage also discusses a hadith from Ibn Mas'ud and a retraction by Imam Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التيمم
الباب لغة النوع، وعرفاً نوع من المسائل اشتمل عليها كتاب وليست بفصل. والتيمم لغة مطلق القصد بخلاف الحج فإنه القصد إلى معظم وشواهدهما كثيرة. واصطلاحاً على ما في شروح الهداية القصد إلى الصعيد الطاهر للتطهير. وعلى ما في البدائع وغيره استعمال الصعيد في عضوين مخصوصين على قصد التطهير بشرائط مخصوصة وزيف الأول بأن القصد شرط لا ركن، والثاني بأنه لا يشترط استعمال جزء من الأرض حتى يجوز بالحجر الأملس فالحق أنه اسم لمسح الوجه واليدين على الصعيد الطاهر والقصد شرط لأنه النية. وله ركن وشروط وحكم وسبب مشروعية وسبب وجوب وكيفية ودليل . أما ركنه فشيئان : الأول ضربتان ضربة للوجه وضربة لليدين إلى المرفقين والثاني استيعاب العضوين، وفي الأوّل كلام نذكره إن شاء الله تعالى. وأما شرائطه أعني شرائط جوازه فستأتي في الكتاب مفصلة. وأما حكمه فاستباحة ما لا يحل إلا به وأما سبب مشروعيته فما وقع لعائشة رضي الله عنها في غزوة بني المصطلق وهي غزوة المريسيع وهو ماء بناحية قديد بين مكة والمدينه لما أضلت عقدها فبعث عليه السلام في طلبه فحانت الصلاة وليس معهم ماء فأغلظ أبو بكر رضي الله عنه على عائشة وقال : حبست رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم والمسلمين على غير ماء فنزلت آية التيمم، فجاء أسيد بن الحضير فجعل يقول : ما أكثر بركتكم يا آل أبي بكر. رواه البخاري ومسلم.
آخر فدار على اجتهاد المجتهد، فإذا بنى على حديث حكماً يجب على من قلده أن يأخذ بالقبول ولا يلتفت إلى قول من ضعفه بعده وكم في كتب الفقه من الاحتجاج بمثل ذلك على أن من تكلم في الحديث المذكور كالدارقطني أبهم الجرح والصحيح عدم قبوله ما لم يفسر ، فلولا نقل رجوع الإمام عنه لأفتينا بوجوب الوضوء منه عند عدم الماء. فإن قلت : حيث كان الحديث ثابتاً فما سبب رجوعه عنه؟ قلت : أمر ظهر للمجتهد من النظر إلى الدليل ألا ترى أن الشافعي رحمه الله رجع عن مذهب مستقل بعد تدوينه؟ وغاية ما يقال هنا إنه ظهر له أن آية التيمم متأخرة عن ليلة الجن فهي ناسخة له اهـ. ملخصاً.

قوله : ( على الصعيد الطاهر) كان عليه أن يقول المطهر كما سينبه عليه نفسه عند قول المصنف البحر الرائق ١ م ١٦
كتاب الطهارة - باب التيمم
أصله
وقال القرطبي : نزلت الآية في عبد الرحمن بن عوف أصابته جنابة وهو مريض فرخص له في التيمم، وقيل غير ذلك. وأما سبب وجوبه فما هو سبب وجوب المتقدم. وأما كيفيته فستأتي. وأما دليله فمن الكتاب في آيتين في سورة النساء والمائدة وهما مدنيتان. ومن السنة فأحاديث منها ما رواه البخاري ومسلم عن عمار بن ياسر قال : بعثني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في حاجة فأجنبت فلم أجد الماء فتمرغت في الصعيد كما تتمرغ الدابة - وفي رواية فتمعكت - ثم أتيت النبي له فذكرت ذلك له فقال : إنما كان يكفيك أن تقول بيديك هكذا ثم ضرب بيديه الأرض ضربة واحدة ثم مسح الشمال على اليمين وظاهر كفيه ووجهه. ثم اعلم أن التيمم لم يكن مشروعاً لغير هذه الأمة وإنما شرع رخصة لنا، والرخصة فيه من حيث الآلة حيث اكتفي بالصعيد الذي هو ملوّث وفي محله بشطر أعضاء الوضوء. كذا في المستصفى.
Chapter of Tayammum. Al-bab linguistically means type, and conventionally a type of topics included in a book, not a section. Tayammum linguistically means absolute intention, unlike Hajj which is intention to the venerated; both have many proofs. Conventionally, according to the commentaries of al-Hidayah: intention to pure earth for purification. According to al-Bada'i' and others: using pure earth on two specific limbs with intention of purification under specific conditions. The first definition is criticized because intention is a condition not a pillar; the second because it requires using a part of the earth while it is permissible with smooth stone; so the correct is that it is a name for wiping the face and hands on pure earth, and intention is a condition because it is the niyyah. It has a pillar, conditions, ruling, reason for legislation, cause of obligation, modality, and proof. As for its pillar: two things: first, two strikes—one strike for the face and one strike for the hands to the elbows; second, covering the two limbs. There is discussion about the first which we will mention, God willing. As for its conditions, i.e., conditions of its permissibility, they will come in detail in the book. As for its ruling: making permissible what is not permissible except with it. As for its reason for legislation: what happened to 'Aisha, may God be pleased with her, in the expedition of Banu al-Mustaliq, the expedition of al-Muraysi', which is water near Qudayd between Mecca and Medina, when she lost her necklace. The Prophet, peace be upon him, sent someone to search for it, and the time for prayer came and they had no water. Abu Bakr, may God be pleased with him, was harsh to 'Aisha and said: 'You have detained the Messenger of God and the Muslims without water.' Then the verse of tayammum was revealed. Usayd ibn Hudayr came and said: 'How blessed you are, O family of Abu Bakr!' Narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. Another [point] depended on the ijtihad of the mujtahid: if he based a ruling on a hadith, those who follow him must accept it and not pay attention to those who declare it weak afterwards. How many fiqh books use such evidences! Concerning the critic of the mentioned hadith like al-Daraqutni, he made his criticism ambiguous (ibham al-jarh), and the correct is that it is not accepted unless it is explained. Had the Imam's retraction not been transmitted, we would have given a fatwa of obligation of wudu from it when water is absent. If you say: since the hadith is authentic, what is the reason for his retraction? I say: A matter became clear to the mujtahid from examining the evidence. Do you not see that al-Shafi'i, may God have mercy on him, retracted an independent madhhab after codifying it? The utmost that can be said here is that it became clear to him that the verse of tayammum is later than the Night of the Jinn, so it abrogated that hadith. End of summary. Chapter of Tayammum. His saying: 'on pure earth' – he should have said 'purifying' as he will point out himself when the author says... [reference to al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 1 m 16]. Its origin. Al-Qurtubi said: the verse was revealed concerning 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf who became junub while sick, so tayammum was permitted for him. Others said otherwise. As for its cause of obligation, it is the same as the cause of obligation of what preceded. As for its modality, it will come. As for its proof, from the Book in two verses in Surahs al-Nisa' and al-Ma'idah, both Medinan. From the Sunnah, among the hadiths is what Bukhari and Muslim narrated from 'Ammar ibn Yasir who said: 'The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, sent me on an errand. I became junub and did not find water, so I rolled in the earth like an animal rolls' – and in another narration: 'so I wallowed' – then I came to the Prophet and mentioned that to him. He said: 'It would have been enough for you to say with your hands like this,' then he struck his hands on the earth one strike, then wiped the left hand on the right, and the apparent parts of his palms and his face. Then know that tayammum was not legislated for other than this ummah; it was legislated as a license for us. The license is in terms of the instrument, as pure earth – which is usually impure – suffices, and in place it substitutes for half the limbs of wudu. This is from al-Mustasfa.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on tayammum by defining both the chapter heading and the term itself. Linguistically, 'tayammum' means absolute intention, while legally it refers to wiping the face and hands on pure earth with the intention of purification. The author then discusses various definitions and settles on the one that includes the action of wiping and the condition of intention. He then enumerates the components of tayammum: its rukn (integral parts) which are two strikes—one for the face and one for the hands up to the elbows—and covering the entire face and hands. The shurut (conditions) are deferred. The hukm (ruling) is that it makes permissible what was impermissible without it. The sabab al-shar'iyyah (reason for legislation) is the incident of 'Aisha during the expedition of Banu al-Mustaliq when she lost her necklace. The Prophet and the companions had no water, so the verse of tayammum was revealed. This is narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. Then there is a discussion about a hadith from Ibn Mas'ud that Imam Abu Hanifa initially relied on, but later he seemed to have retracted. The author comments that the hadith is criticized by al-Daraqutni, but the critic did not specify the defect, so the hadith is still acceptable. The author wonders if there is a report of the Imam's retraction, but if not, we would have to follow the hadith. However, it appears that Imam Abu Hanifa realized that the verse of tayammum abrogates the hadith. Then, the author comments on the matn phrase 'on pure earth' and suggests it should be 'purifying earth'. He then mentions another opinion from Qurtubi about the reason for revelation. He continues with the proof from the Quran (two verses in Surah Nisa and Ma'idah) and from the Sunnah, specifically the hadith of Ammar ibn Yasir. Finally, he notes that tayammum is a license specifically for this ummah, and it shows divine facilitation by using earth which is ordinarily impure.

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Linguistically: absolute intention. Legally: wiping the face and hands on pure earth with intention of purification.
الصعيد الطاهر (al-sa'id al-tahir): Pure earth or any part of the earth that is pure, including smooth stone.
الركن (al-rukn): Integral part of tayammum: two strikes (face and hands) and covering the entire face and hands.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the rukn (pillar) of tayammum?
A) Intention only.
B) Striking the earth twice and wiping the face and hands.
C) Using clean water.
D) Passing wet hands over the head.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is a valid purification method with specific pillars, conditions, and proofs; it substitutes for half of wudu and uses pure earth as a license for this ummah.

The Condition of Water Absence and the Shafi'i Dispute on Insufficient Water
Explaining the condition of water absence and the inter-madhhab dispute with Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for tayammum regarding water absence, explain the Shafi'i position on using insufficient water, and evaluate the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Insufficient water is legally nonexistent – you may perform tayammum without using it.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a key condition for tayammum: the absence of water. It defines absence as water being more than a mile away or insufficient for complete purification. Then it presents a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues that even a little water must be used. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of how Hanafi usul principles shape fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for tayammum
Find the condition stated at the beginning: water must be absent either by distance (more than a mile) or because it is insufficient for purification.
The text mentions 'يتيمم لبعده ميلاً عن ماء'.
2
Locate the point of dispute
What happens when a small amount of water exists but does not suffice for complete wudu or ghusl? The Hanafi school says it is like non‑existent; the Shafi'i school says it must be used.
The phrase 'وغير الكافي كالمعدوم وهذا عندنا' signals the Hanafi stance.
3
Analyse the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi rely on the Quranic verse 'you find no water' interpreted as water sufficient for purification, and a qiyas on partial zakat or emancipation: a part of the cause does not achieve the whole effect.
The analogy is that, like zakat on part of the nisab is not obligatory, using part of the water does not yield complete purification.
4
Analyse the Shafi'i proof
Shafi'i cites the generality of 'water' in the verse (indefinite in a negation) and analogies from removing some najasah, covering some awrah, and combining halal and haram meat in necessity.
The Shafi'i view is that the water, even if little, is still water and must be used to reduce impurity.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
Hanafi rebuts: purification is indivisible – hadath remains as long as even a little spot is left. Using a little water does not lift the hadath, so it is wasteful. The analogies fail because impurity and awrah are divisible, while ritual purity is not.
The response also notes that halal meat that does not remove necessity becomes like non‑existent, just like insufficient water.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (يتيمم لبعده ميلاً عن ماء) أي يتيمم الشخص وهذا شروع في بيان شرائطه فمنها أن لا يكون واجداً للماء قدر ما يكفي لطهارته في الصلاة التي تفوت إلى خلف وما هو من أجزائها لقوله تعالى فلم تجدوا ماء فتيمموا [النساء : ٤٣] وغير الكافي كالمعدوم وهذا عندنا. وقال الشافعي : يلزمه استعمال الموجود والتيمم للباقي لأن «ما» نكرة في النفي فتعم وقياساً على إزالة بعض النجاسة وستر بعض العورة، وكالجمع في حالة الاضطرار بين الذكية والميتة. قلنا : الآية سيقت لبيان الطهارة الحكمية فكأن التقدير فلم تجدوا ماء محللاً للصلاة فإن وجود الماء النجس لا يمنعه من التيمم إجماعاً وباستعمال القليل لم يثبت شيء من الحل يقيناً على الكمال فإن الحل حكم والعلة غسل الأعضاء كلها وشيء من الحكم لا يثبت ببعض العلة كبعض النصاب في حق الزكاة وكبعض الرقبة في حق الكفارة، والقياس على الحقيقية والعورة فاسد لأنهما يتجزآن فيفيد إلزامه باستعمال القليل للتقليل ولا يفيد هنا إذ لا يتجزأ هنا بل الحدث قائم ما بقي أدنى لمعة فيبقى مجرد إضاعة مال خصوصاً في موضع عزته مع بقاء الحدث كما هو، وأما الجمع حالة الاضطرار فلأن الذكية لما لم تدفع الاضطرار صارت كالعدم . كذا ذكر في كثير من الشروح
His saying: 'He performs tayammum because of distance of a mile from water' means a person performs tayammum. This is the beginning of explaining its conditions. Among them is that he must not have water sufficient for his purification in the prayer that is fard and what is part of it, due to His saying: 'and you find no water, then perform tayammum' [Quran 4:43]. And what is insufficient is like nonexistent, and this is our view. Al-Shafi'i said: He must use what he has and perform tayammum for the remainder, because 'ma' is an indefinite negated particle so it is general, and by analogy with removing some impurity and covering some of the private parts, and like combining in a state of necessity between slaughtered and carrion. We say: The verse is specifically for ritual purification, as if the implicit meaning is 'you find no water permissible for prayer.' The existence of impure water does not prevent tayammum by consensus. By using a small amount, nothing of the permission is certainly established to completion. For the permission is a ruling, and the cause is washing all the limbs, and no part of a ruling is established by part of the cause, like part of the nisab regarding zakat and part of the slave regarding expiation. The analogy on real impurity and private parts is invalid because they are divisible, so it would obligate him to use the little amount to reduce, but it is not useful here because it is not divisible here; rather, hadath remains as long as even a small spot remains, so it is just wasting wealth, especially in a place where it is scarce, while the hadath remains as it is. As for combining in case of necessity, it is because the slaughtered (halal) meat, since it did not remove the necessity, becomes like nonexistent. This is mentioned in many commentaries.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage explains the first condition for the permissibility of tayammum: the absence of water. The condition is that water must be more than a mile away, or else one must go to it. The author states that tayammum is permissible when one does not possess water sufficient for the purification needed for the prayer and its parts. The evidence is the Quranic verse 'and you find no water, then perform tayammum'. Insufficient water is considered legally nonexistent. This is the Hanafi position. Then a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i is presented. Shafi'i holds that one must use whatever water is available and then perform tayammum for the rest, based on the generality of 'water' in the negative context, and analogies from partial removal of impurity, partial covering of awrah, and the case of combining halal and haram meat in the state of necessity. The Hanafi response is that the verse is about ritual purification where complete purity is required; the water is considered nonexistent because it does not fulfill the purpose. The analogy with partial removal of impurity is flawed because those things are divisible, while ritual purity is not divisible. The analogy with meat fails because haram meat does not remove the necessity. The author then mentions that this response is mentioned in many commentaries.

Key Terms
ميل (mil): A distance measure; the condition for tayammum is that water is more than a mile away.
الكافي (al-kafi): Sufficient water for full wudu or ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person finds a small amount of water that is insufficient for complete wudu, what is the ruling?
A) Must use it and then perform tayammum for the rest.
B) Is not required to use it and can perform tayammum.
C) Must use it and repeat prayer later.
D) Must combine water and tayammum.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, water insufficient for complete purification is legally considered nonexistent, allowing tayammum without using it.

Prioritizing Water for Najasah over Hadath
Ruling on water prioritization from later Hanafi sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when water is insufficient for both hadath and najasah, water must be used for najasah, and tayammum performed for hadath.

Core Idea
Remove najasah first; tayammum for hadath — water is for actual impurity, not ritual impurity when scarce.

When a person has only a small amount of water, enough only for either wudu or removing najasah from the garment, the Hanafi school rules that the water must be used to remove the najasah, and the person should perform tayammum for hadath. This prioritization is based on the principle that preventing a physical impurity from remaining during prayer is more important than performing wudu with water. This lesson explains the ruling and its consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the resource constraint
Recognize that water is sufficient for only one of two needs: hadath (ritual impurity requiring wudu) or removing najasah haqiqiyyah (physical impurity).
The passage assumes a single use of water, not both.
2
Recognize the two needs
Differentiate between hadath (ritual impurity) and najasah haqiqiyyah (actual impurity). Both must be addressed for valid prayer.
Hadath requires wudu or tayammum; najasah on garment requires washing.
3
Apply the priority rule
According to the majority of scholars, water must be used to remove the najasah, and tayammum is performed for hadath.
The text states: 'غسل به الثوب منها وتيمم للحدث عند عامة العلماء'.
4
Understand the alternative outcome
If one uses water for wudu and prays in najis clothes, the prayer is valid but the person is sinful (musi').
The ruling is 'أجزأه وكان مسيئاً'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لكن في الخلاصة : ولو وجد من الماء قدر ما يغسل به بعض النجاسة الحقيقية أو وجد من الثوب قدر ما يستر بعض العورة لا يلزمه ا هـ . ولو وجد ماء يكفي للحدث أو إزالة النجاسة المانعة غسل به الثوب منها وتيمم للحدث عند عامة العلماء، وإن توضأ به وصلى في النجس أجزأه وكان مسيئاً. كذا في الخانية. وفي المحيط : ولو تيمم أولاً ثم غسل النجاسة يعيد التيمم لأنه تيمم وهو قادر على ما يتوضأ به ا هـ. وفيه نظر بل الظاهر الحكم بجواز التيمم تقدم على غسل الثوب أو تأخر لأنه مستحق الصرف إلى الثوب على ما قالوا والمستحق الصرف إلى جهة معدوم حكماً بالنسبة إلى غيرها كما في مسألة اللمعة مع بطاهر من جنس الأرض. قوله : (كما في مسألة اللمعة أي لو اغتسل الجنب وفرغ ماؤه ثم علم أنه
But in al-Khulasa: If he finds water that can wash some of the real impurity, or finds a garment that can cover part of the private parts, he is not obligated [to use it]. End. And if he finds water sufficient for hadath or for removing the preventer [of prayer], he washes the garment with it and performs tayammum for hadath according to the majority of scholars. If he performs wudu with it and prays in the najis [garment], it suffices him but he is sinful. Thus in al-Khaniyya. In al-Muhit: If he performed tayammum first then washed the najasah, he repeats the tayammum because he performed tayammum while capable of performing wudu. End. There is a consideration: rather, the apparent ruling is the permissibility of tayammum preceding or following washing the garment because the water is obligated to be used for the garment as they said, and what is obligated to be used for a purpose is considered nonexistent legally relative to others, as in the case of the small spot with pure from the genus of earth. His saying: 'as in the case of the small spot' meaning if a junub performed ghusl and his water finished, then he knew that he...
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage presents a set of rulings from al-Khulasa and other works regarding cases of insufficient water. If a person has water that can only wash some of the actual impurity (najasah haqiqiyyah) or a garment that can only cover part of the awrah, they are not obligated to use it. If a person has water sufficient for either hadath (ritual impurity) or removing a preventer of prayer (like najasah), they should use it to wash the garment and perform tayammum for hadath. This is the ruling of the generality of scholars. If, however, a person uses the water for wudu and prays in najis clothes, the prayer is valid but he is sinful (musi'). Then from al-Muhit: if one performs tayammum first and then washes the najasah, he must repeat the tayammum because he was capable of performing wudu at the time of tayammum. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq critiques this, saying the tayammum should be valid either before or after washing the najasah because the water is obligated to be used for the najasah. Finally, the author ends with a comparison to the case of a junub who finishes his ghusl and then learns that he missed a spot (lum'ah).

Key Terms
النجاسة الحقيقية (al-najasah al-haqiqiyyah): Actual impurity (like blood, urine) that must be removed from the body or garment for prayer validity.
الحدث (al-hadath): Ritual impurity that requires wudu or ghusl for prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Use water to remove najasah and perform tayammum.
C) Combine both by using half for each.
D) Perform tayammum first, then use water for wudu.

Key Takeaway
When water is insufficient for both, removing najasah takes priority over wudu; use water for najasah and perform tayammum for hadath.

Condition for Tayammum: Distance from Water – Hanafi vs Shafi'i Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on water availability for tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on insufficient water for tayammum, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument using Quran and qiyas, and evaluate the Hanafi response based on the indivisibility of hadath.

Core Idea
Insufficient water is like non-existent: Hanafis permit tayammum directly; Shafi'is require using any water first.

This lesson examines a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the condition for tayammum. The central question is: if a person has a small amount of water insufficient for complete wudu, must they use it and then perform tayammum for the remaining parts, or may they perform tayammum directly? The answer hinges on the interpretation of Quran 4:43 and the nature of legal impurity (hadath). We will follow the Hanafi reasoning and its refutation of the Shafi'i analogies.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: tayammum is permitted when water is a mile away. More importantly, insufficient water is treated as non-existent, so one may perform tayammum directly without using such water.
The mile is a specific measure; the principle applies to any insufficient amount.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the Quranic phrase 'and you do not find water' includes any water, no matter how little. Therefore, one must use whatever water is available and then perform tayammum for the remainder.
This view relies on the generality of 'maa' (water) in the negative.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof: (1) Quranic general command; (2) qiyas on washing part of filth – using a little reduces impurity; (3) qiyas on covering part of the private parts; (4) qiyas on combining halal meat and carrion in necessity.
These analogies aim to show that partial use has benefit.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response refutes each proof: (a) The verse implies permissible water for prayer; (b) legal impurity is indivisible – using a little does not remove the hadath at all, unlike filth or covering; (c) the analogous cases involve divisible matters where partial action gives partial benefit, but hadath is not divisible; (d) carrion in necessity is useless if it does not satisfy hunger, so the analogy fails.
The key point: the ruling of purification depends on washing all limbs; a cause cannot be established by a part.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: A person with only a cup of water for wudu would, under Shafi'i view, use it then do tayammum for the rest; under Hanafi view, he may perform tayammum directly without using the water. The Hanafi view is mufta bihi in the school.
The Hanafi position conserves water and avoids wastage when purification is incomplete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (يتيمم لبعده ميلاً عن ماء) أي يتيمم الشخص وهذا شروع في بيان شرائطه فمنها أن لا يكون واجداً للماء قدر ما يكفي لطهارته في الصلاة التي تفوت إلى خلف وما هو من أجزائها لقوله تعالى فلم تجدوا ماء فتيمموا [النساء : ٤٣] وغير الكافي كالمعدوم وهذا عندنا. وقال الشافعي : يلزمه استعمال الموجود والتيمم للباقي لأن «ما» نكرة في النفي فتعم وقياساً على إزالة بعض النجاسة وستر بعض العورة، وكالجمع في حالة الاضطرار بين الذكية والميتة. قلنا : الآية سيقت لبيان الطهارة الحكمية فكأن التقدير فلم تجدوا ماء محللاً للصلاة فإن وجود الماء النجس لا يمنعه من التيمم إجماعاً وباستعمال القليل لم يثبت شيء من الحل يقيناً على الكمال فإن الحل حكم والعلة غسل الأعضاء كلها وشيء من الحكم لا يثبت ببعض العلة كبعض النصاب في حق الزكاة وكبعض الرقبة في حق الكفارة، والقياس على الحقيقية والعورة فاسد لأنهما يتجزآن فيفيد إلزامه باستعمال القليل للتقليل ولا يفيد هنا إذ لا يتجزأ هنا بل الحدث قائم ما بقي أدنى لمعة فيبقى مجرد إضاعة مال خصوصاً في موضع عزته مع بقاء الحدث كما هو، وأما الجمع حالة الاضطرار فلأن الذكية لما لم تدفع الاضطرار صارت كالعدم . كذا ذكر في كثير من الشروح لكن في الخلاصة : ولو وجد من الماء قدر ما يغسل به بعض النجاسة الحقيقية أو وجد من الثوب قدر ما يستر بعض العورة لا يلزمه ا هـ
His statement (He performs tayammum if water is a mile away) means: he performs tayammum. This is the beginning of explaining its conditions: among them is that he should not have water sufficient for his purification in the prayer that would be missed, and what is part of it. Because Allah says: "And you do not find water, then perform tayammum" [4:43]. That which is insufficient is like non-existent. This is our position. Al-Shafi'i said: He must use what is available and perform tayammum for the rest, because the word "water" is indefinite in the negative, so it includes all water, and by analogy to removing some filth and covering some of the private parts, and like combining between slaughtered (halal) and carrion in a state of necessity. We say: The verse was narrated to explain the legal purification, so the implied meaning is: you did not find water that is permissible for prayer. Indeed, the presence of impure water does not prevent him from tayammum by consensus. And by using a little (water), nothing of permissibility is established with certainty to perfection, for permissibility is a ruling, and the cause is washing all limbs, and a ruling is not established by a part of the cause, like part of the nisab regarding zakat and part of a slave regarding expiation. The analogy to impurities and private parts is invalid because they are divisible, so it requires him to use a little to reduce, but it is not useful here because there is no divisibility here; rather, the hadath remains as long as any spot remains, so it is merely waste of property, especially when it is scarce, while the hadath remains as it is. As for combining in necessity, the slaughtered animal does not remove the necessity, so it is like non-existent. Thus it is mentioned in many commentaries. But in al-Khulasa: If he finds water sufficient to wash some of the actual impurity or finds enough cloth to cover some of the private parts, it is not obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the condition for tayammum. The Hanafi position is that tayammum is permitted when water is a mile away, based on the Quranic verse "and you do not find water" (4:43). The Hanafis argue that insufficient water is like non-existent water. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that the verse means any water, so one must use what little water is available and then perform tayammum for the remaining parts. He also draws analogies to washing some filth, covering some private parts, and combining halal meat and carrion in necessity. The Hanafi response refutes these analogies: legal impurity (hadath) is indivisible, so using little water does not achieve purification; the ruling of permissibility is based on washing all limbs, and a ruling cannot be established by a part of the cause. The analogy to impurities and private parts is invalid because those are divisible, so using little reduces but does not complete purification. The necessity case is different because carrion does not resolve the necessity. The text concludes with a note from al-Khulasa that if water is only enough for some filth or cloth for some private parts, it is not obligatory to use it. This is consistent with the Hanafi principle of considering insufficient water as non-existent.

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): A dry purification using clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
الميل (al-mil): A unit of distance; approximately 4,000 cubits (about 2 km) in the Hanafi definition used here.
الحدث (al-hadath): Legal impurity (minor or major) that prevents valid prayer; requires wudu or ghusl.
النصاب (al-nisab): Minimum threshold of wealth liable for zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal status of water that is insufficient for complete wudu?
A) It is considered non-existent for the purpose of tayammum.
B) It must be used, and then tayammum is performed for the rest.
C) It can be used for wudu with the intention of partial purification.
D) It is considered impure and cannot be used.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school treats insufficient water as non-existent, permitting direct tayammum, based on the indivisibility of legal impurity (hadath) and the Quranic verse's implication of permissible, sufficient water.
